According to ṭ, the word bodhisattvapiṭaka refers to the whole canon of scriptures as described supra, to the teachings of the bodhisattvas generally. On the connection, however, of Akṣ and the individual sūtra named Bodhisattvapiṭaka, v. introduction.bsdu ba’i dṅos po źes bya ba ni sems can dga’ bar byed pa’i dṅos po źes bya ba’i tha tshig ste, de yaṅ sbyin pa la sogs pa bsdu ba’i dṅos po bźi ñid kyi skabs nas ’chad do.thabs mkhas pa ni dge ba’i rtsa ba chuṅ ṅu yaṅ dpag tu med par ’gyur bar byed pa daṅ, sems can bstan pa ’di la ma źugs pa rnams bstan pa la gzud pa daṅ, źugs pa rnams dge ba’i rtsa ba ’phel bar bya ba daṅ, dge ba’i rtsa ba ’phel ba rnams yoṅs su smin par bya ba daṅ, yoṅs su smin pa rnams rnam par grol bar bya ste, de ñan par byed pas na thabs la mkhas pa ñan pa’i rnam pa źes bya’o.tshaṅs pa ni sdig pa thams cad spaṅs pa’i mya ṅan las ’das pa la bya ste, mdo las kyaṅ: tshaṅs par gyur bsil bar gyur, ces gsuṅs pa’i phyir ro. de’i gnas pa ni thob par byed pa’i rgyu la bya ste, de yaṅ byams pa la sogs pa tshad med pa bźi ñid kyi skabs nas ’chad do.dran pa ni sems can gyi don bya ba la brtson pa’i byaṅ chub sems dpa’ bya ba daṅ mi bya bar śes śiṅ dran pa’o, śes bźin ni chos thams cad sgyu ma daṅ smig rgyu lta bur dṅos po med par śes pa’o.skye ba la mkhas pa ni phyi daṅ naṅ gi rten ciṅ ’brel bar ’byuṅ ba’i chos rnams rgyu gaṅ las ’bras bu gaṅ skye ba śes pa ste, ’di ltar phyi’i rten ciṅ ’brel bar ’byuṅ ba ni sa bon gyi rkyen gyis myu gu źes bya ba nas me tog gi rkyen gyis ’bras bu źes bya ba’i bar daṅ, naṅ gi rten ciṅ ’brel bar ’byuṅ ba yaṅ ma rig pa’i rkyen gyis ’du byed rnams śes bya ba nas skye ba’i rkyen gyis rga śi źes bya ba’i bar du phyi daṅ naṅ gi chos rnams rgyu daṅ rkyen las skye’i, bdag daṅ byed pa po las skye ba ma yin par rtogs pa’o.mi skye ba la mkhas pa ni gzuṅ ba daṅ ’dzin pa las dben pa’i don dam pa yoṅs su grub pa’i mtshan ñid ji lta ba bźin du śes pa ste, de ñan pa’o – "Skill concerning the unoriginated is knowledge of the highest meaning (paramārtha) beyond subject and object (grāhyagrāhakavivikta) characterized as completed (pariniṣpannalakṣaṇa) as it really is (yathābhūtajñāna), it is listening to that."mi sdug pa daṅ, byams pa daṅ, rten ciṅ ’brel bar ’byuṅ ba’i rnam pa źes bya ba’i tshig gsum gyis ’dod chags daṅ źe sdaṅ daṅ gti mug gsum gyi gñen po mi sdug pa bsgom pa la sogs pa rnam pa gsum yaṅ thos pa las ’byuṅ bar ston to. de la mi sdug pa ni ’dod chags kyi gñen po ste, de bas na mdo las kyaṅ: dge sloṅ rnal ’byor bas śi nas dur khrod du bor ba’i ro źag gcig lon pa źes bya ba nas khyi daṅ bya rgod daṅ ’phar ba la sogs pas zos pa yid la gzuṅ bar bya ste, źes gsuṅs pa’i phyir ro. byams pa ni źe sdaṅ gi gñen po ste, de bas na mdo sde las kyaṅ: byams pa daṅ ldan pa’i sems khon med pa, ’gran zla med pa, gnod pa med pas phyogs bcur mos te, khyab par byas te bsgrubs te gnas so, źes gsuṅs pa’i phyir ro. rten ciṅ ’brel bar ’byuṅ ba ni gti mug gi gñen po ste, de bas na mdo las kyaṅ: rten ciṅ ’brel bar ’byuṅ ba gaṅ źe na? gaṅ dus gsum gyi chos rnams la ’du byed tsam daṅ, chos tsam daṅ, dṅos po tsam daṅ, rgyu tsam daṅ, ’bras bu tsam ste, byed pa po med pa de ni rten ciṅ ’brel bar ’byuṅ ba źes bya ste, gaṅ gi tshe de yid la byas na gti mug śas6 che ba’i gaṅ zag rnams gti mug bsrabs par ’gyur ro, źes gsuṅs pa’i phyir ro.mi rtag pa ni dus gsum gyi ’dus byas thams cad skad cig ma re rer ’jig pas gnas pa med pa ste, de la ’di ltar ’das pa’i ’dus byas rnams ni skyes nas ’gag par snaṅ la, da ltar byuṅ ba’i ’dus byas rnams ni skyes pa’i skad cig phan chad du gnas pa’i mthu med la, ma ’oṅs pa’i ’dus byas rnams ni ma skyes la ’gag pa med par snaṅ ba’i phyir ro. de ltar ’dus byas mi rtag pa’i raṅ bźin de yaṅ sdug bsṅal rnam pa gsum gyi rten byed pas na sdug bsṅal ba źes bya ste, sdug bsṅal rnam pa gsum ni: 1) ’du byed kyi sdug bsṅal daṅ, 2) ’gyur ba’i sdug bsṅal daṅ, 3) sdug bsṅal gyi sdug bsṅal te; de la 1) ’du byed kyi sdug bsṅal rgyu daṅ rkyen gyis bskyed pa’i ’du byed thams cad ni mi rtag pa yin pa’i phyir ro; 2) ’gyur ba’i sdug bsṅal ni ’byor ba’i loṅs spyod daṅ bde ba’i tshor ba yaṅ phyis med par ’gyur źiṅ ma ’oṅs pa na rnam par smin pa’i yid du mi ’oṅ ba’i rgyu byed pa’i phyir ro. 3) sdug bsṅal gyi sdug bsṅal ni skye ba daṅ rga ba daṅ ’chi ba daṅ ’dod pa mi rñed pa daṅ sdug bsṅal gyi tshor ba rnams raṅ bźin gyis sdug bsṅal ba’i steṅ du nad la sogs pa sdug bsṅal gźan daṅ yaṅ ’brel ba’i phyir ro. bdag med pa ni ’dus byas daṅ ’dus ma byas kyi chos thams cad med pa ste, de dag kyaṅ thos pa daṅ ldan pas khoṅ du chud par byed pa’i phyir mi rtag pa’i rnam pa la sogs pa źes bya’o.źi ba ni ñon moṅs pa thams cad daṅ sdug bsṅal thams cad źi ba’i phyir mya ṅan las ’das pa la bya’o.stoṅ pa ñid daṅ, mtshan ma med pa daṅ, smon pa med pa źes bya ba rnam par thar pa’i sgo gsum po de dag gi don ni sṅar bśad zin te, de dag khoṅ du chud pa yaṅ thos pa las ’byuṅ ṅo źes bya bar sbyar ro.mṅon par ’du mi byed pa daṅ dge ba mṅon par ’du byed pa tshig gñis kyis ni srog gcod pa la sogs pa mi dge ba’i las spoṅ ba daṅ, dad pa daṅ brtson ’grus la sogs pa dge ba mṅon par ’du byed pa yaṅ thos pa las ’byuṅ źes ston to.bden pas byin gyis brlabs pa ni ’phags pa’i bden pa bźi mthoṅ ba’i mthu daṅ ldan par byed pa ste, bden pa mthoṅ ba’i mthu daṅ ldan par yaṅ thos pa las ’byuṅ bas na thos pa ni bden pas byin gyis brlabs pa’i rnam pa źes bya’o. yaṅ na, mdo dag las byaṅ chub sems dpa’ la sogs pas raṅ gis dam bcas pa’i bden pa’i tshig gis byin gyis brlabs na de bźin du ’gyur ba ste, de yaṅ thos pa las ’byuṅ źes bya bar sbyar ro. The concept satyavacana is explained by J. Burlingame in JRAS 1917 pp. 429-67.chud mi gzon pa ni las daṅ las kyi ’bras bu rnam par smin pa yod par lta ba’o.raṅ gi kha na las pa ni gźan la rag ma lus pa ste, gźan la śes pa ni rag ma lus par bya ba yaṅ thos pa las ’byuṅ ba’i phyir ro; raṅ gi sems sruṅ ba ni bya ba ma yin pa la mi ’jug par byed pa’o.brtson ’grus ni dge ba mṅon par ’du byed pa la sems spro ba yin la, de mi gtoṅ ba ni rtag tu byed pa daṅ gus par byed pa’o.chos ṅes par sems pa ni phuṅ po daṅ khams daṅ skye mched la sogs pa kun nas ñon moṅs pa daṅ rnam par byaṅ ba’i chos rnams blos gtan la ’bebs pa’o.ji ltar bśad pa’i chos rnams mñan nas rig pas bsams te, bsgoms na ñon moṅs pa spoṅ bar ’gyur bas ñon moṅs pa’i gñen po’i rnam pa źes bya’o. One would have expected pratipakṣa for vipakṣa; the two are, however, sometimes confused.raṅ gi phyogs ni byaṅ chub sems dpa’i phyogs te, rnam par byaṅ ba’i chos rnams daṅ, de’i ’khor du gtogs pa’i sems can rnams so. bsruṅ ba ni phyogs de dag gźan gyis mi ’phrogs śiṅ ñon moṅs pa’i dbaṅ du mi ’gyur bar byed pa’o.pha rol gyi phyogs bdud daṅ mu stegs can la sogs pa ste, de dag daṅ ñon moṅs pa tshar gcod pa ni de dag mthu med ciṅ ñams smod par byed pa’o.nor bdun ni 1) dad pa daṅ, 2) tshul khrims daṅ, 3) ṅo tsha śes pa daṅ, 4) khrel yod pa daṅ, 5) thos pa daṅ, 6) gtoṅ ba daṅ, 7) śes rab kyi nor te, thos pa la de dag ’du bar ’gyur bas yaṅ dag par ’du ba’i rnam pa źes bya’o. de ltar ’phags pa’i nor bdun po ’phags pa’i nor ma yin pa’i nor las śin tu khyad źugs pa de dag thos pa la yaṅ dag par ’du ba’i phyir dbul ba thams cad gcod pa źes bya ste, thos pa ’dis dbul ba thams cad gcod ces bya ba’i tha tshig go.mdzaṅs pa ni rig pa’i gnas lṅa khoṅ du chud pa’i gaṅ zag ste, thos pa ni ñes pa thams cad spoṅ ba’i gñen po yin pa daṅ, yon tan mchog rnams thob pa’i rgyu yin pa’i phyir mdzaṅs pa de dag gis bsṅags pa’i rnam pa źes bya’o. The five vidyāsthāna are śabda-, hetu-, adhyātma-, cikitsā-, and śilpakarmasthānavidyā, for ref. v. Edg s. v.
mkhas pa ni legs par bsams pa sems pa daṅ, legs par smra ba brjod pa daṅ, legs par bya ba’i las byed pa daṅ, legs par smras pa daṅ ñes par smras pa’i don khoṅ du chud par nus pa ste, de lta bu dag thos pa la mos par byed pas mkhas pa la mṅon par dga’ ba’i rnam pa źes bya’o. ’phags pa ñan thos daṅ, raṅ saṅs rgyas daṅ, de bźin gsegs pa bdag gis kyaṅ thos pa de lta bu thugs su chud pa’am, thos pa la ’phags pa rnams dgyes pas na thos pa ni ’phags pas kun śes pa’i rnam pa źes bya’o.
’phags pa ma yin pa ni so so’i skye bo ste, thos pa’i śes rab de dag kyaṅ dam pa’i chos la mos śiṅ dad par byed nus pa’i phyir ’phags pa ma yin pa dad par byed pa’i rnam pa źes bya’o.thos pa’i śes rab las ’phags pa’i bden pa bźi mthoṅ ba ’byuṅ ba’i phyir bden pa mthoṅ ba’i rnam pa źes bya’o.zag pa daṅ bcas pa’i phuṅ po’i skyon skye ba daṅ, rga ba la sogs pa rnam par spaṅs pa’i thabs kyaṅ thos pa las ’byuṅ bas na ’di skad ces bya’o. thos pa’i śes rab kyis ’khor ba’i chos rnams kyi skyon khoṅ du chud par byed pas na ’dus byas kyi skyon la yoṅs su ’jal ba’i rnam pa źes bya’o.don la rton pa la sogs pa rton pa bźi po yaṅ thos pa las ’byuṅ źes bya bar sbyar te, de dag gi don ni rton pa bźi’i skabs nas ’chad do.thos pa daṅ ldan na sdig pa mi dge ba’i chos rnams mi byed pas sdig pa thams cad mi bya ba’i rnam pa źes bya’o.bdag daṅ gźan la phan pa ni bdag daṅ gźan mi dge ba’i gnas nas bton te, dge ba la ’jog pa’am śes pa’i mthar phyin par byed pa ste, de yaṅ thos pa las byuṅ źes sbyar ro.thos pa ñid dge ba’i raṅ bźin yin pas legs par byas pa’i las kyi rnam pa źes bya’o; de ltar legs par byas pas na mi ’gyod pa’i rnam pa ste, dge ba byas pa ni phyis: ’di lta bu ’gyur ro, sñam du sems la gduṅ ba med pa’i phyir ro. Reading these two items as one ākāra as in T1 p. 196a2-3 and as the Sanskrit version, and thus making up the right number 84 ākāras altogether, not as in all Tibetan versions, where the two are separate as two ākāras.khyad par du ’gro ba ni yon tan khyad par can ma thob pa las thob par bya’am; yaṅ na, mos pa spyod pa’i sa yan chad goṅ nas goṅ du sa rnams gnon pa la bya ste, de yaṅ thos pa las ’byuṅ bar sbyar ro.saṅs rgyas kyi chos thams cad ni stobs daṅ mi ’jigs pa la sogs pa ste, mdor na saṅs rgyas kyi chos de dag thams cad kyaṅ thos pa la brten nas ’thob par ’gyur gyi, de las thabs gźan med pas na saṅs rgyas kyi chos thams cad ’thob pa’i rnam pa źes bya’o.


de dag ni byaṅ chub sems dpa’ rnams kyi thos pa rnam pa brgyad cu rtsa bźi źes bya’o.

eta ucyante bodhisattvānāṃ caturaśītiḥ śrutākārāḥ.

Those are called the eighty-four forms of learning of the bodhisattvas.


b) btsun pa śa ra dva ti’i bu, de la byaṅ chub sems dpa’ rnams kyi tshul bźin yid la byed pa la ’jug pa ni sum cu rtsa gñis te.

tatra, bhadanta śāradvatīputra, dvātriṃśad bodhisattvānāṃ yoniśomanasikārapravesāḥ.

b) [The entrance into insight (prajñāpraveśa), or, rather, how to understand the essential character of moments of existence (dharmalakṣaṇa) through that insight:] And, reverend Śāradvatīputra, the entrances [into the meaning of things as they are (tattvârtha) ] by thorough mental effort are thirty-two.

śes rab kyi ’jug pa bstan pa’i dbaṅ du byas nas btsun pa śa ra dva ti’i bu, de la byaṅ chub sems dpa’ rnams kyi tshul bźin yid la byed pa la ’jug pa ni sum cu rtsa gñis te źes bya ba la sogs pas gsuṅs so. V. also ṭ. fol. 89a1-2.
ṭ. fol. 97a7-b4: de la tshul ni ’phags pa’i lam daṅ mya ṅan las ’das pa la bya’o. de daṅ mthun par sems śiṅ bsgom pa ni tshul bźin yid la byed pa źes bya ste. tshul bźin yid la byed pa des de kho na ñid kyi don la ’jug ciṅ, tshul bźin yid la byed pa la ’jug pa źes bya’o. de ltar don la ’jug pa de yaṅ bsam pa’i śes rab kyis gtan la phab pa’i chos de la bsgom pa’i śes rab kyis goms par byas nas don rtogs par ’gyur te. de bas na ’di ni bsam pa daṅ bsgom pa’i śes rab yin par rig par bya’o. yaṅ na, tshul ’di ’phags pa’i lam daṅ mya ṅan las ’das pa’am, mṅon sum daṅ rjes su dpag pa la sogs pa’i rigs pa’am, ma nor bar ston pa’i mkhan po daṅ slob dpon gyi man ṅag la bya ste, de daṅ mi ’gal bar yid la byed pa ni tshul bźin yid la byed pa źes bya’o. tshul bźin yid la byed pa de la ’jug pas na tshul bźin yid la byed pa la ’jug pa ste. ’jug pa ni tshul bźin yid la byed pa la gnas pa’am, tshul bźin yid la byed pa de dag gis raṅ bźin daṅ rab tu dbye ba rtogs pa’o – "There reasonable (yukta) means the holy way (āryamārga) and extinction (nirvāṇa). (1) Reflecting on (cint-) and cultivating (bhāvaya-) in accordance with that is thorough mental effort (yoniśomanasikāra). By that thorough mental effort one penetrates the reality of things as they are, so it is called entrance through thorough mental effort (tena yoniśomanasikāreṇa tattvārthaṃ praviśati yoniśomanasikārapraveśa iti). Thus that entrance into the meaning [or thing pointed at by a word, cf. infra] (arthapraveśa) entails that the meaning is understood (artham adhigamyate) after having cultivated (bhāvayitvā) with the insight of cultivation (bhāvanā) the moments of existence discerned (viniścita) by the insight of reflection (cintā). So this is to be known as being the insight concerned with reflection and cultivation (cintābhāvanāprajñā).
Or (atha vā), (2) reasonable (yukta) is the holy path and extinction, but also logical arguments based on sense-perception, inference, etc. (pratyakṣānumānādinyāya), and the instructions of teachers and preceptors who are not imparting wrong instructions (abhrāntadeśikācāryopādhyāyopadeśa); and mental effort not in opposition to that is thorough mental effort (tadaviruddhamanasikāro manasikāra iti). One enters that mental effort, so it is called entrance into thorough mental effort (taṃ yoniśomanasikāraṃ praviśati yoniśomanasikāra iti).
Entrance (praveśa) is (2) to stay within thorough mental effort, or (1) to understand essence (svabhāva) and distinctions (prabheda) through those thorough mental efforts."
This section then is interpreted as cintāmayī and bhāvanāmayī prajñā while section a) on śrutākāra is of course śrutamayī prajñā "insight consisting of learning (or the teachings one has heard)". Cf. ṭ. fol. 89a3: de yaṅ thos pa las śes rab kyi bye brag phyed par gyur te...; and Bhāvanākrama I paragraph 9-12, p. 19821-22: tasmāc cintāmayyā prajñayā yuktyāgamābhyāṃ pratyavekṣya bhūtam eva vastusvarūpaṃ bhāvanīyam, vastūnāṃ svarūpaṃ ca paramārthato ’nutpāda evāgamato yuktitaś ca niścitam etc.
[The word artha primarily means "aim", "what is aimed at", possibly from the root ṛ- "to go, move, reach, obtain", see MMW s. v., then "thing" or "object" aimed at by a word, the "meaning" aimed at by a word. yoniśas is taken as equivalent to yukta and yukti and also to yoni, cf. the beginning of the next paragraph c) with notes].


sum cu rtsa gñis gaṅ źe na? ’di lta ste:

katame dvātriṃśat?

What thirty-two?


źi gnas kyi gnas la ’jug pa daṅ;lhag mthoṅ rnam par dpyod pa’i ’jug pa daṅ;sems las su ruṅ ba’i ’jug pa daṅ;lus dben pa la ’jug pa daṅ;sems dben pa la ’jug pa daṅ;rten ciṅ ’brel bar ’byuṅ ba la ’jug pa daṅ;bden pa’i rjes su ’thun pa la ’jug pa daṅ;chad pa med pa la ’jug pa daṅ;rtag pa med pa la ’jug pa daṅ;rgyu daṅ rkyen la ’jug pa daṅ;bdag med pa daṅ, sems can med pa daṅ, srog med pa daṅ, gaṅ zag med pa la ’jug pa daṅ;’oṅ ba daṅ, ’gro ba daṅ, gnas med pa la ’jug pa daṅ;mi ’pho źiṅ rgyu daṅ ’bras bu chud mi za ba la ’jug pa daṅ;stoṅ pa ñid daṅ, mtshan ma med pa daṅ, smon pa med pa la ’dris par byed pa la ’jug pa daṅ;stoṅ pa ñid daṅ, mtshan ma med pa daṅ, smon pa med pa la mṅon sum du mi byed pa la ’jug pa daṅ;bsam gtan daṅ, tiṅ ṅe ’dzin daṅ, sñoms par ’jug pa skyed pa’i tshul la ’jug pa daṅ;bsam gtan daṅ, tiṅ ṅe ’dzin la sñoms par ’jug pa’i dbaṅ gis mi skye ba la ’jug pa daṅ;mṅon par śes pa’i ye śes la ’jug pa daṅ;zag pa zad pa mṅon sum du byed pa ma yin pa la ’jug pa daṅ;naṅ du rtog pa la ’jug pa daṅ;ṅes par gyur par mi ’jug pa la ’jug pa daṅ;’dus byas kyi skyon yoṅs su ’jal ba la ’jug pa daṅ;’dus ma byas kyi chos mṅon sum du mi byed par ’jug pa daṅ;sems can thams cad la bdag med par so sor rtog pa la ’jug pa daṅ;sñiṅ rje chen po mi gtoṅ ba la ’jug pa daṅ;skye ba thams cad ’jigs par lta ba la ’jug pa daṅ;rtag tu bsams bźin du śes pas srid pa thams cad yoṅs su ’dzin par ’jug pa daṅ;yid byuṅ źiṅ ’dod chags daṅ bral bar ’jug pa daṅ;’dod chags daṅ bral ba’i chos kyaṅ mṅon sum du mi byed par ’jug pa daṅ;’dod pa’i dga’ ba’i yon tan yal bar ’dor ba la ’jug pa daṅ;chos kyi dga’ ba mi gtoṅ ba la ’jug pa daṅ;spros pa daṅ rnam par rtog pa thams cad spoṅ ba la ’jug pa daṅ;thabs mkhas pa’i spros pa daṅ rnam par rtog pa mi spoṅ bar ’jug pa ste.

tad yathā śamathasthānapraveśaḥ;vipaśyanāvyavacārapraveśaḥ;cittakarmaṇyatāpraveśaḥ;kāyavivekapraveśaḥ;cittavivekapraveśaḥ;pratītyasamutpādapraveśaḥ;satyānulomikapraveśaḥ;anucchedapraveśaḥ;aśāśvatapraveśaḥ;hetupratyayapraveśaḥ;nirātmaniḥsattvanirjīvaniḥpudgalapraveśaḥ;nirāgatigatisthitipraveśaḥ;asaṃkrāntihetuphalāvipraṇāśapraveśaḥ;śūnyatānimittāpraṇihitaparijayapraveśaḥ,śūnyatānimittāpraṇihitāsākṣātkaraṇapraveśaḥ;dhyānasamādhisamāpattyutpādanayapraveśo,dhyānasamādhisamāpattivaśānutpādapraveśaḥ;abhijñājñānapraveśaḥ,āsravakṣayāsākṣātkaraṇapraveśaḥ;adhyātmāvekṣāpraveśaḥ,aniyatāvatārapraveśaḥ;saṃskṛtadoṣaparitulanapraveśaḥ,asaṃskṛtāsākṣātkaraṇapraveśaḥ;sarvasattvanairātmyapratyavekṣaṇapraveśaḥ,mahākaruṇānutsargapraveśaḥ;sarvopapattibhayadarśanapraveśaḥ,saṃcintyanityasarvabhavaparigrahapraveśo;udvegavairāgyapraveśaḥ,vairāgyadharmāsākṣātkaraṇapraveśaḥ;kāmaratiguṇopekṣāpraveśaḥ,dharmaratyanutsargapraveśaḥ;sarvaprapañcavikalpaviratipraveśa,upāyakauśalyaprapañcavikalpāviratipraveśaḥ.

1) The entrance of the state of peaceful meditation;2) the entrance of discernment of expanded vision;3) [peaceful meditation and expanded vision is] the entrance of fitness of thought [being the ability to stay according to one’s wish (yathā kāmatayā) with any object concerned (adhyālambanârtha) ];4) the entrance of aloofness of the body [staying in a place conducive to renunciation like a mountain cave (śailaguhā) or in a forest (vana) ];and 5) the entrance of aloofness of thought [without the thought-constructions of cupidity, etc. (rāgābhilāṣākalpanā) ] [the two items designating the practice of cultivating peaceful meditation and expanded vision (śamathavipaśyanābhāvanāprayogadeśanā) ];6) the entrance of dependent origination;7) the entrance of accordance with truth;8) the entrance of no discontinuity;9) the entrance of no permanence;10) the entrance of causes and conditions;11) the entrance of no self, no animated being, no life-principle, no personality;12) the entrance of no going, coming or remaining;13) the entrance of the non-perishing of [the connection between] causes and effects [that is, actions and their fruits], though there is no transmigration [of any moment of existence whatsoever];14) the entrance of making oneself acquainted with emptiness, no distinguishing marks and absence of anything to long for,but 15) the entrance of not realizing emptiness, absence of distinguishing marks and absence of something to long for;16) the entrance of the way of producing [through insight (prajñā) ] meditation, concentration and states of concentration,but 17) the entrance of not being born by the power of meditation, concentration and states of concentration [but by the power of compassion (karuṇā), having the beings in the sphere of passion (kāmadhātu) in view];18) the entrance into knowledge of supernatural powers [through insight (prajñā) ],but 19) the entrance into not realizing the cessation of the sullied states [through compassion (karuṇā) ];20) the entrance of reflection on inner things,but 21) the entrance of not going into the secure [that is, extinction (nirvāṇa) ];22) the entrance of considering the imperfections of the conditioned,but 23) the entrance of not realizing the unconditioned;(p. 64) 24) the entrance of reflecting on the egolessness of all beings,but 25) the entrance of never giving up great compassion;26) the entrance of looking with fear upon any birth,but 27) the entrance of always assuming any form of being in accordance with intention;28) the entrance of disgust and no cupidity,but 29) the entrance of not realizing the moment of existence which is absence of cupidity [namely extinction (nirvāṇa) ];30) the entrance of equanimity when confronted with the qualities of joy in pleasure,but 31) the entrance of not giving up the joy in true religion;32) [to summarize the way of insight and compassion (prajñākaruṇāmārga) it is taught:] the entrance of appeasement of all discursive thinking and thought-constructions,but 33) the entrance of no appeasement of discursive thinking and thought-constructions as expedient means.

źi gnas kyi gnas źes bya ba la źi gnas ñid gnas yin pas źi gnas kyi gnas te, źi gnas de la ’jug pa ni źi gnas kyi raṅ bźin rtogs par byed pa’am, tiṅ ṅe ’dzin de la gnas par byed pa’o – "Peaceful meditation is a state, thus it is said "the state of peaceful meditation" (śamatha eva sthānam śamathasthānam iti) (karmadhāraya-compound). Entering that peaceful meditation means "one understands the essence of peaceful meditation" or "one stays in that concentration" (tasmiñ śamathe praveśa iti śamathasvabhāvam adhigacchati vā tasmin samādhau tiṣṭhati vā)."lhag mthoṅ gis ’dus byas daṅ ’dus ma byas kyi chos rnams kyi raṅ daṅ spyi’i mtshan ñid rab tu rnam par ’byed pas na lhag mthoṅ rnam par dpyod pa źes bya la, de ltar rnam par dpyad pa las de kho na ñid kyi don rtogs par ’gyur bas ’jug pa źes kyaṅ bya’o – "By expanded vision one discerns the special and general characteristics of the conditioned and unconditioned moments of existence, thus it is called discernment of expanded vision (vipaśyanayā saṃskṛtāsaṃskṛtānāṃ dharmāṇāṃ svasāmanyalakṣaṇāni pravicinotīti vipaśyanāvyavacāraḥ); and by such discernment the reality of things as they are is understood, thus it is called entrance (evaṃvyavacārāt tattvārtho ’dhigamyate ceti praveśaḥ)."źi gnas daṅ lhag mthoṅ de ñid kyaṅ sems las su ruṅ ba la ’jug pa bśad de, dmigs par bya ba’i don la ci dgar gnas su btub pa ni źi gnas daṅ lhag mthoṅ yin pa’i phyir ro.lus dben pa daṅ sems dben pa la ’jug pa gñis kyis ni źi gnas daṅ lhag mthoṅ bsgom pa la sbyor ba bstan te, spoṅ ba daṅ mthun pa’i gnas lam brag phug daṅ nags tshal la sogs pa la gnas na chags par ’gyur ba’i yul ’gro ba bzaṅ mo la sogs pa med pa daṅ, ’dod pa la ’dun pa la sogs pa rtog pa med pa na źi gnas daṅ lhag mthoṅ la ’jug par ’gyur ba’i phyir ro.rten ciṅ ’brel bar ’byuṅ ba ni phyi daṅ naṅ gi bye brag gis rnam pa gñis te, sṅar bśad par zad do, de la ’jug pa ni de dag gi mtshan ñid rtogs par byed ces bya ba’i tha tshig go.bden pa’i rjes su mthun pa ni ’phags pa’i bden pa bźi tshul bźin du yid la byed pa’o, yaṅ na khams gsum la yid byuṅ ba daṅ, ñon moṅs pa’i tshogs rnams daṅ bral bar dga’ ba daṅ, mya ṅan las ’das pa la gcig tu phyogs pa daṅ, ’phags pa’i lam sgrub par mos pa ni bden pa bźi rtogs pa’i rgyu yin pas bden pa’i rjes su mthun pa źes bya’o. yaṅ na bden pa bźi ni mthoṅ ba’i lam gyis rtogs par bya ba yin pas de daṅ mthun pa ni ṅes par ’byed pa’i cha bźi yin no; bden pa’i rjes su ’jug pa’i chos des ’jug pas na bden pa’i rjes su mthun par ’jug pa źes kyaṅ bya ste, chos des de kho na’i don rtogs par byed ces bya ba’i tha tshig go. yaṅ na bden pa’i rjes su mthun pa’i rtogs par bya ba’i phyir ’jug ces bya bar yaṅ bśad do.chad pa med pa daṅ rtag pa med pa tshig gñis ni rten ciṅ ’brel bar ’byuṅ ba’i don phyin ci ma log par rtogs pa bstan te, phyi daṅ naṅ gi rten ciṅ ’brel bar ’byuṅ ba rgyu daṅ rkyen la brten nas skad cig ma’i tshul gyis skye ba rgyun mi ’chad pa daṅ, de dag ñid kyaṅ mi rtag pa yin par rtogs na chad pa med pa daṅ rtag pa med pa la ’jug pa źes bya’o. de ñid kyi don gsal bar bstan pa’i phyir rgyu daṅ rkyen la ’jug pa źes gsuṅs so, ma rig pa daṅ sa bon lta bu ni rgyu yin la, sa daṅ chu la sogs pa ni rkyen yin par śes pa’o.bdag la sogs pa mu stegs can gyis bdag tu btags pa’i miṅ gi rnam graṅs ni sṅar bśad par zad de, de dag med par rtogs par byed pas na bdag med pa nas gaṅ zag gi bar du med pa la ’jug pa źes bya’o, cf. fol. 25a5-b3.’oṅ ba daṅ, ’gro ba daṅ, gnas med ces bya ba ni skye ba daṅ ’gag pa daṅ ’jug pa med pa ste, de ltar rtogs pa la ’jug pa źes bya’o.mi ’pho źiṅ rgyu daṅ ’bras bu chud mi za ba la ’jug pa ni ’di nas pha rol tu chos rdul tsam yaṅ ’phos pa med pa la, las dge ba daṅ mi dge ba’i ’bras bu yaṅ chud mi za bar śes pa’o.stoṅ pa ñid daṅ, mtshan ma med pa daṅ, smon pa med pa ’dris par byed pa la ’jug pa źes bya ba la sogs pa ’di man chad kyis mi gnas pa’i mya ṅan las ’das pa’i lam śes rab daṅ sñiṅ rjes zin par ston te, ’khor ba na gnas kyaṅ śes rab kyis ’khor ba’i dṅos po thams cad stoṅ pa ñid la sogs par khoṅ du chud pas ’khor ba’i skyon gyis kyaṅ ma gos la, de ltar khoṅ du chud kyaṅ sñiṅ rjes sems can gyi don du ’khor bar ’jug pas na stoṅ pa ñid daṅ mtshan ma med pa daṅ smon pa med pa mṅon sum du mi byed pa la ’jug par yaṅ byed ces bya bar sbyar te. ’og ma dag la yaṅ lam gñis kyis zin par de bźin du sbyar ro – "... This and the following teaches the way to extinction not founded anywhere (apratiṣṭhitanirvāṇamārga) including both insight (prajñā) and compassion (karuṇā). (The bodhisattva) is not sullied by any of the imperfections of existence (saṃsāradoṣair nopalipyate) even though he stays in existence, because he with insight (prajñā) has penetrated the emptiness and so on of all things in existence. But even so, by compassion (karuṇā) for the sake of all beings he enters existence (saṃsāra), so it is said "entrance into not realizing....". This applies also for the following pairs of items."
On the connection between the concepts of parijaya and asākṣātkaraṇa cf. Āloka p. 6817: tatphalāsākṣadkaraṇād dhyānaparijayaṃ karoti, and the introduction supra.bsam gtan bźi daṅ, nam mkha’ mdzod daṅ, dpa’ bar ’gro ba la sogs pa’i tiṅ ṅe ’dzin daṅ mthar gyis gnas pa’i sñoms par ’jug pa rnams śes rab kyis bskyed pa’i tshul la ’jug ste, dbaṅ byed kyaṅ sñiṅ rje’i dbaṅ gis ’dod pa’i khams kyi sems can rnams la lta ba’i phyir bsam gtan la sogs pa de dag gi dbaṅ gis mi skye ba la ’jug go.mṅon par śes pa ñid ye śes yin pas mṅon par śes pa’i ye śes yin pa’am, yaṅ na bsam gtan mi zad pa’i skabs su bśad pa ltar mṅon par śes pa daṅ ye śes źes phye ste, śes rab kyis de lta bu dag bskyed pa la ’jug kyaṅ, sñiṅ rjes zag pa zad pa mṅon sum du byed pa ma yin pa la ’jug go.śes rab kyis kyaṅ kun tu brtags pa’i chos rnams raṅ bźin med ciṅ sems tsam du śes pa ni naṅ du rtog pa la ’jug pa yin la, de ltar śes kyaṅ sñiṅ rje’i dbaṅ gis mya ṅan las ’das pa ṅes par gyur par mi ’jug go.śes rab kyis ’dus byas kyi skyon mi rtag pa la sogs pa la yoṅs su ’jal yaṅ, sñiṅ rjes ’dus ma byas kyi chos mya ṅan las ’das pa mṅon sum du mi byed par ’jug go.śes rab kyis sems can thams cad la bdag med par so sor rtogs te, don bya ba’i gnas raṅ bźin med par śes kyaṅ, sñiṅ rje chen pos mi gtoṅ ste, sems can gyi don yaṅ byed do. de la rnam pa bdun gyis na sñiṅ rje las sñiṅ rje chen po khyad par du ’phags te, 1) raṅ bźin ni źe mi sdaṅ ba daṅ gti mi mug pa’i raṅ bźin yin pa’i phyir ro; 2) rnam pa ni sdug bsṅal gcig daṅ gñis nas sdug bsṅal brgya stoṅ maṅ po’i bar la rtog pa’i phyir ro; 3) dmigs pa ni ’jig rten gyi khams thams cad la dmigs pa’i phyir ro; 4) sa ni bsam gtan bźi pa’i sar gtogs pa’i phyir ro; 5) rgyud ni byaṅ chub sems dpa’i rgyud la ’byuṅ ba’i phyir ro; 6) ’dod chags daṅ bral ba thob pa ni ’dod pa’i khams thams cad kyi ’dod chags daṅ bral ba thob pa’i phyir ro; 7) sñiṅ rje’i skye mched mi mñam pa ni sems can thams cad la skyob par byed pa’i phyir ro.skye ba thams cad ni ’gro ba rgyud lṅa’i skye ba rnams te, so so’i skye bo dag ltar skye ba de dag tu ñon moṅs pa’i dbaṅ du gyur nas yaṅ daṅ yaṅ du skye bas ’jigs par lta ba ni śes rab ste, de ltar rtogs kyaṅ sñiṅ rje chen po’i smon lam gyi dbaṅ gis rtag tu bsams bźin du śes pas srid pa thams cad kyaṅ yoṅs su ’dzin to.śes rab kyis khams gsum gyi chos rnams la yid byuṅ źiṅ ’dod chags daṅ bral bar ’jug kyaṅ, sñiṅ rjes ’dod chags daṅ bral ba’i chos mya ṅan las ’das pa yaṅ mṅon sum du mi byed do.’dod pa ñid dga’ ba yin la, de dag so so’i skye bos bsten par bya ba yin pas yon tan yaṅ yin te, śes rab kyis de dag raṅ bźin med par rtogs pas ’dod pa’i yon tan lṅa po gaṅ la yaṅ chags pa daṅ sdaṅ ba med de, yal bar ’dor ba la ’jug pa yin yaṅ, chos rnams kyi don rtogs nas yid sim par ’gyur ba’i chos kyi dga’ ba yaṅ mi gtoṅ ba la ’jug go.śes rab daṅ sñiṅ rje’i lam mdor bsdus te bstan pa’i phyir spros pa daṅ rnam par rtog pa thams cad spoṅ ba la ’jug pa daṅ, thabs mkhas pa’i spros pa daṅ rnam par rtog pa mi spoṅ bar ’jug pa źes gsuṅs te, śes rab kyis lus daṅ ṅag gi las kyi spros pa daṅ sems kyi rnam par rtog pa thams cad spoṅ yaṅ, dga’ ldan nas ’bab pa daṅ yum gyi lhums su gśegs pa la sogs pa sku’i phrin las daṅ chos ston pa’i gsuṅ gi phrin las kyi thabs mkhas pa’i spros pa daṅ thugs kyi chos rnams kyi mtshan ñid rab tu ’byed pa’i rnam par rtog pa yaṅ mi spoṅ źes sbyar ro.


btsun pa śa ra dva ti’i bu, de dag ni byaṅ chub sems dpa’ rnams kyi tshul bźin yid la byed pa la ’jug pa sum cu rtsa gñis śes bya’o.

eta ucyante, bhadanta śāradvatīputra, bodhisattvānāṃ dvātriṃśad yoniśomanasikārapraveśāḥ.

Those are called, reverend Śāradvatīputra, the bodhisattvas’ thirty-two entrances of thorough mental effort.


c) btsun pa śa ra dva ti’i bu, gźan yaṅ tshul bźin źes bya ba, de ni rigs pa’i tshig go;de ni tshul gyi tshig go;de ni sgo’i tshig go;de ni kha’i tshig go;de ni rgyu’i tshig go;de ni rkyen gyi tshig go;de ni mi ’gog pa’i tshig go;de ni mi ’gal ba’i tshig go;de ni btaṅ sñoms kyi tshig go;de ni len pa med pa’i tshig go;de ni dor ba med pa’i tshig go;de ni rkyen med pa’i tshig go;de ni rten pa med pa’i tshig go;de ni mi gnas pa’i tshig go;de ni ma g-yos pa’i tshig go;de ni rnam par ma g-yos pa’i tshig go;de ni sgro btags pa med pa’i tshig go;de ni mñam pa ñid kyi tshig go;de ni mi mñam pa med pa’i tshig go;de ni bden pa’i tshig go;de ni yaṅ dag pa’i tshig go;de ni mi ’gyur ba’i tshig go;de ni phyir bya ba med pa’i tshig go;de ni źi ba’i tshig go;de ni rab tu źi ba’i tshig go;de ni ñe bar źi ba’i tshig go;de ni spros pa med pa’i tshig go;de ni ’degs pa med pa’i tshig go;de ni gźag pa med pa’i tshig go;de ni ma tshaṅ ba med pa’i tshig go;de ni lhag pa med pa’i tshig go;de ni phyir dbyuṅ du med pa’i tshig go;de ni gñen po med pa’i tshig go;de ni dam pa’i tshig go;de ni de kho na’i tshig go;de ni de bźin ñid kyi tshig go;de ni ma nor ba de bźin ñid kyi tshig go;de ni gźan ma yin pa de bźin ñid kyi tshig go;de ni ji lta ba bźin gyi tshig go;de ni chud mi za ba’i tshig go;de ni yaṅ dag pa’i mtha’i tshig go;de ni dus gsum mñam pa ñid kyi tshig go;de ni dus gsum yoṅs su ma chad pa’i tshig go;de ni gzugs la rnam par śes pa mi gnas pa’i tshig go,de ni tshor ba daṅ, ’du śes daṅ, ’du byed daṅ, rnam par śes pa la rnam par śes pa mi gnas pa’i tshig go;de ni sa’i khams la rnam par śes pa mi gnas pa’i tshig go;de bźin du de ni chu’i khams daṅ, me’i khams daṅ, rluṅ gi khams la rnam par śes pa mi gnas pa’i tshig go;de ni mig daṅ gzugs daṅ mig gi rnam par śes pa’i khams la mi gnas pa’i tshig go;de bźin du de ni rna ba daṅ sgra daṅ rna ba’i rnam par śes pa’i khams daṅ, sna daṅ dri daṅ sna’i rnam par śes pa’i khams daṅ, lce daṅ ro daṅ lce’i rnam par śes pa’i khams daṅ, lus daṅ reg bya daṅ lus kyi rnam par śes pa’i khams daṅ, yid daṅ chos daṅ yid kyi rnam par śes pa’i khams la mi gnas pa’i tshig go;de ni don la rton pa’i tshig go;de ni chos la rton pa’i tshig go;de ni ye śes la rton pa’i tshig go;de ni ṅes pa’i don gyi mdo sde la rton pa’i tshig go.

punar aparaṃ, bhadanta śāradvatīputra, yonir iti yuktipadam etat,yuktapadam etat,dvārapadam etat,mukhapadam etat,hetupadam etat,pratyayapadam etat,anirodhapadam etat,avirodhapadam etat,upekṣāpadam etat,anupādānapadam etat,ahānapadam etat,apratyayapadam etat,anāśrayapadam etat,anāśritapadam etat,acalitapadam etat,avicalitapadam etat,asamāropapadam etat,samatāpadam etat,aviṣamatāpadam etat,satyapadam etat,samyakpadam etat,nirvikārapadam etat,apunaḥkāryapadam etat,śāntapadam etat,praśāntapadam etat,upaśāntapadam etat,niṣprapañcapadam etat,anutkṣepapadam etat,aprakṣepapadam etat,avikalapadam etat,anadhikapadam etat,aniṣkāsanapadam etat,niṣpratipakṣapadam etat,paramapadam etat,tattvapadam etat,tathatāpadam etat,avitathāpadam etat,ananyatathatāpadam etatyathābhūtapadam etat,avipraṇāśapadam etat,bhūtakoṭipadam etat,trikālasamatāpadam etat,trikālāparicchedapadam etat,rūpavijñānāniśrayapadam etat,vedanāsaṃjñāsaṃskāravijñānavijñānāniśrayapadam etat,pṛthivīdhātuvijñānāniśrayapadam etat,evam abdhātutejodhātuvāyudhātuvijñānāniśrayapadam etat,cakṣūrūpacakṣurvijñānadhātvaniśrayapadam etat,evam śrotraśabdaśrotravijñānadhātughrāṇagandhaghrāṇavijñānadhātujihvārasajihvāvijñānadhātukāyaspraṣṭavyakāyavijñānadhātumanodharmamanovijñānadhātvaniśrayapadam etat,arthapratisaraṇapadam etat,dharmapratisaraṇapadam etat,jñānapratisaraṇapadam etat,nitārthapratisaraṇapadam etat.

c) [The entrance of insight (prajñāpraveśa) is called “thorough” (yoni), and now its meaning (artha) is explained, its “etymology” (nirukti):]Further, reverend Śāradvatīputra, thorough, this is a word for reasoning,a word for reasonable [the true essence (aviparītasvabhāva) of moments of existence, or, as explained in the preceding paragraph, the holy way or extinction (āryamārganirvāṇa) ],a word for gate into [the meditations (dhyāna), supernormal knowledges (abhijñā), powers (bala) and intrepidities (vaiśāradya) and so on, endless qualities],a word for door into,a word for causes,a word for conditions [by which two the qualities of a Buddha are attained],a word for no cessation,a word for no conflict,a word for equanimity,a word for no grasping,a word for no rejection,a word for no conditions,a word for not leaning on,a word for not being established anywhere,a word for being unchangeable,a word for being unperturbed,a word for being beyond attribution,a word for sameness,a word for never not the same,a word for truth,a word for right,a word for unchanging,a word for not having to be repeated,a word for peaceful,a word for absolutely peaceful,a word for calm,a word for no discursive thinking,[and thus also] a word for not doing away with [the adventitious vices (āgantukakleśa) ],a word for not adding [anything to the originally pure thought (prakṛtiprabhāsvaracitta) because of thorough (yoniśaḥ) understanding],a word for the unimpaired,a word for having no superior,a word for no getting out of,a word for having no contrary,a word for the highest,a word for the real,a word for things being such as they are,a word for not being apart from things such as they are,a word for things being nothing else but what they are,(p. 65) a word for being qua being,a word for never breaking the contact [with awakening (bodhi) ],a word for the limit of being,a word for sameness of the three times,a word for not breaking up into [categories of] three times,a word for consciousness not being attached to forms [which are imagined (parikalpita) by ordinary people (pṛthagjana) ],a word for consciousness not being attached to feeling, perception, formative factors or consciousness,a word for consciousness not being attached to the element of earth,and thus a word for consciousness not being attached to the element of water, the element of fire or the element of wind,a word for not being attached to the sphere of eye, form or eye-consciousness,and thus a word for not being attached to the sphere of ear, sound or ear-consciousness, the sphere of nose, smell or nose-consciousness, the sphere of tongue, taste or tongue-consciousness, the sphere of body, tangibles or body consciousness or to the sphere of mind, moments of existence or mind-consciousness,a word for reliance on meaning,a word for reliance on religion,a word for reliance on knowledge,a word for reliance on the explicit meaning.

śes rab kyi ’jug pa tshul bźin źes bya ba de’i don yaṅ bstan ciṅ, ṅes pa’i tshig gi dbaṅ du byas nas btsun pa śa ra dva ti’i bu, gźan yaṅ tshul bźin źes bya ba, de ni rigs pa’i tshig go źes bya ba la sogs pa gsuṅs so. (107a)
yoni means "uterus" "the female generative organ", then "place of birth", "origin", and adverbially "fundamentally", "thoroughly". The translation "thorough" is kept to connect it with yoniśomanasikāra, "thorough mental activity", notwithstanding the play on the other meanings.
Cf. Buddhasaṃgītisūtra as quoted in Bhāvanākrama I p. 19914-16: katamā yoniśaḥ pṛcchā? katamā yoniḥ? āha: anutpādo yoniḥ, tasya pṛcchā yoniśaḥ pṛcchā. Tib. (ibid. p. 2469-12): tshul bźin ’dri ba ni gaṅ lags? tshul bźin ni gaṅ lags? bka’ stsal pa: skye ba med pa ni tshul bźin no, de ’dri ba ni tshul bźin ’dri ba’o.slu bar mi byed pa ni rigs pa ste, rigs pa bźi daṅ ldan pa’i śes pa la tshul bźin bya’o. rigs pa bźi ni 1) ltos pa’i rigs pa daṅ, 2) bya ba byed pa’i rigs pa daṅ, 3) ’thad par bsgrub pa’i rigs pa daṅ, 4) chos ñid kyi rigs pa’o. [de la 1) ltos pa’i rigs pa ni: rgyu gaṅ daṅ rkyen gaṅ dag la ltos te chos gaṅ skye ba’o; 2) bya ba byed pa’i rigs pa ni: chos skyes pa rnams raṅ gi bya ba byed pa ste, ’di lta ste dper na mig gis gzugs rnams la lta bar byed pa daṅ, rna bas sgra rnams ñan pa byed la sogs pa lta bu’o; 3) ’thad par bsgrub pa’i rigs pa ni: chos rnams mi rtag pa’am, rten ciṅ ’brel bar ’byuṅ ba’am, sdug bsṅal ba’am, stoṅ pa’am, bdag med pa’o, źes tshad ma gsum po yid ches pa’i luṅ daṅ mṅon sum daṅ rjes su dpag pa dag gis ñe bar rtog par byed ciṅ mi rtag pa la sogs par sgrub par byed pa’o; 4) chos ñid kyi rigs pa ni: ci’i phyir ’jig rten gnas pa de lta bur gyur pa yin, ci’i phyir sa’i mtshan ñid sra ba yin źes bya ba nas chos thams cad la yaṅ sbyar te ci’i phyir de lta bu yin źe na? de ni chos ñid yin te, chos de dag gi raṅ bźin de yin źiṅ, de dag gi ṅo bo ñid de lta bu yin pas, chos ñid de gaṅ kho na yin pa de ñid ’dir rigs pa yin no.] rigs pa de lta bu dag tshul bźin yid la byed pas śes śiṅ rtogs par byed pas na, tshul bźin źes bya ba de ni rigs pa’i tshig ces bya ste. ’og ma rnams la yaṅ tshul de bźin du sbyar ro – "It does not cheat, thus it is reasoning (yukti), thorough should be taken in the meaning ’knowledge furnished with four kinds of reasoning’ (caturyuktiyuktajñāne yonir iti). The four kinds of reasoning are 1) reasoning concerned with dependence on (apekṣāyukti), 2) reasoning concerned with cause and effect (kāryakāraṇayukti), 3) reasoning by presenting proof (upapattisādhanayukti), and 4) reasoning concerned with the true nature of things (dharmatāyukti). [There, 1) reasoning concerned with dependence on [is concerned with] the causes and conditions by which moments of existence arise; 2) reasoning concerned with cause and effect [is concerned with] the appropriate effects that arisen moments of existence cause, as when the eye sees form and the ear hears sound; 3) reasoning by presenting proof investigates the moments of existence as impermanent, originated in dependence, as suffering, empty, and selfless by the three standards of knowledge, viz. canonical scripture, sense-perception and inference, and it establishes impermanence, etc.; and 4) reasoning concerned with the true nature of things [is concerned with questions like] "Why has the state of the world become like this?", "Why does the element earth have the essential character of hardness?", etc., with regard to all things [it asks the question] "Why is it like that?" [and answers like] "This is the nature (prakṛti) of those moments of existence, such is their essence (svabhāva), this is the true nature of things (dharmatā)". That reasoning is concerned with that very true nature of things.] That reasoning knows and understands by thorough mental effort, thus one says ’Thorough is a word for reasoning’. The following should be understood accordingly."
The part in brackets is a quotation from Śbh with some changes – mainly the substitution of dharma for skandha – and abbreviations: 1. (fol. 7A33, S p. 14112-13, D fol. 57b3-4) tatrotpattyapekṣā yair hetubhir yaiḥ pratyayaiḥ skandhānāṃ prādurbhāvo bhavati / 2. (7A34-5, S p. 1423-6, D fol. 57b6-7) kāryakāraṇayuktiḥ katamā / yeṣām utpannānāṃ skandhānāṃ svena hetunā svena pratyayena tasmiṃs tasmin svakāryakaraṇe viniyogas tad yathā / cakṣuṣā rūpāṇi draṣṭavyāni / śrotre(5)ṇa sabdāḥ śrotavyāḥ / 3) (fol. 7A35-6, 14212-1431, D fol. 58a1-4) upapattisādhanayuktiḥ [(5) katamā /] anityāḥ skandhāḥ pratītyasamutpannā duḥkhāḥ śūnyā anātmāna iti tribhiḥ pramāṇair upaparīkṣate [yad uta] āptāgamena pratyakṣeṇānumānena ca / [ebhis tribhiḥ pramāṇairupapattiyuktaiḥ satāṃ hṛdayagrāhakair vyavasthāpanā] sādhanā kriyate [/ yad uta skandha-]anityatāyā vā .... 4) ( fol. 7A37-7B31, S p. 1434-13, D fol. 58a4-7) dharmatāyuktiḥ katamā / kena kāraṇena .... tathābhūto lokasanniveśaḥ kena kāraṇena kharalakṣaṇā pṛthivī ..(7B3).. prakṛtir eṣāṃ dharmāṇām iyaṃ svabhāva eṣām īdṛśaḥ / dharmataiṣā / yaiva cāsau dharmatā / saivātra yuktir [yoga upāyaḥ /]
Msa. p. 1685-11 treats the four ways of reasoning by relating them to the three vehicles, but also to thorough mental effort (yoniśomanasikāra), which indeed is also the the basis of the treatment in ṭ. Differing somewhat from ṭ and Śbh, the fourth reasoning is concerned with the unthinkable (acintya) nature of things. yuktiprajñaptivyavasthānaṃ caturvidhaṃ / apekṣāyuktiḥ / kāryakāraṇayuktiḥ / upapattisādhanayuktiḥ / dharmatāyuktiś ca / yānaprajñaptivyavasthānaṃ trividhaṃ / śrāvakayānaṃ / pratyekabuddhayānaṃ / mahāyānaṃ ca / tatrāpekṣāyuktis triṣv api yāneṣu yoniśomanaskāraḥ / tam apekṣya tena pratyayena lokottarāyāḥ samyagdṛṣṭer utpādāt / kāryakāraṇayuktiḥ samyagdṛṣṭiḥ saphalā / upapattisādhanayuktiḥ / pratyakṣādibhiḥ pramāṇaiḥ parīkṣā / dharmatāyuktir acintyaṃ sthānaṃ / siddhā hi dharmatā na punaś cintyā / kasmāt / yoniśomanaskārāt samyagdṛṣṭir bhavati / tato vā kleśaprahāṇaṃ phalam ity evam ādi /
Saṃdhinirmocana X, 7,4,7 treats the four in great detail. Cf. also Mavbh III, 12; Bbh p. 37 and 29317-18; Śbh p. 3698ff.
Notes to the Sanskrit text: 1) S yair hetupratyayaiḥ for yair hetubhir yaiḥ pratyayaiḥ 2) ṭ probably read tatrāpekṣāyuktir yān hetūn yān pratyayān apekṣya ye ’pi dharmā prādurbhavanti 3) As tib. bya ba byed pa’i rigs pa gaṅ źe na / ...gaṅ yin pa rnams MS ...yuktir yād and no daṇḍa 4) MS tasmims 5) MS śabdā 6) ṭ probably abbreviated as kāryakāraṇayuktir utpannānāṃ dharmāṇāṃ svakāryakaraṇas tad yathā / cakṣuṣā rūpāṇi draṣṭavyāni / śrotreṇa sabdāḥ śrotavyāḥ / 7) Bracketed part not in ṭ 8) ṭ has dharmāḥ for skandhāḥ MS, S has iti, which probably is a misreading for the visarga and has no equivalent in tib. 9) MS om. visarga 10) MS yad uta tāptāgamena 11) W ...saṃni... 12) ṭ abbreviates * ity ādi yāvat kena kāraṇena tathābhūtāḥ sarvadharmāḥ 13) W idaṃ 14) As tib. and ṭ de dag gi MS,S,W eṣa 15) W om. daṇḍa 16) W ...ṣā(ṃ); daṇḍa as in tib. and ṭ, MS,S,W om. 17) As tib. and ṭ gaṅ kho na yin pa S,W caiva MS ambiguous.tshul ni chos rnams kyi raṅ bźin phyin ci ma log pa’am, yaṅ na tshul bźin yid la byed pa sum cu rtsa gñis kyi skabs su (ṭ. 97b1, v. supra) tshul gyi sgra bśad pa de la bya’o.sgo ni tshul bźin te, bsam gtan daṅ, mṅon par śes pa daṅ, stobs daṅ mi ’jigs pa la sogs pa yon tan dpag tu med pa rnams sgrub pa’i sgo yin pa’i phyir ro, yaṅ na de’i sgo nas chos yaṅs śiṅ rgya che ba rtogs par byed pa’i phyir ro.kha ni rten la bya ste, tshul bźin la brten nas chos phra źiṅ zab pa rnams rtogs par byed pa’i phyir ro.rgyu daṅ rkyen źes bya ba ni tshul bźin te, saṅs rgyas kyi chos rnams kyi rgyu daṅ rkyen yin pa’i phyir ro.mi ’gog pa źes bya ba la tshul bźin daṅ mi mthun pa’i rgyu daṅ rkyen rnams kyis de med par ’gyur ba ni ’gog pa źes bya na, tshul bźin yid la byed pa las byuṅ ba’i śes rab dkar po’i chos kyi mthu daṅ ldan pas raṅ daṅ mi mthun pa’i rkyen gyis med par mi ’gyur bas mi ’gog pa’i tshig ces bya’o.mi ’gal ba ni chos rnams kyi raṅ bźin ji ltar gnas pa las mi ’gal bar rtogs pa’i phyir ro.tshul bźin gyi dṅos po thams cad bdag med par rtogs te, gaṅ la yaṅ chags pa daṅ sdaṅ ba med par btaṅ sñoms kyi tshig ces bya’o.The last two mentiond items refer to not being dependent upon ālayavijñāna: kun gźi rnam par śes pa la mi gnas pas na mi rten pa’i tshig ces bya’o. mi gnas pa ni rten smos ma thag pa de gñis la mi gnas pa’i phyir ro. yaṅ na gaṅ zag gi dṅos por chags pa med pas na rten pa med pa’o, chos kyi dṅos por chags pa med pas na mi rten pa’o, kun gźi rnam par śes pa’i gnas la gnas pa med pas na mi gnas pa źes bya’o. The last paragraph seems to have read three items in the sūtra, the two and, in addition, rten pa med pa – *aniśraya (?) ST has mi rten pa for DLNQ rten pa med pa, and the respective editions may have lost one of the two items. The text read by ṭ may originally have had aniśrayapadam etad, anāśrayapadam etad, anāśritapadam etat, and the three have been interpreted respectively as freedom from grasping for substance in a) the pudgala and b) the dharmas, and from being dependent on the ālayavijñāna.ma g-yos pa ni raṅ bźin gźan du mi ’gyur ba ste, tshul bźin de ṅo bo ñid kyis dag pas nams kyaṅ raṅ bźin gźan du mi ’gyur ba la bya’o; rnam par ma g-yos pa źes bya ba la mi mthun pa’i phyogs kyi dbaṅ du gyur pa ni rnam par g-yos pa ste, tshul bźin des mi mthun pa’i phyogs spaṅs pas mi rtag pa la rtag par ’dzin pa la sogs pa mi mthun pa’i phyogs kyi chos rnams kyi dbaṅ du mi ’gyur ba’i phyir rnam par ma g-yos pa źes bya’o, yaṅ na ’dod chags la sogs pa kun nas ñon moṅs pa daṅ phyin ci log bźi’i rluṅ gis bskyod par mi nus pas na ma g-yos pa źes bya la, phuṅ po daṅ khams daṅ skye mched la mṅon par chags pa’i rluṅ gis bskyod par mi nus pas na rnam par ma g-yos pa źes bya’o.kun brtags pa’i ṅo bo la yod par mi ’dzin pas na sgro btags pa med pa’o. ".... not apprehending the imagined essence (parikalpitasvabhāva) as existent".rtag pa daṅ chad pa la sogs pa’i mthar ma lhuṅ ba na mñam pa ñid do, gzugs daṅ sgra la sogs pa’i mtshan ma rnam pa sna tshogs su ’byed pa ni mñam pa ste, chos thams cad brjod du med pa’i raṅ bźin du tshul bźin gyis khoṅ du chud pa la de lta bur ’byed pa med pas mi mñam pa med pa’o.ji ltar bsgrubs pa bźin du ’bras bu ’thob ste, mi slu bas na bden pa’i tshig go, ’phags pa rnams kyi spyod yul yin pa’am, tshad ma gsum daṅ mi ’gal bas yaṅ dag pa’i tshig go.’jig rten gyi chos brgyad kyis mi ’gyur ba’am, yaṅ na chos rnams kyi raṅ bźin don dam pa skye ba daṅ ’jig pa daṅ bral ba rtogs par byed pa’i tshul bźin yaṅ mi ’gyur ba’i tshig ces bya’o.phyir bya ba ni gñen po’i chos kyis sbyaṅ źiṅ gtaṅ dgos pa ste, tshul bźin de ñid kun nas ñon moṅs pa’i chos gźan sbyoṅ ba’i gñen po yin te, de la gźan gaṅ gis kyaṅ sbyaṅ źiṅ gtaṅ mi dgos pas na phyir bya ba med pa’i tshig go. Dbh p. 7115.’jig rten pa’i lam daṅ, ’jig rten las ’das pa’i lam daṅ, de gñis ka’i goṅ ma theg pa chen po’i lam gyis spaṅs par bya ba’i skyon spaṅs pas źi ba daṅ rab tu źi ba daṅ ñe bar źi ba’i tshig go. mi mthun pa’i phyogs daṅ gñen po’i chos rnam pa sna tshogs su rtog pa’i spros pa med pas spros pa med pa’i tshig ste; ji ltar mi rtog ce na? ’degs pa med pa daṅ gźag pa med pa źes smos te, kun nas ñon moṅs pa’i chos glo bur ba bdegs śiṅ bsal du yaṅ med la, rnam par byaṅ ba’i chos sems kyi raṅ bźin ’od gsal ba gsar du bsnan ciṅ gźag tu yaṅ med par tshul bźin gyis rtogs pa’i phyir ro.phuṅ po lṅa daṅ, khams bco brgyad daṅ, skye mched bcu gñis la sogs pa ji sñed yod pa daṅ, de dag ñid kyaṅ mi rtag pa daṅ, sdug bsṅal ba la sogs pa ji lta ba bźin du yod pa ma lus pa daṅ, phyin ci ma log par tshul bźin gyis rtogs pas na ma tshaṅ ba med pa’i tshig go; bdag la sogs pa dṅos po med pa’i rnams yod par sgro btags nas śes pa’i yul du ’jal ba ni lhag pa ste, tshul bźin de ltar mi ’jal bas lhag pa med pa’o.... of saṃsāra? Cf. Śikṣ p. 354-5: kalyāṇamitrā .... niṣkāsayitāraḥ saṃsārapurāt. bsal źiṅ bsñigs pa ni phyir dbyuṅ ba ste, tshul bźin śes pa thams cad kyi sñiṅ po yin pas de ltar byar med pa’i phyir dbyuṅ du med pa’o.tshul bźin daṅ mi mthun pa mi rtag pa la rtag par ’dzin pa la sogs pa ni gñen po ste, de dag ’dis spaṅs pas na gñen po med pa’o.theg pa mchog gi lam du źugs pa’i tshul bźin gyis gaṅ zag daṅ chos la bdag med pa khoṅ du chud de, ñan thos daṅ raṅ saṅs rgyas la sogs pa mchog rnams las kyaṅ dam par gyur pas na dam pa’i tshig go.de kho na’i tshig ces bya ba ni bstan pa’o. lhag ma bźi ni bśad pa ste: rtag du de bźin du gnas śiṅ rnam par mi ’jig pas de bźin ñid daṅ ma nor ba daṅ phyin ci log tu gyur pa med pas ma nor ba de bźin ñid daṅ gźan du ’gyur ba med pas gźan ma yin pa’i de bźin ñid daṅ chos rnams kyi raṅ bźin yin pas ji lta ba bźin źes bya ste, chos rnams kyi yoṅs su grub pa’i mtshan ñid de lta bur śes par byed pa’i tshul bźin yid la byed pa la yaṅ de skad ces bya’o – "This is said in connection with thorough mental effort (yoniśomanasikāra) that knows the absolute character (pariniṣpannalakṣaṇa) of moments of existence."
ṭ. fol. 101a5: yaṅ na de kho na la sogs pa ni chos kyi dbyiṅs kyi rnam graṅs kyi tshig yin te – "Or, ’the real (tattva)’ and the following words are synonyms of total reality (dharmadhātuparyāyapada)".
To elucidate this a quotation from the Ratnameghasūtra on the topic then follows, ṭ. fol. 101a5-b4: de bas na dkon mchog sprin gyi mdo las byaṅ chub sems dpa’ sgrib pa thams cad rnam par sel bas gsol pa: bcom ldan ’das, de kho na źes bgyi ba ci lags? bcom ldan ’das kyis bka’ stsal pa: rigs kyi bu, ’di lta ste, de kho na źes bya ba ni yaṅ dag pa’i don gyi tshig bla dags so. gsol pa: bcom ldan ’das, yaṅ dag pa źes bgyi ba ci lags? bcom ldan ’das kyis bka’ stsal pa: gaṅ de bźin ñid daṅ ma nor ba de bźin ñid daṅ gźan ma yin pa de bźin ñid do. gsol pa: bcom ldan ’das, de bźin ñid źes bgyi ba ji lta bu lags? bcom ldan ’das kyis bka’ stsal pa: rigs kyi bu, chos ’di dag ni so so raṅ gis rig pa ste, de dag la yi ges gdags par mi nus so. ci’i phyir źe na? chos de dag ni yi ge thams cad las śin tu ’das pa, brjod pa thams cad las śin tu ’das pa, tshig gi spyod yul thams cad las śin tu ’das pa, tshig gi lam thams cad las śin tu ’das pa, spros pa thams cad daṅ bral ba, phye ba daṅ btsums pa thams cad daṅ rtog ge thams cad daṅ bral ba, rtog ge thams cad kyis brtag pa’i spyod yul ma yin pa, mtshan ma med pas mtshan ma’i spyod yul thams cad las yoṅs su ’das pa, byis pa’i spyod yul las śin tu ’das pa, bdud thams cad kyi spyod yul las śin tu ’das pa, ñon moṅs pa’i spyod yul thams cad las śin tu ’das pa, rnam par śes pa’i spyod yul las śin tu ’das pa, mi gnas pa, gnas ma yin pa, źi ba ’phags pa’i ye śes kyi spyod yul, de dag ñid kyis so sor raṅ gis rig par bya ba, dri ma med pa, daṅ ba, dag pa, gya nom pa rtag pa, brtan pa, rgyun du gnas pa, ’jig par mi ’gyur ba’i chos de, de bźin gśegs pa rnams byuṅ yaṅ ruṅ, ma byuṅ yaṅ ruṅ, chos kyi dbyiṅs ni gnas pa’o, źes gsuṅs pa’i phyir ro.byaṅ chub ṅes par thob pa ni chud mi za ba ste, tshul bźin gyis byaṅ chub thob par byed pas chud mi za ba’i tshig go.yaṅ dag pa ñid de kho na ñid phyin ci ma log pa’i mthar thug pas yaṅ dag pa’i mtha’i tshig go.sṅon gyi mtha’ daṅ, phyi ma’i mtha’ daṅ, da ltar byuṅ ba dus gsum bdag ñid thams cad du mi dmigs pas dus gsum yaṅ dag par rjes su mthoṅ ba ni dus gsum mñam pa’i tshig ces bya’o. de ji ltar mñam źe na? dus yoṅs su ma chad pa źes smos te, ’dus byas kyi chos kyi phuṅ po la sogs pa skye ba daṅ, gnas pa daṅ ’jig pa’i sgo nas dus gsum du gdags par zad kyi, yoṅs su grub pa’i mtshan ñid la ni de lta bu dbye ba med pa’i phyir ro – ".... since this kind of classification is not existent in what has the absolute character (pariniṣpannalakṣaṇa)".gzugs la rnam par śes pa mi gnas pa la sogs pas dus gsum gyi chos ’dus byas rnams la ma chags pa’am, de dag la miṅ daṅ mtshan ma’i bdag ñid du mṅon par źen pa med pa ni tshul bźin yin par ston te, ji ltar so so’i skye bo dag kun brtags pa’i gzugs la rnam par śes pas rnam pa sna tshogs su rtog ciṅ de’i bdag ñid du mṅon par źen pa de ltar mi byed pas gzugs la rnam par śes pa mi gnas pa źes bya ste, tshor ba la sogs pa lhag ma rnams la yaṅ de daṅ ’dra bar bśad do.de ni don la rton pa’i tshig ces bya ba la sogs pas tshul bźin de tshig ’bru daṅ, gaṅ zag daṅ, rnam par śes pa daṅ, bkri ba’i don gyi mdo sde la mi rton gyi, so sor rton pa bźi la brten ces bya ba’i tha tshig go.


d) btsun pa śa ra dva ti’i bu, gźan yaṅ tshul bźin źes bya ba ni chos thams cad do.

punar aparaṃ, bhadanta śāradavatīputra, yonir iti sarvadharmāḥ.

d) Further, reverend Śāradvatīputra, “thorough” is [concerned with] all moments of existence.


de ci’i phyir źe na?

tat kasya hetoḥ?

[To teach the causes of insight (prajñāhetu), and the fruit which is insight (prajñāphala), it is said:] Why?

See ṭ. fol. 88b4, b5: śes rab kyi rgyu, and cf. ṭ. fol. 103a4-7, infra. rnam pa gcig tu na tshul bźin źes bya ba de ni rigs pa’i tshig go źes bya ba la ṅes pa’i tshig smos pa thams cad tshul bźin yid la byed pa daṅ mi sbyar bar chos rnams kyi de bźin ñid yoṅs su grub pa’i ṅes pa’i tshig gi rnam graṅs yin par sbyar źiṅ bśad de, de bas na mjug thogs su tshul bźin źes bya ba ni chos thams cad do źes gsuṅs pa’i phyir te; gaṅ zag la bdag med pa daṅ chos la bdag med pa ni tshul bźin źes bya ba ste, de chos thams cad la ma khyab pa med pa’i phyir tshul bźin źes bya ba ni chos thams cad do źes bśad do. ’bras bu bstan pa’i dbaṅ du byas nas: ci’i phyir źes bya ba la sogs pa gsuṅs te, ci’i phyir źes bya ba ni chos thams cad la ci’i phyir tshul bźin źes bya ba’i gtan tshigs ’dri ba’o – "And further, the etymology (nirukti) saying: ’Thorough is a word for reasoning’ (in the preceding paragraph: yonir iti yuktipadam etat) does not apply for thorough mental effort (yoniśomanasikāra) concerned with everything, so then one goes on referring to the etymology concerned with things as they really are, to the perfected state of things (tathatāpariniṣpannanirukti). Thus follows ’Thorough is [concerned with] all moments of existence’: The fact of selflessness of the person (pudgalanairātmya) and selflessness of all things (dharmanairātmya) is thorough [or fundamental], and because this fact applies for all moments of existence (sarvadharmāvyāpyabhāvatvāt), it is said ’Thorough is [concerned with] all moments of existence’. To demonstrate the fruit (phala) of this it is said ’Why’ etc." Cf. ṭ. fol. 88b1-2.
The "etymology" is made in treating yoniśas and yuktitas as the same word; cf. the two preceding paragraphs b) and c), especially notes in the beginning of these paragraphs.


ji ltar bdag la bdag med pa, de bźin du chos thams cad rigs pas mthoṅ źiṅ;ji ltar sems can la bdag med pa, de bźin du chos thams cad rigs pas mthoṅ na,de ltar mthoṅ ba ni tshul bźin mthoṅ ba’o.

yathātmanairātmyaṃ tathā sarvadharmān yuktitaḥ paśyet,yathā sattvanairātmyaṃ tathā sarvadharmān yuktitaḥ paśyet.evaṃdarśanaṃ yoniśodarśanam.

As one looks upon selflessness in oneself [that is, in one’s own parts of personality (svôpādānaskandha) ], one should look upon all moments of existence in accordance with reason,as one looks upon selflessness in living beings one should look upon all moments of existence in accordance with reason.Seeing that way is the thorough way of seeing.

ji ltar bdag la bdag med pa, de bźin du źes bya ba la sogs pas ni tshul bźin mthoṅ ba daṅ sbyor ba bstan pa’i sgo nas chos thams cad la tshul bźin źes bya ba ston te, bdag ces bya ba ni raṅ gi ñe bar len pa’i phuṅ po ste, de la gaṅ zag daṅ chos kyi raṅ bźin bdag med pa bźin du phuṅ po daṅ khams daṅ skye mched la sogs pa chos thams cad kyaṅ tshad ma gsum mam, śes rab rnam pa gsum gyi rigs pas mthoṅ ba’am, ji ltar sems can la bdag med pa bźin du phuṅ po daṅ khams daṅ skye mched la sogs pa chos thams cad kyaṅ bdag med par mthoṅ na tshul bźin mthoṅ ba źes bya bas chos thams cad tshul bźin źes bya bar grub bo.


’khor ba’i khams kyi tshul bźin gaṅ yin pa, mya ṅan las ’das pa’i dbyiṅs kyi tshul bźin yaṅ de yin no, źes gaṅ gis de ltar mtshuṅs śiṅ bye brag med par mthoṅ ba, de ni tshul bźin rab tu sbyor ba źes bya’o;gaṅ gis kun nas ñon moṅs pa’i raṅ bźin daṅ rnam par byaṅ ba’i raṅ bźin mtshuṅs śiṅ bye brag med par mthoṅ ba, de ni tshul bźin rab tu sbyor ba źes bya’o;gaṅ rigs pa daṅ mi rigs par mi sems pa, de ni tshul bźin rab tu sbyor ba yin te;

yā saṃsāradhātor yoniḥ sā nirvāṇadhātor api yonir iti ya evaṃ samanirviśeṣataḥ paśyati sa ucyate yoniśaḥprayogaḥ;yaḥ saṃkleśasvabhāvaṃ vyavadānasvabhāvaṃ samanirviśeṣataḥ paśyati sa ucyate yoniśaḥprayogaḥ;yo na yuktyayuktitaś cintayati sa ucyate yoniśaḥprayogaḥ.

“That which is thorough [namely the nature (prakṛti) ] of the sphere of existence is also what is thorough [namely the nature (prakṛti) ] of the sphere of extinction”, as one sees in this way according to sameness and no distinction it is called thorough practice;as one sees the essence of impurity and the essence of purity in this way according to sameness and no distinction it is called thorough practice;as one does not see things in the way of reason and non-reason it is thorough practice.

’khor ba’i khams kyi tshul bźin ni ’khor ba’i raṅ bźin te, ji ltar mya ṅan las ’das pa’i dbyiṅs kyi tshul bźin yoṅs su dag pa bźin ’khor ba’i raṅ bźin yaṅ yoṅs su dag par mthoṅ na źes bya ba’i tha tshig go. Cf. Kpv 52: yoniśodharmaprayogaḥ, and Rāṣṭrapālaparipṛcchā p. 129: āśayena śrutvā dhīra yoniśaḥ prayujyate/.kun nas ñon moṅs pa’i raṅ bźin ni ’dod chags la sogs pa ste, lus daṅ sems la gnod pa sna tshogs skyed par byed pa’i phyir ro, rnam par byaṅ ba ni byaṅ chub kyi phyogs daṅ, pha rol du phyin pa ste, ñon moṅs pa rnams ’joms pa’i gñen po yin pa’i phyir ro, mi mthun pa’i phyogs daṅ gñen po de gñi ga yaṅ brjod du med pa’i raṅ bźin du mtshuṅs śiṅ mi mthun pa’i phyogs daṅ gñen po źes brjod pa ltar don dam par bye brag med par mthoṅ ba, de ni tshul bźin rab tu sbyor ba źes bya’o.de ltar gñi ga yaṅ brjod du med par ’dra bas rnam par byaṅ ba’i chos la yon tan can du rigs par yaṅ mi sems, kun nas ñon moṅs pa’i chos la skyon can du mi rigs par yaṅ mi sems pa, de ni tshul bźin rab tu sbyor ba źes bya’o.


btsun pa śa ra dva ti’i bu, mdor na, byaṅ chub sems dpa’i tshul bźin sbyor ba ji sñed pa, de dag thams cad kyi gnas ni sems can no.de sems can gyi gnas kyaṅ mi spoṅ la chos kyi gnas kyaṅ ’khrugs par mi byed de.de ni byaṅ chub sems dpa’i tshul bźin la ’jug pa’i sbyor ba źes bya’o.

saṃkṣepato, bhadanta śāradvatīputra, yāvanto bodhisattvānāṃ yoniśoyogās teṣāṃ sarveṣāṃ sthitis tu sattvāḥ.sa na sattvasthitiṃ tyajati nāpi dharmasthitiṃ vikopayati.sa ucyate bodhisattvānāṃ yoniśaḥpraveśayogaḥ.

In short, reverend Śāradvatīputra, the place [or object] of all thorough efforts of the bodhisattvas is living beings.He should not give up [being born in] the places of living beings, nor [think that he by that will] disturb the place [or state] of the [totality of] moments of existence [even though making living beings the object of his great compasssion].That is called the bodhisattvas’ effort of thorough entrance.

btsun pa śa ra dva ti’i bu, mdor na źes bya ba la sogs pas ni byaṅ chub sems dpa’ de ltar tshul bźin sbyor ba de dag thams cad gaṅ la dmigs śiṅ gaṅ la brten nas sbyor ba’i gnas ston te, tshul bźin sbyor ba ji sñed pa źes bya ba ni tshul bźin gyi ’jug pa graṅs ji sñed yod pa’am, ji sñed byed pa źes bya ba’i don to. de dag thams cad kyi gnas ni sems can no źes bya ba ni tshul bźin de dag gi rten daṅ dmigs par bya ba’i yul sems can yin te, ’di ltar byaṅ chub sems dpa’ sems can la thugs brtse bas de dag yoṅs su gzuṅ ba’i phyir tshul bźin yid la byed pa de dag la sbyor ba mdzad pa’am, yaṅ na ji ltar sems can la bdag med pa de bźin du chos thams cad rigs pas mthoṅ źes bya ba la sogs pa’i tshul gyis sems can gyi yul la tshul bźin gyi sbyor ba mdzad do źes bya ba’i tha tshig go. de ltar thugs rje chen po’i dbaṅ gis sems can la dmigs nas dmigs pa daṅ bcas pas: chos kyi dbyiṅs dkrugs par mi ’gyur ram? sñam pa la de sems can gyi gnas kyaṅ mi spoṅ la chos kyi gnas kyaṅ ’khrugs par mi byed do źes gsuṅs te, byaṅ chub sems dpa’ de sems can gyi gnas ’khor bar skye ba yaṅ mi gtoṅ la, chos kyi gnas stobs daṅ mi ’jigs pa la sogs pa yon tan gyi chos rnams kyi ’byuṅ gnas kyi chos kyi dbyiṅs rnam par dag pa daṅ rnam par mi rtog pa’i ye śes ’khrugs par mi byed de, sems can kyi don du ’khor bar gnas kyaṅ de gñis las ñams par mi ’gyur źes bya ba’i tha tshig go.
Cf. also Aṣṭādaśa (71), p. 824ff: tad bodhisattvo mahāsattva prakṛtiśūnyatāpāramitāsu caran rūpaṃ na vikopayati. śūnyaṃ vā nāśūnyam iti. ... na rūpaṃ śūnyatāṃ vikopayati ... na śūnyatā bodhiṃ vikopayati. tat kasya hetoḥ? na hy eṣāṃ svabhāvo ’sti ya evaṃ vikopayed.


btsun pa śa ra dva ti’i bu, de ltar de’i chos kyi rnam pa daṅ, thos pa’i rnam pa daṅ, tshul bźin la ’jug pa’i sbyor ba rgyu ’thun pa, de ni śes rab ces bya’o.

evaṃ, bhadanta śāradvatīputra, tasya dharmākāraśrutākārayoniśaḥpraveśaniṣyandaḥ socyate prajñā.

[Then, to summarize the above-mentioned form of insight (prajñâkāra), etc., to demonstrate that the fruit of the above-mentioned moments of existence is insight, it is said:] Thus, reverend Śāradvatīputra, the outcome for him [the bodhisattva trained in the above-mentioned imperishabilities] of those forms of religion, forms of learning and efforts of thorough entrance is called insight.

śes rab kyi rnam pa la sogs pa goṅ du bśad pa rnams bsdus te bstan pa daṅ, goṅ du bśad pa’i chos rnams kyi ’bras bu śes rab yin par bstan pa’i phyir btsun pa śa ra dva ti’i bu, de ltar de’i chos kyi rnam pa daṅ, thos pa’i rnam pa daṅ, tshul bźin la ’jug pa’i sbyor ba rgyu mthun pa, de ni śes rab ces bya’o źes smras te; de’i źes bya ba ni sems bskyed pa daṅ bsam pa mi zad pa la sogs pa nas śes rab mi zad pa’i bar la gnas pa’i byaṅ chub sems dpa’ ’di’i źes bya ba’i don to; chos kyi rnam pa ni phuṅ po daṅ khams daṅ skye mched la sogs pa’o, yaṅ na, chos kyi rnam pa ni sems bskyed pa daṅ, bsam pa daṅ, sbyor ba daṅ, lhag pa’i bsam pa daṅ, sbyin pa daṅ, tshul khrims daṅ, bzod pa daṅ, brtson ’grus daṅ, bsam gtan la sogs pa goṅ du bśad pa’i chos rnams so; thos pa’i rnam pa ni goṅ du thos pa’i rnam pa brgyad cu rtsa bźi smos pa’o; tshul bźin la ’jug pa’i sbyor ba ni goṅ du tshul bźin la ’jug pa sum cu rtsa gñis smos pa’o; chos de rnams ñid rgyu bas na chos kyi rnam pa daṅ, thos pa’i rnam pa daṅ, tshul bźin la ’jug pa’i sbyor ba’i rgyu źes bya ste, rgyu de daṅ mthun pa’i ’bras bu ni rgyu mthun pa ste, dṅos su śes rab mi zad pa’o; don du na rgyu mthun pa źes bya ba ni rgyu ci ’dra bar mthun par ’gyur ba’i ’bras bu la bya ste, chos kyi rnam pa daṅ, thos pa’i rnam pa daṅ, tshul bźin la ’jug pa’i sbyor ba’i rgyu de dag las ’bras bu śes rab mi zad pa ’byuṅ bar ’os kyi, gźan ni ma yin pa’i phyir ro.


e) de la śes rab ni ’grogs pa bcu drug daṅ lhan cig mi gnas te.bcu drug po dag gaṅ źe na?

tatra prajñā na ṣoḍaśadharmaiḥ sārdhaṃ saṃvasati.katame ṣoḍaśa?

(p. 66)e) [The essence of insight (prajñāsvabhāva), the fact that insight is not polluted by the contraries of insight (prajñāvipakṣa):]Insight, then, does not stay with these sixteen things.What sixteen?

śes rab kyi raṅ bźin bstan pa’i dbaṅ du byas nas de la śes rab ni ’grogs pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas te źes bya ba la sogs pas gsuṅs so. Cf. 88b4, b5-6: śes rab de śes rab kyi mi mthun pa’i phyogs daṅ ma ’dres pa.’grogs pa bcu drug daṅ lhan cig mi gnas źes bya bas ni śes rab kyaṅ skabs ’dir rnam par mi rtog pa’i ye śes dmigs pa daṅ, spros pa thams cad las ’das pa, mtshan ma thams cad ma ’dres pa’i raṅ bźin la bya bar ’dod de, de bas na dmigs pa daṅ, mtshan ma’i skyon rnams daṅ ma ’dres pa’i phyir ’grogs pa bcu drug daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so źes bśad do.
The expression ’grogs pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas is somewhat problematic, and the Tibetan text is possibly corrupt. Dbh p. 5226-27: na ca saṃskṛtasaṃvāsena saṃvasati, and Aṣṭa p. 79326.: na ca tena vānyena vā nimittena sārdhaṃ saṃvasati (cf. also Aṣṭādaśa (55) p. 211-2; Suvkr p. 524-7; Aṣṭa p. 76020) seem to be expressions very close to Akṣ, but both ’grogs pa ~ saṃvāsa and lhan cig ~ sārdham cannot be in the same sentence. Thus it seems that either the expression from Dbh or the one from Aṣṭa has to be chosen. From item no. 8 the ’grogs pa has been left out, and suggests the Aṣṭa variant of the expression, while in the case of no. 1 to no. 7 the Dbh variant is the basis for the reconstruction. There are no variants in the available Tibetan material. The §£¶Ì of T1 (p. 196b19ff) and the §£ªP(¶X)¶P, with variants, of T2 (p. 5964ff) also give no clue to the original Sanskrit. The introduction is based on T1 p. 196b19,: ṃ–¬ƒºz™Ã¶≥§Q§ª™k§£©Û§§¶Ì which seems to have read dharma, the probability of this reconstruction being strengthened by T2 (p. 5964) which has ṛ∆ for ™k, also a common equivalent for dharma: ¶≥§Q§ªṛ∆§£ªPºz¶X.


’di lta ste: ma rig pa’i ’grogs pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so, de bźin du ’du byed daṅ, rnam par śes pa daṅ, miṅ daṅ gzugs daṅ, skye mched drug daṅ, reg pa daṅ, tshor ba daṅ, sred pa daṅ, len pa daṅ, srid pa daṅ, skye ba daṅ, rga śi’i ’grogs pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so;

tad yathā nāvidyāsaṃvāsena saṃvasati, evaṃ na saṃskāravijñānanāmarūpaṣaḍāyatanasparśavedanātṛṣṇopādānabhāvajātijarāmaraṇasaṃvāsena saṃvasati.

1) It does not stay in the company of ignorance, nor does it stay in the company of formative factors, consciousness, name and form, the six fields of sense-perception, touch, feeling, thirst, grasping, existence, birth, old age and death.

de la ma rig pa’i ’grogs pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so źes bya ba la sogs pas ’khor ba’i rgyu srid pa’i yan lag bcu gñis rnams daṅ lhan cig mi gnas par bstan te: de la ma rig pa ni yaṅ dag pa’i mtha’ khoṅ du ma chud pa’o; ma rig pa de ñid ’grogs pa yin pas na ma rig pa’i ’grogs pa ste, ma rig pa’i dbaṅ du gyur pa’am, ma rig pa daṅ ’dres par gyur pa’o. mi gnas so źes bya ba ni de daṅ ma ’dres pa’am, ma ’bags pa źes bya ba’i don to. gal te rnam par mi rtog pa’i ye śes de ma rig pa daṅ ’dres na ni gźan gyi dbaṅ gi mtshan ñid bźin du ’khor bar lhuṅ ba’i skyon du ’gyur ro. de bźin du źes bya ba ni de daṅ ’dra ba źes bya ba’i don to. ’du byed rnams daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so źes bya ba nas yan lag lhag ma rnams la yaṅ de daṅ ’dra bar sbyar ro. de la ’du byed ni rnam pa gsum ste, bsod nams ma yin par ñe bar ’gro ba’i ’du byed daṅ, bsod nams su ñe bar ’gro ba’i ’du byed daṅ, mi g-yo bar ñe bar ’gro ba’i ’du byed do. rnam par śes pa ni sa bon thams cad kyi rten rnam par smin pa’i raṅ bźin kun gźi rnam par śes pa’o. miṅ ni tshor ba daṅ ’du śes daṅ ’du byed daṅ rnam par śes pa rnams so. gzugs ni bstan du yod la thogs pa daṅ bcas pa’am, bstan du med la thogs pa daṅ bcas pa daṅ, bstan du yaṅ med la thogs pa yaṅ med pa ste, de gñis gcig tu bsdus na miṅ daṅ gzugs źes bya’o. skye mched drug ni mig gi skye mched nas yid kyi skye mched kyi bar du’o. reg pa ni yul daṅ dbaṅ po daṅ rnam par śes pa rnams rgyu daṅ ’bras bu’i mtshan ñīd du dus mñam du tshogs pa’o. tshor ba ni bde ba daṅ sdug bsṅal ba daṅ bde ba yaṅ ma yin sdug bsṅal ba yaṅ ma yin pa’i tshor ba rnams so. sred pa ni yul daṅ loṅs spyod la rgyun du spyod kyaṅ tshva chu ’thuṅ ba daṅ ’dra bar ṅoms pa daṅ tshim pa med pa’o. len pa ni ’dod pa len pa daṅ, tshul khrims daṅ brtul źugs len pa daṅ, lta ba len pa daṅ, bdag tu smra ba len pa daṅ. srid pa ni ’dod pa’i srid pa daṅ, gzugs kyi srid pa daṅ, gzugs med pa’i srid pa’o. skye ba ni las kyi bag chags rnam pa sna tshogs bags pa’i khyad par las ñiṅ mtshams sbyor ba de daṅ de dag tu phuṅ po daṅ khams daṅ skye mched la sogs pa mṅon par grub pa’o. rga ba ni mer mer po daṅ, nur nur po daṅ, mkhraṅ gyur pa daṅ, rkaṅ lag ’gyus pa nas gźon nu daṅ laṅ tsho daṅ dar la bab pa’i stobs daṅ mthu daṅ gzi brjid daṅ mdaṅs la sogs pa rab tu gźan du gyur te ñams pa’o. śi ba ni tshe daṅ drod daṅ rnam par śes pa med par gyur pa’o.


ma rig pa ’gog pa’i ’grogs pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so, de bźin du ’du byed daṅ, rnam par śes pa daṅ, miṅ daṅ gzugs daṅ, skye mched drug daṅ, reg pa daṅ, tshor ba daṅ, sred pa daṅ, len pa daṅ, srid pa daṅ, skye ba daṅ, rga śi ’gog pa’i ’grogs pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so;

na cāvidyānirodhasaṃvāsena saṃvasati, evaṃ na saṃskāravijñānanāmarūpaṣaḍāyatanasparśavedanātṛṣṇopādānabhāvajātijarāmaraṇanirodhasaṃvāsena saṃvasati.

2) It does not stay in the company of cessation of ignorance, nor does it stay in the company of cessation of formative factors, consciousness, name and form, the six fields of sense-perception, touch, feeling, thirst, grasping, existence, birth, old age and death.

ma rig pa ’gog pa’i ’grogs pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so źes bya ba la sogs pas ma rig pa ’gags pa la sogs pa ’khor ba las ldog pa’i rgyu rnam par byaṅ ba’i chos rnams daṅ yaṅ ma ’dres pa bstan te, ma rig pa ’gags pa ni ma rig pa spaṅ ba’am, ma rig pa med par gyur nas de daṅ mi mthun pa’i rig pa skyes pa la bya’o.


’jig tshogs la lta ba’i ’grogs pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa nas ’jig tshogs la lta ba’i rtsa ba las byuṅ bar lta bar gyur pa drug cu rtsa gñis po’i bar dag gi ’grogs pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so;

na ca satkāyadṛṣṭisaṃvāsena saṃvasati, yāvan na satkāyadṛṣṭimūlotpannadvāṣaṣṭidṛṣṭigatasaṃvāsena saṃvasati.

3) It does not stay in the company of the view that a true substance [a self] is found [which is the root of all views], nor does it stay in the company of the sixty-two view-points which originate from the root view that a true substance is found.

’jig tshogs la lta ba’i ’grogs pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa źes bya ba la sogs pas log pa’i lta ba rnams daṅ ma ’dres pa bstan te, de la ’jig tshogs źes bya ba ni gzugs la sogs pa phuṅ po lṅa ’jig pa’i raṅ bźin can rnams phuṅ po daṅ tshogs su gyur pa la bya ste, de la bdag yod par lta ba ni ’jig tshogs la lta ba’o. ’jig tshogs la lta ba de ñid rtsa ba yin pas na ’jig tshogs la lta ba’i rtsa ba ste, lta bar gyur pa thams cad kyi rgyu yin pa’i phyir ro – tatrātmadṛṣṭiḥ satkāyadṛṣṭiḥ, saiva satkāyadṛṣṭir mūlam iti satkāyadṛṣṭimūlam, sarvadṛṣṭigatahetutvāt.
lta ba de’i rtsa ba las byuṅ ba ni lta bar gyur pa drug cu rtsa gñis po’i bar dag ste, lta bar gyur pa drug cu rtsa gñis ni rtag par lta ba daṅ, mtha’ daṅ mtha’ med par smra ba la sogs pa tshaṅs pa’i dra ba daṅ lṅa gsum pa la sogs pa las gsuṅs pa bźin du rig par bya’o. bar dag ces smos pas ni bdag tu lta ba’i ri’i rtse mo ñi śu po gzugs la bdag tu lta ba daṅ, bdag gzugs daṅ ldan pa daṅ, gzugs bdag gi yin pa daṅ, gzugs la bdag gnas par lta ba daṅ, de bźin du tshor ba la sogs pa phuṅ po lhag ma bźi la yaṅ mthun mthun du sbyar te, de dag la sogs pa lta bur gyur pa thams cad daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa źes bya ba’i tha tshig go.
Cf. Mvy 4684-4704: viṃśatiśikharasamudgataḥ satkāyadṛṣṭiśailaḥ ...; Brahmajālasūtra; lṅa gsum pa?; Aṣṭādaśa (57) p. 4426: satkāyadṛṣṭau dvāṣaṣṭidṛṣṭigatāny antargatāni bhavanti.


mthon dman gyi ’grogs pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa nas ’jig rten gyi chos rñed pa daṅ ma rñed pa daṅ, sñan pa daṅ mi sñan pa daṅ, smad pa daṅ bstod pa daṅ, bde ba daṅ sdug bsṅal gyi bar gyi ’grogs pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so;

na ca natonnatasaṃvāsena saṃvasati, yāvan na lābhālābhayaśo’yaśonindāpraśaṃsāsukhaduḥkhalokadharmasaṃvāsena saṃvasati.

4) It does not stay in the company of [thinking in categories of] high and low [the result (phala) of the ways of the world mentioned in the following], nor does it stay in the company of the ways of the world, gain and loss, fame and absence of fame, disgrace and praise, pleasure and pain [being the cause (hetu) ].

mthon dman ni ’bras bu yin la, ’jig rten gyi chos ni rgyu yin te, ’di ltar rñed pa la sogs pas ni mtho bar sems pa ’byuṅ la, ma rñed pa la sogs pa las mi dma’ bar sems pa ’byuṅ ba’i phyir te, ’jig rten gyi chos brgyad po de dag gis sems kheṅs pa daṅ źum par mi ’gyur bas na mthon dman gyi ’grogs pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa nas ’jig rten gyi chos brgyad kyi bar gyi ’grogs pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas źes gsuṅs so. de la rñed pa daṅ ma rñed pa ni chos gos daṅ lhuṅ bzed la sogs pa’o, sñan pa daṅ mi sñan pa ni yon tan daṅ skyon rnams so, smad pa daṅ bstod pa ni skyon smos pa daṅ yon tan tshigs su bcad pas brjod pa’o, bde ba daṅ sdug bsṅal ni lus daṅ sems la phan ’dogs pa daṅ gnod pa bskyed pa’o.


khro ba daṅ, khon du ’dzin pa daṅ, ’chab pa daṅ, yoṅs su gduṅ ba daṅ, phrag dog daṅ, ser sna daṅ, sgyu daṅ, g-yo daṅ, ṅo tsha med pa daṅ, khrel med pa daṅ, kheṅs pa daṅ, rtsod pa daṅ, rgyags pa daṅ, bag med pa daṅ, ṅa rgyal daṅ, lhag pa’i ṅa rgyal daṅ, ṅa rgyal las kyaṅ ṅa rgyal daṅ, ṅa’o sñam pa’i ṅa rgyal daṅ, chuṅ zad sñam pa’i ṅa rgyal daṅ, mṅon pa’i ṅa rgyal daṅ, log pa’i ṅa rgyal rnams kyi ’grogs pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa nas ñe ba’i ñon moṅs pa thams cad kyi bar gyi ’grogs pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so;

na ca krodhopanāhamrakṣaparidāherṣyāmātsaryamāyāśāṭhyāhrīkyānapatrāpyonnativivādamadapramādamānātimānamānātimānāsmimānonamānābhimānamithyāmānasaṃvāsena saṃvasati, yāvan na sarvopakleśasaṃvāsena saṃvasati.

5) It does not stay in the company of anger, subsequent annoyance, concealing [wrongdoings though reprehended with good will], vexation, grudging [because of others’ good qualities], enviously wishing [something without yielding anything], deception, guile, shamelessness, indecency, swagger, quarreling, infatuation, intoxication [with vices], conceit, pride, arrogance, self-conceit, pride of modesty, conceitedness and pride of being wrong [about one’s own qualities], as it does not stay in the company of any of the mental impurities.

The different mental impurities (upakleśa) are explained in detail: khro ba daṅ khon du ’dzin źes bya ba nas ñe ba’i ñon moṅs pa thams cad kyi bar gyi ’grogs pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas źes bya ba ñe ba’i ñon moṅs pa daṅ ma ’dres par bstan te: ṅa rgyal yaṅ sems ñe bar ñon moṅs par byed pa’i sgo nas ñe ba’i ñon moṅs pa źes gdags so; cf. Kośa p. 3121-5: tatra ye yāvat kleśā upakleśā api te, cittopakleśanāt.
The following are abbreviated quotations from Pañcaskandhaprakaraṇavaibhāṣya fol. 222a4ff and/or Triṃśikābhāṣya p. 303ff, on the basis of which the present reconstructions of the ṭ text are made, but cf. the introduction. Abhidharmasamuccaya p. 813ff, tib. 50b2ff treats the same concepts, but does not have the same text.
de la khro ba ni ’phral du gnod par byed pa la gnas te, sems kyi kun nas mnar sems pa’o – tatra krodho vartamānam apakāram āgamya cetasa āghātaḥ. [For the equivalents āgam- and gnas cf. Dbh index s.v.]. Triṃśikābhāṣya p. 303, tib. fol. 159a4-5; Pañcaskandhaprakaraṇa fol. 14a4, Dantinne p. 139; cf. Pañcaskandhaprakaraṇavaibhāṣya fol. 222a4.
khon du ’dzin pa ni khros pa’i ’og tu ’dis bdag la gnod pa ’di byas so źes śar gñer ba’i mdud par ’dzin pa mi gtoṅ ba’o – upanāhaḥ krodhād ūrdhvaṃ mamānenedam apakṛtam iti vairānubandhasyānutsargaḥ. Triṃś p. 306-8, tib. fol. 159a6-b1 = Pskvai fol. 222b1-2.
’chab pa ni ’dun pa daṅ źe sdaṅ daṅ ’jigs pa la sogs pa bsal te, phan par ’dod pa’i gleṅ ba pos: khyod ’di lta bu byed pa’o, źes bsñad pa na kha na ma tho ba mkhyud pa’o – mrakṣaś chandadveṣabhayādīn nirākṛtya taddhitaiṣiṇā codakena tat tvam evaṃkārīty anuyuktasyāvadyapracchādanā. Triṃś p. 3010-12, tib. fol. 159b1-3 = Pskvai fol. 222b2-4.
yoṅs su gduṅ ba ni tshig brlaṅ pos gźan gyi sems gduṅ bar bskyed pa’o – paridāhaś caṇḍena vacasā parapradāśitā. Triṃś p. 3015ff, tib. fol. 159b3ff = Pskvai fol. 222b3ff. The words paridāha (ṭ) and pradāsa (-śa) are given the same meaning, cf. Edg s. v. pradāsa; Triṃś and Pskvai have tshig brlaṅ po.
phrag dog ni pha rol po’i rñed pa daṅ, bkur sti daṅ, rigs daṅ, tshul khrims daṅ, thos pa la sogs pa’i yon tan mthoṅ nas źe sdaṅ gi char gtogs pa’i sems khoṅ nas ’khrug pa’o – īrṣyā lābhasatkārakulaśīlaśrutādīn guṇān parasyopalabhya dveṣāṃśiko cetaso vyāroṣaḥ. Triṃś p. 3020ff, tib. fol. 159b6ff ~ Pskvai fol. 222b7f.
ser sna ni rñed pa daṅ bkur sti la źen nas ’dod chags kyi sems kyis phyi daṅ naṅ gi dṅos po mi gtoṅ ba’o – mātsaryaṃ lābhasatkārādhyavasitasya rāgacetasā bāhyādhyātmavastvaparityāgaḥ. Triṃś p. 3024ff, tib. fol. 160a1ff = Pskvai fol. 223a1ff.
sgyu ni rñed pa daṅ bkur sti la lhag par chags pas gźan la bslu ba’i bsama pas tshul khrims la sogs pa’i don gźan du gnas la gźan du ston pa’o – māyā lābhasatkārādhyavasitasya paravañcanābhiprāyeṇānyavasthitasya śīlāder arthasyānyathā prakāśanā. Triṃś p. 3029ff, tib. fol. 160a3ff = Pskvai fol. 223a3ff.
g-yo ni bdag gi ñes pa bcab pa’i thabs bzuṅ ste, gźan nas gźan du sgyur źiṅ gtam rluṅ la bskur pa daṅ, gsal bar mi byed pa’o – śāṭhyaṃ svadoṣapracchādanopāyasaṃgṛhītaṃ, anyenānyat pratisaran vikṣipati, aparisphuṭaṃ vā pratipadyate. Triṃś p. 313ff, tib. fol. 160a3ff = Pskvai fol. 223a5ff.
ṅo tsha med pa ni las de bdag gi cha ma yin par śes kyaṅ kha na ma tho bas mi ’dzems pa’o – āhrīkyaṃ tasmin karmaṇy ātmānam ayogyaṃ manyamānasyāpy avadyenālajjā. Triṃś p. 3117f, tib. fol. 160b5f = Pskvai fol. 224a1ff.
khrel med pa ni gźan la kha na ma tho bas mi ’dzems pa’o – anapatrāpyaṃ parato ’vadyenālajjā. Triṃś p. 3118f, tib. fol. 160b6f treated also in Pskvai fol. 224a2, but in even shorter form, just noting it is the opposite of the former upakleśa. The section on upakleśa ends after this item in both Triṃś and Pskvai.
ṭ fol. 105a5-b6:
kheṅs pa ni ’dod chags śas che ba’i dbaṅ gis lus kyi ’gyur ba rkaṅ lag brkyaṅ ba daṅ, mgo ’phaṅ bstod pa daṅ, smin ma bsdus pa daṅ, so gtsigs pa la sogs pa ’gyiṅ bar snaṅ ba ste, mkhan po daṅ slob dpon daṅ bla ma la sogs pa la thal mo sbyar ba daṅ, ’dud pa la sogs pa’i las mi byed pa’o – unnati, not identified as quotation.
rtsod pa ni de dag gi rgyu las lus daṅ ṅag gi las rdeg pa daṅ, ’chiṅ ba daṅ, skyon smos pa daṅ, mtshaṅ ’dru ba la sogs pa byed pa’o – vivāda, not identified as quotation.
rgyags pa ni bdag gi rigs daṅ, nad med pa daṅ, gzugs daṅ laṅ tsho la sogs pa raṅ gi phun sum tshogs pa la dga’ ba’i bye brag daṅ ldan pa’i sred pas sems raṅ dbaṅ med par byed pa’o – madaḥ svakulārogyarūpayauvanasvasaṃpattiharṣaviśeṣā tṛṣṇā cittam asvatantrīkriyate. Triṃś p. 319ff, tib. fol. 160b1ff ~ Pskvai fol. 224a1-4. This paragraph is quoted from Pskvai, as this work includes a short sentence on sred pa (fol. 224a4: dga’ ba’i bye brag daṅ ldan pa’i sred pa’i rnam pa), which Triṃś does not have.
bag med pa ni ’dod chags daṅ źe sdaṅ daṅ gti mug gi dbaṅ gis dge ba mi sgom źiṅ mi dge ba byed pa’o – pramādo lobhadveṣamohavaśāt kuśalaṃ na bhāvayaty akuśalaṃ karoti; similar to Psk fol. 14b2 (Dantinne p. 140 §17) but quotes, rather, and abbreviates Triṃśikābhāṣya p. 323-5. Triṃś 324-5 ~ Pskvai fol. 224b1-2, but this piece is not in ṭ.
The following passages on the seven kinds of conceit are quoted with minor differences from Triṃśikābhāṣya p. 2828ff; the text given is the reconstruction of the text in ṭ. sapta mānāḥ are treated otherwise in Kośa p. 28423ff; Abhidharmasamuccaya rec. p. 457-13, tib. fol. 79b4-80a1, tr. p. 72 = Pañcaskandhaprakaraṇa fol. 13a7-b4 (Dantinne p. 137); Ybh p. 505-6;
Mvy 1946-1952.
ṅa rgyal ni rigs daṅ śes rgya daṅ nor la sogs pas dma’ ba bas de dag gis bdag che’o sñam du sems kheṅs pa’am, rigs la sogs pa mtshuṅs pa ñid la de dag daṅ bdag mtshuṅs so sñam du sems kheṅs pa’o – hīnāt kulavijñānavittādibhiḥ śreyān āsmi tair iti cittasyonnatir, sadṛśena vā kulādibhir eva sadṛśo ’smīti cittasyonnatir mānaḥ. From Triṃś p. 294-6, tib. fol. 158a5-6 = Pskvai fol. 217a7-b2.
lhag pa’i ṅa rgyal ni rigs daṅ śes rgya la sogs pas mtshuṅs pa bas gtoṅ ba daṅ tshul khrims daṅ ñams rtsal la sogs pas bdag che’o sñam pa’am, rigs daṅ nor la sogs pas che ba la bdag daṅ mtshuṅs so sñam du sems kheṅs pa’o – kulavijñānādibhiḥ sadṛśāt tyāgaśīlapauruṣādibhir śreyān asmi, śreyasā vā kulavittādibhir sadṛśo ’smīti cittasyonnatir atimānaḥ. From Triṃś p. 296-8, tib. fol. 158a6-7 = Pskvai fol. 217b1-2.
ṅa rgyal las kyaṅ ṅa rgyal ni rigs la sogs pa che ba bas kyaṅ bdag che’o sñam du sems kheṅs pa’o – śreyasaḥ kulādibhir aham eva śreyān iti cittasyonnatir mānātimānaḥ. From Triṃś p. 299-10, tib. fol. 158a7 = Pskvai fol. 217b2-3.
ṅa’o sñam pa’i ṅa rgyal ni ñe bar len pa’i phuṅ po la bdag daṅ bdag gi daṅ bral ba de dag la bdag daṅ bdag gir mṅon par źen nas sems kheṅs pa’o – teṣūpādānaskandheṣv ātmātmīyarahiteṣv ātmātmīyābhiniveśaś cittasyonnatir asmimānaḥ. From Triṃś p. 2910-11, tib. fol. 158a7-b1 ~ Pskvai fol. 217b3-6, which expands Triṃś.
cuṅ zad sñam pa’i ṅa rgyal ni rigs daṅ śes rgya daṅ nor la sogs pas khyad ches ’phags pa la bdag cuṅ zad cig gis chuṅ ṅo sñam du sems kheṅs pa’o – bahvantaraviśiṣṭāt kulavijñānavittādibhir alpāntarahīno ’smīti cittasyonnatir ūnamānaḥ. From Triṃś p. 2913-14, tib. fol. 158b2-3 ~ Pskvai, which expands Triṃś in fol. 218a1-4.
mṅon pa’i ṅa rgyal ni yon tan khyad par can ’bras bu daṅ bsam gtan la sogs pa ma thob pa thob bo sñam du sems kheṅs pa’o – aprāpteṣu viśeṣaguṇeṣu phaladhyānādiṣu prāptā [mayeti] cittasyonnatir abhimānaḥ. From Triṃś p. 2911-12, tib. fol. 158b1-2 ~ Pskvai, which expands Triṃś in fol. 217b6-218a1.
log pa’i ṅa rgyal ni yon tan ma yin pa daṅ ldan pa la bdag yon tan daṅ ldan no sñam du sems kheṅs pa’o – aguṇavato guṇavān asmīti cittasyonnatir mithyāmānaḥ. From Triṃś p. 2914-15, tib. fol. 158b3 ~ Pskvai, which expands Triṃś in fol. 218a4-6.
