ñe ba’i ñon moṅs pa thams cad kyi źes bya bas ni goṅ du miṅ gis smos pa’i ñe ba’i ñon moṅs pa rnams daṅ mi ’grogs par ma zad kyi, gźan yaṅ ñe ba’i ñon moṅs pa rnam par g-yeṅ ba daṅ, śes bźin med pa daṅ, ’gyod pa daṅ, gñid la sogs pa daṅ yaṅ mi ’grogs so źes bya ba’i tha tshig go.


’dod chags daṅ, źe sdaṅ daṅ, gti mug gi kun nas ldaṅ ba phra mo daṅ, sbom po daṅ, chuṅ ṅu daṅ, ’briṅ daṅ, chen po’i ’grogs pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa nas ñon moṅs pa’i kun nas ldaṅ ba thams cad kyi bar gyi ’grogs pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so;

na ca sūkṣmasthūlamṛdumadhyamādhimātrarāgadveṣamohaparyutthānasaṃvāsena saṃvasati, yāvan na sarvakleśaparyutthānasaṃvāsena saṃvasati.

6) It does not stay in the company of the manifestation of subtle or coarse, trifling, average or significant cupidity, aversion or delusion, as it does not stay in the company of any vices.

’dod chags daṅ, źe sdaṅ daṅ, gti mug gi kun nas ldaṅ ba źes bya ba la sogs pa ñon moṅs pa rnams daṅ lhan (114a) cig mi gnas par bstan te,
ṭ. fol. 105b7-106a2 seems quoted from Triṃśikābhāṣya p. 2813ff:
’dod chags ni srid pa daṅ srid pa’i loṅs spyod la chags śiṅ smon pa’o – rāgo bhavabhogayor adhyavasānaṃ prārthanā. Triṃś p. 2813-14, tib. fol. 157b2 = Pskvai fol. 214a2;
źe sdaṅ ni sems can rnams la kun nas mnar sems pa ste, gaṅ gi dbaṅ gis sems can rnams la gsod pa daṅ ’chiṅ ba la sogs pa byed pa’o – dveṣaḥ sattveṣv āghāto yadvaśāt sattvānāṃ vadhabandhanādikarmakaḥ. Quotes from Triṃś p. 2816-23, tib. fol. 157b2-7 = Pskvai fol. 216b7-217a4;
gti mug gis ṅan soṅ daṅ, mtho ris daṅ, mya ṅan las ’das pa daṅ, de dag thob par byed pa’i rgyu daṅ, de dag gi rgyu daṅ ’bras bu ’brel pa phyin ci ma log par mi śes pa’o – moho ’pāyeṣu svarge nirvāṇe tatpratiṣṭhāpakeṣu hetuṣu teṣāṃ cāviparīte hetuphalasaṃbandhe ’jñānam. Triṃś p. 2823-24, tib. fol. 157b7.
Cf. Abhidharmasamuccaya p. 71-5, tib. fol. 49a6-7 is not the same.
ṭ. fol. 106a2-7: kun nas ldaṅ ba ni de dag skye ba’i rgyu daṅ rkyen phrad nas mṅon du ’byuṅ ba ste, de yaṅ yul ñe bar gyur la, tshul bźin ma yin pa yid la byed pa daṅ ldan źes gsuṅs pa’i phyir ro. ñon moṅs pa de dag kyaṅ mthoṅ ba’i lam gyis spaṅ bar dka’ ba daṅ sla ba’i bye brag gis phra mo daṅ sbom po źes bya ba la, bsgom pa’i lam gyis spaṅ bar sla ba daṅ, dka’ ba daṅ, śin tu dka’ ba’i bye brag gis chuṅ ṅu daṅ, ’briṅ daṅ, chen po źes bya ste, bsgom pa’i lam chen po’i chen po la sogs pa dgus spaṅs pa’i ñon moṅs pa rnams la bya’o; yaṅ na ’jig rten las ’das pa’i lam gyis spaṅ bar bya ba ni bag chags daṅ bcas te, spaṅ bar bya ba yin pas spaṅ dka’ ba’i phyir phra mo źes bya la, ’jig rten pa’i lam gyis spaṅ bar bya ba ni spaṅ sla bas sbom po źes bya’o; yaṅ na gaṅ zag ñon moṅs pa’i śas chuṅ ba rnams kyis ni phra mo yin la, gaṅ zag ñon moṅs pa śas che ba rnams kyis ni sbom po źes bya’o; yaṅ na gzugs daṅ gzugs med pa’i khams su gtogs pa’i ñon moṅs pa rnams ni kha naṅ du bltas pa yin pas phra mo źes bya la, ’dod pa’i khams kyi ñon moṅs pa rnams kyis ni ’dod pa’i yon tan lṅa la chags te, kha phyir bltas pa yin pas sbom po źes bya’o. ñon moṅs pa’i kun nas ldaṅ ba thams cad kyi bar źes bya ba ni ñon moṅs pa de dag gsum daṅ yaṅ mi ’grogs par yaṅ ma zad kyi, gźan yaṅ the tshom daṅ, mdud pa daṅ, ’chiṅ ba la sogs pa daṅ mi ’grogs par ston to.
Notes to the Sanskrit: 1) Triṃś, Pskvai pratighaḥ 2) Triṃś, Pskvai yenāviṣṭaḥ 3) Triṃś vadhabandhanādikam anarthaṃ cintayati, but Triṃś tib. has gsod pa daṅ ’chiṅ ba la sogs pa’i gnod pa bya bar sems so which suggests vadhabandhanādikaraṇaṃ (-kāryaṃ?) cintayati, -karmaka is by analogy with the use of this word in Triṃś p. 2818 et passim. 4) As ṭ mtho ris for Triṃś sugatau tib. bde ’gro 5) Triṃś ins. yad


gti mug gi mun pa daṅ, rab rib kyi liṅ tog daṅ, sgrib pa daṅ, chod pa’i ’grogs pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa nas ñams par ’gyur ba’i cha daṅ ’thun pa’i chos kun nas ldaṅ ba thams cad kyi bar gyi ’grogs pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so;

na ca mohāndhakāratimirapaṭalāvaraṇanīvaraṇasaṃvāsena saṃvasati, yāvan na sarvahānibhāgīyadharmaparyutthānasaṃvāsena saṃvasati.

7) It does not stay in the company of the hindrances and obstructions, darkness of delusion [as basis of all vices], obscurations of clear sight, as it does not stay in the company of any manifestation of moments of existence to be done away with.

gti mug gi mun pa daṅ, rab rib kyi liṅ tog daṅ źes bya ba la sogs pas ñams par ’gyur ba’i chos rnams daṅ lhan cig mi gnas par bstan te, goṅ du ñon moṅs pa’i naṅ du yaṅ gti mug smos mod kyi, mdo las: rmoṅs pa med pa la gźan mi ’byuṅ ṅo, źes gsuṅs te, ñon moṅs pa thams cad ’byuṅ ba’i gźi gti mug yin pas ’dir logs śig tu yaṅ smos so. gti mug ñid mun pa yin pas na gti mug gi mun pa ste, dper na mun pas dṅos (Q 130a) po rnams mi mthoṅ źiṅ log par mthoṅ ba, de bźin du gti mug gis kyaṅ sdug bsṅal la bde bar mthoṅ bas na gti mug gi mun pa źes bya’o; rab rib ñid liṅ tog yin pas na rab rib kyi liṅ tog ste, liṅ tog daṅ ’dra bar tshe rabs gźan gyi ñes dmigs yod, yaṅ dag pa yaṅ mi mthoṅ ba’i phyir ro; gaṅ gi phyir sgrib par gyur pa, de’i phyir chod pa źes bya ste, rtsig pas chod pa’i pha rol na dṅos po yod pa ma mthoṅ ba bźin du tshe ’di’i ñes dmigs yod, yaṅ dag pa yaṅ śin tu mi mthoṅ ba’i phyir ro. yaṅ na tshe rabs gźan gyi las daṅ ñon moṅs pa’i mtshan ñid mi śes pa ni gti mug pa’o, las daṅ ñon moṅs pa de’i ’bras bu sdug bsṅal gyi bdag ñid gnod pa du ma’i raṅ bźin can gyi mtshan ñid mi śes pa ni mun pa’o; tshe ’di’i las daṅ ñon moṅs pa rnams mi śes pa ni rab rib bo, ñon moṅs pa de’i rgyus tshe ’di la gnod pa sna tshogs ’byuṅ ba daṅ phuṅ po ñid kyaṅ sdug bsṅal sna tshogs kyi raṅ bźin can du mi śes pa ni liṅ tog go; las gaṅ byas pas tshe rabs gźan du ’bras bu gaṅ thob par mi śes pa ni sgrib pa’o, ’bras bu de dag kyaṅ tshe ’di nas ma ’phos pa daṅ raṅ bźin med par mi śes pa ni chod pa’o. ñams par ’gyur ba’i cha daṅ mthun pa’i chos kun nas ldaṅ ba thams cad kyi bar gyi ’grogs pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas źes bya ba ni ñams par ’gyur ba’i chos de rnams daṅ lhan cig mi gnas par yaṅ ma zad kyi, gźan yaṅ ñon moṅs pa’i phyogs su gtogs pa’i chos yon tan daṅ sa rim pa goṅ ma la sogs pa ’thob pa las kyaṅ ñams par ’gyur, (Q 130b) ma thob pa yaṅ thob par mi ’gyur ba rnams daṅ lhan cig mi ’grogs so źes bya ba’i don to.


’dod pa daṅ thab mo’i rñog pa daṅ, phuṅ po daṅ, ñon moṅs pa daṅ, ’chi bdag daṅ, lha’i bu’i bdud rnams daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa nas bdud kyi las thams cad kyi bar daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so;

na ca kāmakalahāvilaskandhakleśamṛtyudevaputramāraiḥ sārdhaṃ saṃvasati, yāvan na sarvamārakarmabhiḥ sārdhaṃ saṃvasati.

8) It does not stay with the impurities of cupidity, quarreling and the Evil Ones consisting in the parts of personality, the vices, in death or in sons of gods, as it does not stay with any actions of the Evil One.

’dod pa daṅ ’thab mo’i rñog pa daṅ źes bya ba la sogs pas bdud kyi phyogs su gtogs pa’i skyon rnams daṅ, bdud daṅ bdud kyi las rnams spaṅs pa bstan te, ’dod pa ni gzugs la sogs pa ’dod pa lṅa’i yon tan la bya’o, ’thab mo’i don ni sṅar smras pa bźin te, ’dod pa daṅ ’thab mo de dag ñid rñog pa daṅ ’dra bas na rñog pa źes bya’o.
The commentary on māra and mārakarma is based upon quotations from Śbh:
ṭ. fol. 107a2-b4: bdud bźi la gzugs la sogs pas ñe bar len pa’i phuṅ po lṅa ni phuṅ po’i bdud do. khams gsum spyod pa’i ñon moṅs pa thams cad ni ñon moṅs pa’i bdud do. sems can de daṅ de dag sems can gyi ris mthun pa de daṅ de dag nas śi ’phos pa ni ’chi bdag gi bdud do. gaṅ dag dge ba’i phyogs la rab tu źugs nas phuṅ po daṅ, ñon moṅs pa daṅ, ’chi bdag gi bdud las ’da’ bar ’dod pa’i khams su skyes pa’i lha’i bu dbaṅ phyug chen po rñed pa bar chad bya ba’i phyir ñe bar lhags pa rnams ni lha’i bu’i bdud do.
Śbh fol. 11B15-6, S p. 3444-454, D fol. 126a3-5, not in W: paṃcopādānaskandhāḥ skandhamāraḥ / traidhātukāvacārāḥ kleśāḥ kle(6)śamāraḥ / teṣāṃ teṣāṃ satvānāṃ tasmāt tasmāt sattvanikāyāt yan maraṇaṃ kālakriyā maraṇamāraḥ / yo ’sya kuśalapakṣaprayuktasya skandhakleśamṛtyusamatikramāya kāmadhātūpapanno devaputra aiśvaryaprāpto ’ntarāyam upasaṃharati vyākṣepakaraṇe / ayam ucyate devaputramāraḥ / Śbh goes into further details on devaputramāra fol. 11B16ff, S p. 3454-21, D fol.126a5ff.
ṭ. fol. 107a4-5: bdud kyi las thams cad kyi bar daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so źes bya ba ni gaṅ ’dod pa lṅa’i yon tan la chags pa daṅ, srog gcod pa la sogs pa sdig pa mi dge ba’i las rnams daṅ, gźan yaṅ de kho na rtogs pa’i bar du gcod pa rtog pa daṅ rnam par rtog pa la sogs pa bdud kyi glags rñed par ’gyur ba’i las thams cad bdud kyi las su śes par bya’o ; not in Śbh: – "’It (prajñā) does not stay with any of the actions of the Evil One’ it is said in the text; actions of the Evil One are attachment to the five kinds of desired sense objects (pañcakāmaguṇa), the sinful (pāpaka) and bad actions (akuśalakarma) like killing (prāṇātipāta), etc., but further it is the thought-constructions and fictions (kalpavikalpa) which hinder the understanding of the things themselves (tattvāvabodha), it is all the actions where the Evil One finds weak points to attack (avatāra)".
ṭ. fol. 107a5-6: de yaṅ mdor bstan na gaṅ a la la źig thar bar ’gyur bas mṅon par bsdus (Q 130b8, N 115b) pa mya ṅan las ’das pa daṅ rjes su mthun pa’i dge ba’i chos la dad pa yaṅ dag par skyes pa na ’dod pa la chags pa’i dbaṅ du gyur nas ldog pa ni bdud kyi las so – Śbh fol. 11B19-11A23, S p. 34522-34620, D fol. 126b2-127a2: tatra mārakarmāṇi / yasya kasyacit kuśaladharmacchandaḥ samutpanno naiṣkramyopasaṃhitaḥ / kāmagredham adhipatiṃ kṛtvāpavarttate / veditavyaṃ mārakarmai(11A2)tad iti /
ṭ. fol. 107a6-7: dbaṅ po’i sgo bsdams te gnas pa na gaṅ chags par ’gyur ba’i gzugs daṅ, sgra daṅ, dri daṅ, ro daṅ, reg bya daṅ, chos rnams la mtshan mar ’dzin ciṅ mṅon rtogs su ’dzin pa ni bdud kyi las so – indriyair guptadvārasya viharataḥ / yasya raṃjanīyeṣu rūpeṣu śabdagandharasaspraṣṭavyadharmeṣu nimittagrāhitāyām abhisamayagrāhitāyāṃ cittaṃ praskandati / veditavyaṃ mārakarmaitad iti /
ṭ. fol. 107a7-b1: de bźin du zas kyi tshod rig par gnas pa na ro’i khyad par la sems chags pa daṅ, nam gyi cha stod daṅ cha smad la mi ñal bar rjes su sbyor ba na gñid kyi bde ba daṅ, ñal ba’i bde ba daṅ, glos ’bebs pa’i bde ba la chags śiṅ sems ’jug pa ni bdud kyi las su rigs par bya’o – evaṃ bhojaneṣu mātrajñasya viharataḥ praṇīteṣu raseṣu [chandarāgam] anunayena cittaṃ praskandati / [bhaktavaiṣamye evaṃ] pūrvvarātrāpararātraṃ jāgarikāyo(2)gam anuyuktasya viharataḥ / nidrāsukhe śayanasukhe pārśvasukhe cittaṃ praskandhati / veditavyaṃ mārakarmaitad iti /
ṭ. fol. 107b1-3: śes bźin daṅ bcas par gnas pa ni byis pa’am ’gro ba bzaṅ mo kha dog mchog daṅ ldan pa’i rnams mthoṅ nas tshul bźin ma yin pa yid la byed ciṅ der sems ’jug pa daṅ, ’jig rten gyi ’phral gyi bya ba maṅ po la sems ’jug pa daṅ, ’du ’dzi maṅ po’i naṅ du ’drea źiṅ sdig pa’i grogs po mi dge ba’i las byed pa rnams mthoṅ nas sems la mos pa skye ba ni bdud kyi las so – tathā saṃprajānadvihāriṇo viharataḥ / abhikramapratikramādiṣu śiśum udāravarṇṇaṃ raṃjanīyaṃ mātṛgrāmaṃ dṛṣṭvā ayoniśo nimittagrāheṇa cittaṃ praskandati / lokacitrāṇi vā dṛṣṭvā cittaṃ praskandati / bahvarthatāyāṃ bahu(3)kṛtyatāyāṃ cittaṃ prakandati / tad yathā gṛhasthapravrajitaiḥ saṃsargarāmatāyāṃ pāpamitraiḥ saha ekasya vāsitāyāṃ dṛṣṭyanumataye cittaṃ praskandati / veditavyaṃ mārakarmaitad iti //
ṭ. fol. 107b3: de bźin du saṅs rgyas daṅ, chos daṅ, dge ’dun daṅ, sdug bsṅal daṅ, kun ’byuṅ daṅ, ’gog pa daṅ, lam daṅ, tshe ’di daṅ, tshe rabs pha rol rnams la the tshom daṅ yid gñis skye ba ni bdud kyi las so – tathā buddhe dharme saṃghe duḥkhe samudaye nirodhe mārge / ihaloke paraloke kāṃkṣāvimataya utpadyante / veditavyaṃ mārakarmaitad iti /
ṭ. fol. 107b3-4: gaṅ gi tshe rñed pa daṅ bkur sti la sems chags pa daṅ, ser sna daṅ, ’dod chen daṅ, chog mi śes pa daṅ, khro ba daṅ, khon du ’dzin pa daṅ, tshul ’chos pa daṅ, kha gsag la sems ’jug na bdud kyi las su rig par bya’o – Śbh fol. 11A22-4, S p. 3473-6, D fol. 127a4-5: yadā lābhasatkāre cittaṃ pra(5)skandati / mātsarye mahecchatāyāṃ asaṃtuṣṭau / krodhopanāhakuhanālapanādiṣu [śramaṇālaṃkāravipakṣeṣu dharmeṣu] cittaṃ praskandati / veditavyaṃ mārakarmaitad iti /
After the statement in ṭ. fol. 107b4-5: gźan yaṅ rgyas par bśad na, de la sogs pa bdud kyi las tshad med par yod de, ’jam dpal rnam par ’phrul ba las kyaṅ: "Further, if speaking extensively, these and the other works of the Evil One are immeasurable (apramāṇa) ...", ṭ. then fol. 107b5-109a5 quotes a long passage from Mañjuśrīvikurvāṇaparivarta on the topic of Works of the Evil One, which enumerates twenty kinds: lha’i bu ji tsam du las rnams ’byuṅ ba de tsam du bdud kyi las so. ji tsam du smon pa daṅ, ji tsam du log par ’dzin pa daṅ, ji tsam du mchog tu ’dzin pa, de tsam du bdud kyi las so. ji tsam du ’dod pa daṅ, ji tsam du ’du śes pa daṅ, ji tsam du rlom sems pa daṅ, ji tsam du yoṅs su rtog pa, de tsam du bdud kyi las so. lha’i bu, gźan yaṅ byaṅ chub kyi sems la mṅon par źen pa yaṅ bdud kyi las so, sbyin pa’i sems la mṅon par źen pa yaṅ bdud kyi las so, tshul khrims daṅ bzod pa daṅ brtson ’grus daṅ bsam gtan daṅ śes rab kyi sems la mṅon par źen pa yaṅ bdud kyi las so. sbyin pa’i rlom sems su byed pa, daṅ tshul khrims mchog tu ’dzin pa daṅ, bzod pa ’dzin pa daṅ, brtson ’grus len pa daṅ, bsam gtan la mtshan ma daṅ, śes rab rgyu ba yaṅ bdud kyi las so. dgon pa la dga’ źiṅ mos pa’i sems daṅ, btaṅ sñoms su ltuṅ ba yaṅ bdud kyi las so. ’dod pa ñuṅ ba daṅ, chog śes pa daṅ, sbyaṅs pa’i yon tan daṅ, yo byad bsñuṅs pa rlom sems su byed pa yaṅ bdud kyi las so. bdag ni stoṅ pa ñid la gnas pa, bdag ni mtshan ma med pa la gnas pa, bdag ni smon pa med pa la gnas pa, bdag ni spros pa med pa la gnas pa, bdag ni de bźin gśegs pa’i bka’ sgrub ciṅ gnas pa’o, sñam du rlom sems su byed ciṅ rnam par rtog pa yaṅ bdud kyi las so. lha’i bu, rtog pa daṅ, rnam par rtog pa daṅ, yoṅs su rtog pa daṅ, mthoṅ ba daṅ, thos pa daṅ, bye brag phyed pa daṅ, rnam par śes pa’i gnas ji tsam pa, de tsam du bdud kyi las so. lha’i bus smras pa: ’jam dpal, bdud kyi las ga las byuṅ? ’jam dpal gyis smras pa: lha’i bu, bdud kyi las ni brtson ’grus las byuṅ ṅo. de ci’i phyir źe na? lha’i bu, brtson pa la bdud glags tshol gyi, mi brtson pa la bdud kyis ci źig bya bar ’gyur , de ñid bdud kyi las yin no. lha’i bus smras pa: ’jam dpal, byaṅ chub sems dpa’ ji ltar na brtson pa yin, ji ltar na mi brtson pa yin? ’jam dpal gyis smras pa: lha’i bu, ji tsam du gñis la sbyor ba, de tsam du brtson pa ma yin no. de ci’i phyir źe na? ’jig rten gnas pa ni gñis la sbyor ba daṅ ldan no. lha’i bu, brtson pa źes bya ba ’di ni sbyor ba yaṅ dag pa’i tshig bla dags so. sbyor ba yaṅ dag pa źes bya ba ’di ni sbyor ba med pa’i tshig bla dags so. sbyor ba med pa źes bya ba ’di ni spros pa med pa’i tshig bla dags so. spros pa med pa źes bya ba ’di ni sbyor ba yaṅ dag pa’i tshig bla dvags so. lha’i bu, gaṅ na mig la mi sbyor ba daṅ, gzugs la mi sbyor ba ’di ni byaṅ chub sems dpa’i sbyor ba yaṅ dag pa źes bya, gaṅ na rna ba la mi sbyor ba daṅ, sgra la mi sbyor ba daṅ, sna la mi sbyor ba daṅ, dri la mi sbyor ba daṅ, lce la mi sbyor ba daṅ, ro la mi sbyor ba daṅ, lus la mi sbyor ba daṅ, reg bya la mi sbyor ba daṅ, yid la mi sbyor ba daṅ, chos la mi sbyor ba ’di ni byaṅ chub sems dpa’i sbyor ba yaṅ dag pa źes bya’o. yaṅ de bźin du lha’i bu, ñi śu po ’di dag ni byaṅ chub sems dpa’ rnams kyi bdud kyi las yaṅ dag phul yin no. ñi śu gaṅ źe na? ’di lta ste: 1) rnal ’byor spyod pa rnam par grol ba ’dod ciṅ ’khor bas skrag pa rnams la bsñen pa daṅ, bsten pa daṅ, bsñen bkur byed pa ni bdud kyi las so. 2) stoṅ pa ñid la so sor rtog ciṅ sems can yal bar ’dor ba yaṅ bdud kyi las so. 3) ’dus ma byas la so sor rtog ciṅ ’dus byas kyi dge ba’i rtsa bas yoṅs su skyo ba yaṅ bdud kyi las so. 4) bsam gtan bskyed ciṅ bsam gtan las rnam par mi ldog pa tshol ba yaṅ bdud kyi las so. 5) chos ston kyaṅ chos ñan pa rnams la sñiṅ rje chen po mi skyed pa yaṅ bdud kyi las so. 6) yon tan daṅ ldan pa daṅ sbyin gnas tshol bźin du tshul khrims ’chal pa rnams la khro ba yaṅ bdud kyi las so. 7) ñan thos daṅ raṅ saṅs rgyas kyi gtam ston ciṅ theg pa chen po’i gtam ’chab pa yaṅ bdud kyi las so. 8) zab mo’i gtam ’chab ciṅ gtam sna tshogs ston pa yaṅ bdud kyi las so. 9) byaṅ chub sems dpa’i lam śes kyaṅ pha rol tu phyin pa’i lam yoṅs su mi tshol ba yaṅ bdud kyi las so. 10) rab tu brtson pa’i bsṅags pa thob kyaṅ sems can mi brtson pa rnams mṅon par mi sbyor ba yaṅ bdud kyi las so. 11) dge ba’i rtsa ba stsogs kyaṅ byaṅ chub kyi sems mṅon du mi byed pa yaṅ bdud kyi las so. 12) lhag mthoṅ gi rnal ’byor daṅ ldan par gnas kyaṅ sems can rnams lhag mthoṅ dag par ’dzin du mi ’jug pa yaṅ bdud kyi las so. 13) ñon moṅs pa ma lus par zad pa tshol źiṅ ’khor ba’i rgyun gyi ñon moṅs pa rnams la smod pa yaṅ bdud kyi las so. 14) śes rab kyis rnam par dpyod ciṅ sñiṅ rje chen po la dmigs pa mi ’dzin pa yaṅ bdud kyi las so. 15) thabs daṅ mi ldan par dge ba spyod pa thams cad kyaṅ bdud kyi las so. 16) byaṅ chub sems dpa’i sde snod mi tshol gyi ’jig rten rgyaṅ phan pa’i gsaṅ tshig ’dzin pa yaṅ bdud kyi las so. 17) maṅ du thos kyaṅ gźan gyi śes kyis dogs te, chos la slob dpon gyi dpe mkhyud byed pa yaṅ bdud kyi las so. 18) ’jig rten pa’i dgos pa’i źal ta byed ciṅ maṅ du thos pa mi tshol ba yaṅ bdud kyi las so. 19) byaṅ chub sems dpa’ chos smra ba theg pa chen po la yaṅ dag par źugs pa skal pa mñam pa rnams la mi bsten, mi bsñen, bsñen bkur mi byed kyi, ñan thos daṅ raṅ saṅs rgyas kyi theg pa la yaṅ dag par źugs pa skal pa mi mñām pa la dga’ ba yaṅ bdud kyi las so. 20) gaṅ gi tshe brgya byin nam, tshaṅs pa’am, ’jig rten skyoṅ ba’am, rgyal po’am, tshoṅ dpon nam, khyim bdag gi loṅs spyod daṅ, nor daṅ, rin po che daṅ, dbaṅ phyug gi che ba ñid du gyur pa, de’i tshe chos kyi che ba ñid daṅ ldan pa rnams la mi bsten, mi bsñen, bsñen bkur mi byed pa, ’di dag ni, lha’i bu, byaṅ chub sems dpa’ rnams kyi bdud kyi las yaṅ dag phul ñi śu’o źes bya ba la sogs pa gsuṅs te . The quotation also has special relevance to the concept of yuganaddha as described in Akṣ.
For further information one is refered to Śata and other sūtras: śes rab kyi pha rol tu phyin pa stoṅ phrag brgya ba la sogs pa mdo de daṅ de dag gi naṅ nas gsuṅs pa’i bdud kyi las rnams la yaṅ bya bar rig par bya’o.
The Lokottaraparivarta quoted in Śikṣ. p. 1511ff mentions ten kinds of mārakarma. Śbh gives a bibliography on p. 343 n. 2.
Notes to the Sanskrit text: 1) S om. kleśamāraḥ 2) S satv... MS, S ins. daṇḍa 3) As D and ṭ .. nas MS, S ...āḥ for ...āt 4) S ya(yādya)n 5) S yopyakuśala... 6) MS, S ...aḥ / 7) MS ..prāptaḥ / an... S niścayaprāptaḥ an... 8) MS, S ins. daṇḍa. Both D (fol. 126a4 bar chad bya ba [daṅ rnam par g-yeṅ bar bya ba]’i phyir .... ñe bar logs so) and ṭ seem to have read antarāya - upasaṃkramati for ’ntarāyam upasaṃharati 9) As D dge ba’i chos la ’dun pa MS kuśalo dharma.. S karmaṇo dharmacch... 10) S kṛtvā pravarttante 11) S sahagatvarasampraṣṭavyadharmeṣu 12) As D, ṭ mṅon rtogs su ’dzin pa MS, S anuvyaṃjanagrāhitāyāṃ 13) D mi mthun pa dag la seems to read pratikūleṣu, but ṭ khyad par la suits praṇīteṣu 14) Bracketed part not in ṭ 15) D reads veditavyaṃ mārakarmaitad iti / for bhaktavaîṣamye D should be preferred in accordance with the structure of the text, but ṭ om. both, which may imply that the reading of MS is a very old one. 16) S ...rva... for ...rvva... 17) S ananuyuktasya 18) MS ....īṣāṃ for īyāṃ 19) MS bahvarthatāṃ 20) S ...sargārāma... 21...21) S saha ekavyavasitāyāṃ MS ins. daṇḍa after ...tāyāṃ. ekasya has no counterpart in D lhan cig gnas śiṅ, which is a possible translation of sahavāsitāyāṃ. The syllable interpreted as sya is blurred. 22) S ...mate for ...mataye 23) MS, S ins. daṇḍa. 24) S asant... MS, S om. daṇḍa. 25) MS, S ins. daṇḍa after ...ādiṣu MS ins. daṇḍa after ...nāha


bdag daṅ, sems can daṅ, srog daṅ, gso ba daṅ, skyes bu daṅ, gaṅ zag daṅ, śed las skyes daṅ, śed bur ’dzin pa la mṅon par źen pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa nas ’dzin pa la mṅon par źen pa thams cad kyi bar daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so;

na cātmasattvajīvapoṣapuruṣapudgalamānavamānujagrāhābhiniveśena sārdhaṃ saṃvasati, yāvan na sarvagrāhābhiniveśena sārdhaṃ saṃvasati.

9) It does not stay with attachment of grasping for a self, an animated being, a life-principle, a life-sustaining principle, a spirit, personality, a man or human, as it does not stay with attachment to any grasping.

bdag daṅ, sems can daṅ, srog daṅ, gso ba źes bya ba la sogs pas bdag tu ’dzin pa la mṅon par chags pa daṅ ma ’dres pa bstan te, bdag la sogs pa thams cad kyaṅ bdag tu ’dod pa’i rnam graṅs te, de dag kyaṅ bdag can rtag par smra ba daṅ, gźuṅ gcig mod kyi, grub pa’i mtha’ tha dad pa las mtshan ñid mi mthun pa tsam gyis phye ste, miṅ so sor btags nas gźag pa’o. ’dzin pa la mṅon par źen ces bya ba’i sgra bdag daṅ sems can la sogs pa’i tshig re re daṅ yaṅ sbyar te, bdag tu ’dzin pa la mṅon par źen ces bya ba daṅ, sems can du ’dzin pa la mṅon par źen ces bya ba la sogs par sbyar ro. bdag la sogs pa ’di dag gi khyad par ni sṅar bśad par zad do. ’dzin pa la mṅon par źen pa thams cad kyi bar daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so źes bya ba’i bdag tu ’dzin pa goṅ du smos pa rnams daṅ lhan cig mi gnas par yaṅ ma zad kyi, gźan yaṅ bdag tu ’dzin pa dbaṅ phyug daṅ, gtso bo daṅ, dus la sogs pa yod par sems pa rnams daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so źes bya ba’i don to.


las kyi sgrib pa daṅ, chos kyi sgrib pa daṅ, ñon moṅs pa’i sgrib pa daṅ, lta ba’i sgrib pa daṅ, ’gro ba’i sgrib pa daṅ, rnam par smin pa’i sgrib pa daṅ, śes pa’i sgrib pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa nas bag chags kyi mtshams sbyor ba thams cad kyi bar daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so;

na ca karmāvaraṇadharmāvaraṇakleśāvaraṇadṛṣṭyāvaraṇagatyāvaraṇavipākāvaraṇajñānāvaraṇaiḥ sārdhaṃ saṃvasati, yāvan na sarvavāsanāpratisaṃdhibhiḥ sārdhaṃ saṃvasati.

10) It does not stay with the hindrances of actions [that is, obstacles to seeing truth (satyadarśanântarāya) in one life caused by bad actions in another life], the hindrances to [obtain] religion, the hindrances of vices, the hindrances of viewpoints, the hindrances to [seeing truth because born in bad] states of existence, the hindrances [to seeing truth when born in good states of existence, that because] of maturation [of previous bad actions] or the hindrances to knowledge, as it does not stay with any connections to rebirth caused by bad habits.

las kyi sgrib pa daṅ chos kyi sgrib pa daṅ źes bya ba la sogs pas bag chags kyi mtshams sbyor ba sgrib pa rnams daṅ ma ’dres pa bstan te, las kyi sgrib pa ni tshe ’di ñid la mtshams med pa lṅa’i las byas pas las des tshe de la bden pa mthoṅ ba la bar du gcod pa ni las kyi sgrib pa’o. chos la ser sna byed ciṅ mos pa bzlog pa la sogs pa chos thos pa’i bar du gcod pa’i las rnams byas pas tshe rabs de daṅ de dag tu dge ba’i bśes gñen la sogs pa daṅ mi ldan źiṅ chos thos par mi ’gyur ba ni chos kyi sgrib pa źes bya’o. ’dod chags la sogs pa ñon moṅs pa śas che bas ’phags pa’i lam bsgrub par mi nus pa ni ñon moṅs pa’i sgrib pa’o. ’jig tshogs daṅ mthar ’dzin par lta ba la sogs pa lta ba lṅa rnams ni lta ba’i sgrib pa źes bya’o. sems can dmyal ba daṅ dud ’gro’i skye gnas la sogs pa ṅan soṅ gsum gyi ’gro ba dag tu skyes nas bden pa mthoṅ bar mi ’gyur ba ni ’gro ba’i sgrib pa źes bya’o. tshe sṅa ma la sdig pa mi dge ba’i las byas pa’i rnam par smin pas lha daṅ mir skyes kyaṅ rnam par smin pa des bsgribs pas bden pa mi mthoṅ ba ni rnam par smin pa’i sgrib pa źes bya’o. ji tsam du śes par bya ba la bar du gcod pa phuṅ po daṅ, khams daṅ skye mched la sogs pa la mṅon par chags pa’i bag chags ñon moṅs pa can ma yin pa’i ma rig pa ni śes pa’i sgrib pa’o. bag chags de dag gi mtshams sbyor bas na, bag chags daṅ mtshams sbyor ba ste, de’i dbaṅ gis gcig nas gcig tu tshe len par byed pas so.


rtog pa daṅ, rnam par rtog pa daṅ, yoṅs su rtog pa daṅ, mtshan ma daṅ, dmigs pa daṅ, mthoṅ ba daṅ, thos pa daṅ, bye brag phyed pa daṅ, rnam par rig pa rnams daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa nas mdud pa daṅ sgro btags pa thams cad kyi bar daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so;

na ca kalpavikalpaparikalpanimittārambaṇadṛṣṭaśrutamatavijñaptaiḥ sārdhaṃ saṃvasati, yāvan na sarvagranthasamāropaiḥ sārdhaṃ saṃvasati.

11) It does not stay with thought-constructions, fictions, imaginations, distinguishing marks, objects, whatever is seen, heard, thought or known, as it does not stay with any ties [the three first mentioned] or imputations [the rest].

rtog pa daṅ rnam par rtog pa daṅ yoṅs su rtog pa źes bya ba la sogs pas mdud daṅ sgro btags pa rnams daṅ ma ’dres pa bstan te, rtog pa daṅ rnam par rtog pa daṅ yoṅs su rtog pa gsum ni mdud pa źes bya ste, byaṅ chub sems dpa’i ’chiṅ ba ni rnam par rtog pa sna tshogs yin pa’i phyir ro. mtshan ma daṅ dmigs pa la sogs te, lhag ma rnams ni sgro btags pa źes bya ste, mtshan ma la sogs pa’i rnam par chos rnams bskyed pa’i phyir ro.
de la mig daṅ rna ba la sogs pa naṅ gi dṅos po rnams la yod pa’am med par ’dzin pa ni rtog pa’o, gzugs daṅ sgra la sogs pa phyi’i yul rnams la yod pa daṅ med par ’dzin pa ni rnam par rtog pa’o, phyi daṅ naṅ gi dṅos po gñi ga la yod pa daṅ med par ’dzin pa ni yoṅs su rtog pa’o. yaṅ na, ñan thos kyi theg pa la mṅon par chags śiṅ rtog pa ni rtog pa źes bya’o, raṅ saṅs rgyas kyi theg pa la mṅon par chags pa ni rnam par rtog pa’o, theg pa bla na med pa la mṅon par chags pa ni yoṅs su rtog pa’o. yaṅ na, rtog ge ba rnams ni dṅos po la tshad ma rnam pa gsum gyis ’jal te, mṅon sum daṅ, rjes su dpag daṅ, luṅ gi tshad ma’o; de la mṅon sum gyi tshad mas dṅos po la ’jal ba ni rtog pa’o, rjes su dpag pa’i tshad mas dṅos po ’jal ba ni rnam par rtog pa’o, luṅ gi tshad mas dṅos po ’jal ba ni yoṅs su rtog pa’o.
sṅon po daṅ ser po daṅ mya ṅan las ’das pa daṅ ’khor ba źes bya ba dag ni mtshan ma’o, gzugs daṅ sgra daṅ dri daṅ ro la sogs pa yul rnams ni dmigs pa’o, mthoṅ ba ni mig gis so, thos pa ni rna bas so, bye brag phyed pa ni yid kyis so, rnam par rig pa ni rnam par śes pa lhag ma rnams kyis so. yaṅ na, mthoṅ ba la sogs pas ni sṅar bśad pa bźin no.
mdud daṅ sgro btags pa thams cad kyi bar daṅ lhan cig mi gnas źes bya ba ni mdud daṅ sgro btags pa goṅ ma rnams daṅ lhan cig mi gnas par yaṅ ma zad kyi, gźan yaṅ byaṅ chub sems dpa’i ’chiṅ bar ’gyur ba daṅ dṅos po la sgro ’dogs pa gźan dag daṅ yaṅ lhan cig mi gnas par ston to.
The commentary is unfortunately not very enlightening from an epistemological point of view.


bdag daṅ, rtag pa daṅ, gtsaṅ ba daṅ, bde ba’i ’grogs pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa nas phyin ci log thams cad kyi bar daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so;

na cātmanityaśucisukhaiḥ sārdhaṃ saṃvasati, yāvan na sarvaviparyāsaiḥ sārdhaṃ saṃvasati.

(p. 67) 12) It does not stay with self, permanence, purity or happiness, as it does not stay with any wrong understanding.

No. 12 is omitted by T1 p. 196c4, the number of items then mentioned rightly becoming 16, not 17, which is one too many according to the text. ṭ. has only a very short commentary, a fact which also indicates the late insertion of this item: bdag daṅ rtag ces bya ba la sogs pas ni phyin ci ma log daṅ ma ’dres par bstan to.


sems can gyi sems kyi spyod pa brgyad khri bźi stoṅ daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa nas chos kyi phuṅ po brgyad khri bźi stoṅ gi bar daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so;

na ca caturaśītisahasrasattvacittacaritaiḥ sārdhaṃ saṃvasati, yāvan na caturaśītisahasradharmaskandhaiḥ sārdhaṃ saṃvasati.

13) It does not stay with the eighty-four thousand kinds of mental behaviour in living beings [the contrary (vipakṣa) ], as it does not stay [with the antidote (pratipakṣa), namely] the eighty-four thousand multitudes of religious teachings.

sems can gyi sems kyi spyod pa brgyad khri bźi stoṅ daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa źes bya ba la sogs pa mi mthun pa’i phyogs daṅ gñen po daṅ ma ’dres pa bstan te; sems can gyi sems kyi spyod pa brgyad khri bźi stoṅ ni mi mthun pa’i phyogs so, chos kyi phuṅ po brgyad khri bźi stoṅ ni gñen po’i phyogs te, lhag ma rnams la yaṅ de bźin du sbyar ro. de la sems can ’dod chags la spyod pa ñi khri chig stoṅ daṅ, źe sdaṅ la spyod pa ñi khri chig stoṅ daṅ, gti mug la spyod pa ñi khri chig stoṅ daṅ, cha mñam pa la spyod pa ñi khri chig stoṅ ste, de ltar brgyad khri bźi stoṅ ṅo. de la ’dod chags kyi gñen po chos kyi phuṅ po ñi khri chig stoṅ, źe sdaṅ gi gñen po chos kyi phuṅ po ñi khri chig stoṅ, gti mug gi gñen po chos kyi phuṅ po ñi khri chig stoṅ, cha mñam pa’i gñen po chos kyi phuṅ po ñi khri chig stoṅ ste, de ltar na chos kyi phuṅ po brgyad khri bźi stoṅ ṅo.


ser sna daṅ gtoṅ ba daṅ, ’chal pa’i tshul khrims daṅ tshul khrims daṅ, gnod sems daṅ bzod pa daṅ, le lo daṅ brtson ’grus daṅ, rnam par g-yeṅ ba daṅ bsam gtan daṅ, ’chal pa’i śes rab daṅ śes rab daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa nas pha rol tu phyin pa’i phyogs daṅ mi ’thun pa’i phyogs sems pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so;

na ca mātsaryatyāgadauḥśīlyaśīlavyāpādakṣāntikausīdyavīryavikṣepadhyānadauṣprajñāprajñābhiḥ sārdhaṃ saṃvasati, yāvan na pāramitāpakṣacintyatāvipakṣābhyāṃ sārdhaṃ saṃvasati.

14) It does not stay with stinginess or generosity, bad or good morality, malice or tolerance, laziness or vigour, distraction or meditation, wrong or right insight, as it does not stay with either the side of perfections, or the contrary of mental activity.

de la ñe bar blaṅs pa’i dṅos po gter daṅ ’bru la sogs pa mi gtoṅ ba ni ser sna’o, de las bzlog na gtoṅ ba’o; srog gcod pa daṅ, ma byin par len pa daṅ, ’dod pas log par g-yem pa la sogs pa mi dge ba’i las la źugs pa ni ’chal pa’i tshul khrims can yin la, srog gcod pa la sogs pa las phyir log pa ni tshul khrims so; sems can rnams la rdeg pa daṅ ’chiṅ ba la sogs pas ’tshe bar sems pa ni gnod sems so, rdeg pa daṅ ’chiṅ ba la sogs pas sems can la mi ’tshe źiṅ gnod par byas kyaṅ slar gnod par mi byed pa ni bzod pa’o; dge ba’i phyogs la sems mi spro źiṅ mi ’jug pa ni le lo ste, de las bzlog na brtson ’grus so, phyi’i yul rnams la sems ’phros pa ni rnam par g-yeṅ ba’o, dmigs pa’i dṅos po la sems rtse gcig pa ni bsam gtan no, chos kyi mtshan ñid la phyin ci log tu chags śiṅ ’dzin pa ni ’chal pa’i śes rab bo, chos kyi mtshan ñid la phyin ci ma log par ’byed par byed ni śes rab bo.


ṅes pa daṅ ma ṅes pa daṅ, yaṅ dag pa daṅ log pa daṅ, dge ba daṅ mi dge ba daṅ, kha na ma tho ba daṅ bcas pa daṅ kha na ma tho ba med pa daṅ, zag pa daṅ bcas pa daṅ zag pa med pa daṅ, ’dus byas daṅ ’dus ma byas daṅ, ’jig rten pa daṅ ’jig rten las ’das pa daṅ, bzaṅ po daṅ ṅan pa daṅ, kun nas ñon moṅs pa daṅ rnam par byaṅ ba daṅ, ’khor ba daṅ mya ṅan las ’das pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa nas chos thams cad kyi mi ’thun pa’i phyogs daṅ gñen po’i bar daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so;

na ca nityānityasamyagmithyākuśalākuśalasāvadyānavadyasāsravānāsravasaṃskṛtāsaṃskṛtalaukikalokottarapraṇītahīnakliṣṭavyavadātasaṃsāranirvāṇaiḥ sārdhaṃ saṃvasati, yāvan na sarvadharmavipakṣapratipakṣaiḥ sārdhaṃ saṃvasati.

15) It does not stay with the decided or the undecided [when it concerns religious development], nor with the true or false, good or bad, blameworthy or blameless, sullied or unsullied, conditioned or unconditioned, worldly or unworldly, excellent or insignificant, pure or impure, existence or extinction, as it does not stay with contraries or antidotes to any moments of existence.

ṅes pa daṅ ma ṅes pa źes bya ba la sogs pa rigs rnam pa lṅa ste: ñan thos kyi rigs can daṅ, raṅ saṅs rgyas kyi rigs can daṅ, theg pa chen po’i rigs can daṅ, rigs ma ṅes pa daṅ, rigs med pa’o. de la rigs med pa’i gaṅ zag rnams ni ṅes pa ste, de dag tu thams cad du ’khor bar gnas par gdon mi za ba’i phyir ro. theg pa gsum du ṅes pa’i rigs can ni ma ṅes pa ste, dge ba’i bśes gñen gyi rkyen gyis mya ṅan las ’das par yaṅ ’gyur bas na, khams gsum du gnas par ṅes pa med pa’i phyir ro. yaṅ na rigs can rnam pa gsum ni ṅes pa ste, raṅ raṅ gi theg pa la brten nas ’bras bu thob par gdon mi za ba’i phyir ro. ma ṅes pa’i rigs can ni ma ṅes pa ste, dge ba’i bśes gñen gyi rkyen gyis theg pa gar btsud par ’jug ciṅ, dge ba’i bśes gñen daṅ ma phrad na mya ṅan las ’das par ’gyur bar chad pa med pa’i phyir ro.
yaṅ dag pa’i lta ba la źugs pa’i gaṅ zag rnams ni yaṅ dag pa źes bya ste, las daṅ las kyi ’bras bu daṅ, dkon mchog daṅ bden pa la sogs pa yod par lta bas so. log par lta ba la źen pa’i gaṅ zag ni log pa źes bya ste, las daṅ las kyi ’bras bu daṅ, bden pa daṅ dkon mchog la sogs pa med par ’dod pa’i phyir ro. yaṅ na, bcom ldan ’das kyis tshogs rnam pa gsum gsuṅs te, yaṅ dag pa ñid du ṅes pa’i tshogs daṅ, log pa ñid du ṅes pa’i tshogs daṅ, ma ṅes pa’i tshogs so. de la yaṅ dag pa ñid du ṅes pa’i tshogs ni gaṅ ’phags pa rnams te, ’dod chags ma lus par spaṅs pa daṅ, źe sdaṅ ma lus par spaṅs pa daṅ, gti mug ma lus par spaṅs pa ste, de dag ni ñon moṅs pa zad par ṅes pas na, yaṅ dag par ṅes pa źes bya’o; de la log par ṅes pa ni mtshams med pa byed pa’i gaṅ zag rnams te, de dag ni ṅan soṅ gsum du skye bar ṅes pa’i phyir log par ṅes pa źes bya’o; ṅes pa las gźan pa rnams ni ma ṅes pa źes bya ste, rkyen la ltos nas gal te na ñon moṅs pa spoṅ bar byed la, gal te mtshams med pa’i las kyaṅ byed pa’i phyir ro.
chos de dag ñid ’bras bu yid du ’oṅ ba daṅ yid du mi ’oṅ ba skyed pa’i bye brag gis rnam pa gñis su gźag ste, dge ba daṅ mi dge ba’o. de la ’bras bu yid du ’oṅ ba ni lha daṅ mi la sogs pa bde ’gro rnams so; de skyed pa ni dge ba źes bya ste, srog mi gcod pa daṅ, ma byin par mi len pa la sogs pa dge ba bcu’i las kyi lam rnams so. ’bras bu yid du mi ’oṅ ba ni sems can dmyal ba daṅ dud ’gro la sogs pa’o; de skyed par byed pa ni mi dge ba źes bya ste, srog gcod pa la sogs pa mi dge ba bcu’i las kyi lam rnams so.
chos de kyaṅ dag gleṅ du mi ruṅ ba daṅ gleṅ du ruṅ ba’i sgo nas gñis su gźag ste, kha na ma tho ba daṅ bcas pa daṅ kha na ma tho ba med pa’o. de la dam pa rnams kyi gleṅ źiṅ bsñad du mi ruṅ ba ni kha na ma tho ba daṅ bcas pa źes bya ste, srog gcod pa la sogs pa mi dge ba’i las ñid do; dam pa rnams kyi naṅ du gleṅ źiṅ bsñad du ruṅ ba ni kha na ma tho ba med pa ste, srog gcod pa las phyir log pa la sogs pa dge ba bcu’i las kyi lam daṅ, dad pa daṅ, tshul khrims la sogs pa’o.
chos de dag kyaṅ khams gsum du ’byuṅ bar byed pa daṅ mi byed pa’i bye brag gis rnam pa gñis su gźag ste, zag pa daṅ bcas pa daṅ zag pa med pa’o. de la khams gsum du ’byuṅ bar byed pa’i chos rnams ni zag pa daṅ bcas pa źes bya ste, khams gsum du skye ba’i rgyu byed pa’o; de la zag pa ni ’dod chags la sogs pa’i ñon moṅs pa la bya ste, de daṅ bcas pas zag pa daṅ bcas pa’o. khams gsum du ’byuṅ bar mi byed pa’i chos de dag ni zag pa med pa ste, ’phags pa’i lam la sogs pa’o.
chos de dag ñid rgyu rkyen gyis bskyed pa daṅ ma bskyed pa’i bye brag gis rnam pa gñis su gźag ste, ’dus byas daṅ ’dus ma byas so. de la gaṅ rgyu daṅ rkyen gyis bskyed pa rnams ni ’dus byas źes bya’o; gaṅ rgyu daṅ rkyen gyis ma bskyed pa ni ’dus ma byas źes bya ste, de bźin ñid daṅ mya ṅan las ’das pa la sogs pa’o.
chos de dag ñid ’jig rten gyis ’dris par byas pa daṅ ma byas pa’i bye brag gis rnam pa gñis su gźag ste, ’jig rten pa daṅ ’jig rten las ’das pa’o. de la ’jig rten pa rnams kyis ’dris par byas pa ni ’jig rten pa ste, ñe bar len pa’i phuṅ po lṅa la sogs pa ’khor bar gtogs pa’i chos thams cad do. ’jig rten pa rnams kyis ’dris par ma byas pa ni ’jig rten las ’das pa źes bya ste, gaṅ zag daṅ chos la bdag med pa’i de bźin ñid rnam par dag pa daṅ, rnam par mi rtog pa’i ye śes daṅ, dag pa’i ’jig rten pa’i ye śes la sogs pa’o.
chos de dag ñid dam pa daṅ dam pa ma yin pa’i sgo nas rnam pa gñis su gźag ste, bzaṅ po daṅ ṅan pa’o. de la gaṅ dam pa rnams ni bzaṅ po źes bya ste, ñon moṅs pa’i phyogs su gyur pa spaṅs pas na ’jig rten las ’das pa’i chos rnams la bya’o. de la chos gaṅ dam pa ma yin pa rnams ni ṅan pa źes bya ste, ’jig rten par gtogs pa’i chos rnams so.
chos de dag ñid nag po’i phyogs daṅ dkar po’i phyogs kyi bye brag gis rnam pa gñis su gźag ste, kun nas ñon moṅs pa daṅ rnam par byaṅ ba’o. de la nag po’i phyogs ni kun nas ñon moṅs pa źes bya ste, ’dod chags la sogs pa’o; dkar po’i phyogs ni rnam par byaṅ ba ste, byaṅ chub kyi phyogs daṅ sa daṅ pha rol tu phyin pa la sogs pa’o.
chos de dag ñid sdug bsṅal gyi gźi daṅ bde ba’i gźi’i bye brag gis rnam pa gñis su gźag ste, ’khor ba daṅ mya ṅan las ’das pa’o. de la chos gaṅ sdug bsṅal gyi gźir gyur pa rnams ni ’khor ba źes bya ste, ’di ltar ’khor ba źes bya ba ni sdug bsṅal gsum daṅ brgyad la sogs pa sdug bsṅal dpag tu med pa’i rten du gyur pa’i phyir ro. bde ba’i gźir gyur pa ni mya ṅan las ’das pa ste, mya ṅan las ’das pa ni ’jig rten daṅ ’jig rten las ’das pa’i bde ba thams cad daṅ ldan pa’i phyir ro.


theg pa tha dad pa daṅ, sems can tha dad pa daṅ, źiṅ tha dad pa daṅ, saṅs rgyas tha dad pa daṅ, chos tha dad pa daṅ, dge ’dun tha dad pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa nas tha dad pa thams cad kyi bar daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so;

na ca yānanānātvasattvanānātvakṣetranānātvabuddhanānātvadharmanānātvasaṃghanānātvena sārdhaṃ saṃvasati, yāvan na sarvanānātvena sārdhaṃ saṃvasati.

16) It does not stay with difference in religious ways, difference of living beings, difference of buddha-lands, difference of Buddhas, difference of teachings or difference of congregations, as it does not stay with difference of anything.

theg pa tha dad pa daṅ, sems can tha dad pa daṅ źes bya ba la sogs pas tha dad pa thams cad daṅ ma ’dres pa bstan te, de la ñan thos kyi theg pa źe’am, raṅ saṅs rgyas kyi theg pa źe’am, theg pa chen po źes bya ba la sogs pa ni theg pa tha dad pa’o; lha źe’am, mi źe’am, bud med ces bya ba la sogs pa ni sems can tha dad pa’o; dga’ ba can gyi saṅs rgyas kyi źiṅ źe’am, padmo can gyi saṅs rgyas kyi źiṅ źes bya ba la sogs pa ni źiṅ tha dad pa’o; ’od dpag med ce’am, mi ’khrugs pa źe’am, śākya thub pa źes bya ba la sogs pa ni saṅs rgyas tha dad pa’o; sa bcu źe’am, sdoṅ po brgyan pa źe’am, laṅ kar gśegs pa źes bya ba ni chos tha dad pa’o; ’di ni ñan thos kyi dge ’dun, ’di ni raṅ saṅs rgyas kyi dge ’dun, ’di ni byaṅ chub sems dpa’i dge ’dun źe’am, ’di ni sems daṅ po bskyed pa’i byaṅ chub sems dpa’, ’di ni mos pas spyod pa’i byaṅ chub sems dpa’, ’di ni mthoṅ ba’i lam la źugs pa’i byaṅ chub sems dpa’ źes bya ba la sogs pa ni dge ’dun tha dad pa’o.


mi śes pa daṅ śes pa daṅ rnam par śes pa daṅ, kun rdzob daṅ don dam pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa nas mtshan ma yid la byed pa thams cad kyi bar daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so.

na cājñānajñānavijñānasaṃvṛtiparamārthena sārdhaṃ saṃvasati, yāvan na sarvanimittamanasikāreṇa sārdhaṃ saṃvasati.

17) It does not stay with ignorance or knowledge, consciousness, concealed truth or the highest truth, as it does not stay with mental effort concerned with any distinguishing marks.

mi śes pa daṅ śes pa daṅ źes bya ba la sogs pas mtshan ma yid la byed pa rnams daṅ ma ’dres pa bstan te; de la mi śes pa ni ma rig pa ste, rtag pa daṅ, gtsaṅ ba daṅ, bdag daṅ, bde bar ’dzin pa’o; śes pa ni rig pa ste, mi rtag pa daṅ, bdag med pa daṅ, mi gtsaṅ ba daṅ, sdug bsṅal bar ’dzin pa’o; rnam pa sna tshogs su śes pa ni rnam par śes pa ste, gzugs su śes pa daṅ, sgrar śes pa nas chos su śes pa’i bar du yin pas mig la sogs pa’i rnam par śes pa rnams so; brjod du yod ciṅ bsam du yod pa rnams ni kun rdzob bo; de las bzlog pa ni don dam pa ste, brjod pa daṅ bsam pas thog tu mi phebs pa’o; mtshan ma yid la byed pa thams cad kyi bar daṅ lhan cig mi gnas źes bya ba ni mtshan ma yid la byed pa goṅ du bśad pa de rnams daṅ lhan cig mi gnas par ma zad kyi, gźan yaṅ yod pa daṅ med pa źes bya ba daṅ, rtag pa daṅ mi rtag pa la sogs pa’i mtshan ma rnams yid la byed pa daṅ yaṅ lhan cig mi gnas so źes bya ba’i don to.


śes rab ni rgyu ba med pa, lus med pa, mtshan ñid med pa, mtshan ma med pa, ’dus ma byas pa ste;de ni mtshan ma daṅ yid la byed pa thams cad daṅ, sems daṅ, yid daṅ, rnam par śes pa daṅ, gnas daṅ, miṅ daṅ, mtshan ma daṅ, gcig pa daṅ, tha dad pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas te; btsun pa śa ra dva ti’i bu, śes rab ni ’grogs pa bcu drug po de dag daṅ lhan cig mi gnas so.

prajñā tv apracārāśarīrālakṣaṇānaimittāsaṃskṛtā,sā tu na sarvanimittamanasikāreṇa cittena manasā vijñānena cāśrayena ca namnā ca nimittena caikatvena nānātvena ca sārdhaṃ saṃvasati; prajñā, bhadanta śāradavatīputra, na taiḥ ṣoḍaśadharmaiḥ sārdhaṃ saṃvasati.

Insight is beyond roaming about [among the objects of perception], it has no body [as basis], no characteristics, no distinguishing marks, it is unconditioned,[and, to summarize what is the essence of insight (prajñāsvabhāva), after having explained it extensively: That insight giving up all distinguishing marks (nimitta) being beyond thought-constructions (nirvikalpa) ] does not stay with either mental effort concerned with distinguishing marks, or with thought, mind or consciousness, with bases [or sense-organs (indriya) ], names or distinguishing marks, or with oneness or plurality; insight, reverend Śāradvatīputra, does not stay in the company of those sixteen things.

śes rab ni rgyu ba med pa, lus med pa źes bya ba la sogs pas goṅ du smos pa lta bu’i tshul gyis mtshan ma thams cad spaṅs pa’i raṅ bźin cis kyaṅ ma gos par rnam par mi rtog pa’i raṅ bźin ñid bstan te, goṅ du smos pa’i śes rab ni źes bya ba’i tha tshig go. gaṅ rgyu ba med pa’i źes bya ba la gzuṅ ba daṅ ’dzin pa’i mtshan mar ’du śes pa ni rgyu ba’o; śes rab des gzuṅ ba daṅ ’dzin par ’du śes thams cad spaṅs pas gzuṅ ba daṅ ’dzin pa’i mtshan mar ’du śes pa’i rgyu med pas na rgyu ba med pa źes bya’o; chos gźan gyi gźi daṅ rten kyaṅ ma yin la, gźan la yaṅ mi rten pas na lus med pa’o; kun rdzob tu śes rab kyi mtshan ñid chos rab tu rnam par ’byed pa lta bu yaṅ ma yin źiṅ, de lta bur yaṅ mi gnas pas na mtshan ñid med pa’o; śes rab kyi yul rnam pa brgyad po ’og nas bśad la sogs pa gaṅ la yaṅ mtshan mar mi ’dzin pas na mtshan ma med pa’o.śes rab kyi raṅ bźin rgyas par bśad nas bsdus te bstan pa’i phyir de ni mtshan ma daṅ yid la byed pa thams cad daṅ źes bya ba la sogs pa smos te, mtshan ma thams cad spaṅs pa rnam par mi rtog pa’i raṅ bźin gyi śes rab de ni źes bya ba’i don to, lhan cig mi gnas pa’i sgra thams cad daṅ yaṅ sbyar te, mtshan ma yid la byed pa thams cad daṅ lhan cig mi gnas, sems daṅ lhan cig mi gnas, yid daṅ lhan cig mi gnas źes bya ba’i don to; de la zag pa daṅ bcas pa daṅ zag pa med pa’i mtshan ñid du yid la byed pa thams cad daṅ ma ’dres pas na mtshan ma yid la byed pa thams cad daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa źes bya’o.
dge ba daṅ mi dge ba’i bag chags rnam pa sna tshogs bsags pa rnam par smin pa’i ’bras bu len par byed pa’i kun gźi rnam par śes pa daṅ ma ’dres pas na sems daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa źes bya’o; ṅa daṅ ṅa’i źes rlom sems pa bdag rgyal ba daṅ bdag la chags pa la sogs pa ñon moṅs pa bźi daṅ lhan cig pa’i ñon moṅs pa’i yid daṅ ma ’bags pas na yid daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa źes bya’o; gzugs la sogs pa’i yul rnams la dmigs par byed pa, kun gźi rnam par śes pa la brten pa’i mig la sogs pa ’jug pa’i rnam par śes pa daṅ ma ’dres pas na rnam par śes pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa źes bya’o. citta (1), manas (2) and vijñāna (3) are thus defined according to Yogācāra doctrine as ālayavijñāna (1); kliṣṭamanas, the mind full of vices, of conceit concerned with me and mine (ahaṃ mameti mānaḥ) (2); and the six vijñāna resulting from sense-perception (3).
gnas ni mig gi rnam par śes pa’i rten mig gi dbaṅ po nas yid kyi rnam par śes pa’i rten yid kyi dbaṅ po’i bar du dbaṅ po rnams so. dbaṅ po de rnams la mi brten pas na gnas daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa’o.
miṅ ni gzugs daṅ sgra daṅ dri daṅ ro źes bya ba daṅ, mig daṅ rna ba źes bya ba daṅ, ’khor ba daṅ mya ṅan las ’das pa źes bya ba daṅ, lha sbyin daṅ mchod sbyin la sogs pa tha sñad du btags pa ste, de dag daṅ ma ’bags pas na miṅ daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa’o. gzugs daṅ sgra la sogs pa dmigs pa’i yul rnams ni mtshan ma źes bya ste, de dag daṅ ma ’dres pas na mtshan ma daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa’o.
chos can daṅ chos ñid daṅ, kun rdzob daṅ don dam pa daṅ, zag pa daṅ bcas pa daṅ zag pa med pa daṅ, ’dus byas daṅ ’dus ma byas rnams, de bźin ñid daṅ gźan par ’dod pa ni gcig pa daṅ tha dad pa ste, de lta bu’i spros pa daṅ ma ’dres pas na gcig pa daṅ tha dad pa daṅ lhan cig mi gnas pa źes bya’o – "Characterized by moments of existence (dharmin) and the real nature of things (dharmatā), concealed truth (saṃvṛtisatya) and the highest truth (paramārtha), sullied (sāsrava) and unsullied (anāsrava), conditioned (saṃskṛta) and unconditioned (asaṃskṛta), things thus as they really are (tathatā) and wishing them to be otherwise (anyakāmatā) is oneness and plurality. Since (insight) is not polluted by such discursive thinking (prapañca) it is said ’it does not stay with oneness or plurality’."


bam po bźi pa:
f) de la śes rab kyi yul gaṅ źe na?’di lta ste: chos brgyad la mkhas pa’o.de la chos brgyad la mkhas pa gaṅ źe na?

tatra katamaḥ prajñāyā viṣayaḥ?tad yathāṣṭau dharmakauśalyāni.tatra katamāny aṣṭau dharmakauśalyāni?

(p. 68)f) [Thus the essence of insight (prajñāsvabhāva) has been explained, then comes the range of its action:]What then is the range of insight [viz. the objects (ālambana) of, or things (vastu) to be understood by insight]?Skills with eight things.What then are the skills with eight things?

de ltar śes rab kyi raṅ bźin bśad nas, de’i yul bstan pa’i phyir de la śes rab kyi yul gaṅ źe na źes bya ba la sogs pa smos so.de la źes bya ba’i don ni gźan las dgar ba’am mgo draṅ bar lta’o. śes rab kyi yul gaṅ źe na źes bya ba ni dris pa ste, śes rab kyis dmigs par bya ba’am, śes rab kyis khoṅ du chud par bya ba’i dṅos po gaṅ źe na źes bya ba’i don to.


’di lta ste: phuṅ po la mkhas pa daṅ;khams la mkhas pa daṅ;skye mched la mkhas pa daṅ;bden pa la mkhas pa daṅ;rten ciṅ ’brel bar ’byuṅ ba la mkhas pa daṅ;dus gsum la mkhas pa daṅ;theg pa thams cad la mkhas pa daṅ;chos thams cad la mkhas pa’o.

tad yathā skandhakauśalyaṃ;dhātukauśalyam;āyatanakauśalyaṃ;satyakauśalyaṃ;pratītyasamutpādakauśalyaṃ;trikālakauśalyaṃ;sarvayānakauśalyaṃ;sarvadharmakauśalyam.

1) Skill with the parts of personality;2) skill with spheres;3) skill with fields;4) skill with truth;5) skill with dependent origination;6) skill with the three times;7) skill with all ways of religious development;8) skill with all moments of existence.

dris pa la lan gdab pa’i phyir ’di lta ste: chos brgyad la mkhas pa’o źes bya ba smos te, ’di lta ste źes bya ba ni tshig mgo draṅ ba daṅ tshig gi rgyan du bya ba’o; chos brgyad khoṅ du chud ciṅ rtogs pa ni chos brgyad la mkhas pa ste, de bas na chos brgyad ni śes rab kyi yul lo, de’aṅ bstan pa daṅ bśad pa lta bur rig par bya’o. de la bstan pa las brtsams na chos brgyad la mkhas pa gaṅ źe na? ’di lta ste: phuṅ po la mkhas pa daṅ, khams la mkhas pa daṅ źes bya ba la sogs pa smos so, bśad pa las brtsams nas gsuṅs pa de la byaṅ chub sems dpa’i phuṅ po la mkhas pa gaṅ źe na źes bya ba la sogs pa’o. yaṅ na graṅs daṅ, miṅ daṅ, dpe daṅ, rab tu dbye ba bstan pa’i phyir de la śes rab kyi yul gaṅ źe na źes bya ba la sogs pa smos so, ’di lta ste: chos brgyad la mkhas pa’o źes bya bas ni graṅs bstan te, chos brgyad la mkhas pa gaṅ źe na? ’di lta ste: phuṅ po la mkhas pa źes bya ba la sogs pas miṅ bstan to.
Cf. Bbh. p. 3311-13: prajñāyāṃ yogaṃ karoti skandhakauśalyaṃ vā karoti dhātukauśalyam āyatanakauśalyaṃ pratītyasamutpādakauśalyam ...; Śbh p. 194,2-4 et seq., e. g. p. 2481 and note 1; Pratyekabuddhabhūmi p. 3317-19, 24-26, 341-2.


de la byaṅ chub sems dpa’i phuṅ po la mkhas pa gaṅ źe na?

tatra katamad bodhisattvasya skandhakauślyam?

1) What then is the bodhisattva’s skill with the parts of personality [that is, understanding their essential characteristics (lakṣaṇa) and essence (svabhāva) ]?

de la byaṅ chub sems dpa’i phuṅ po la mkhas pa gaṅ źe na? ’di phuṅ po rnams kyi dper bya ba bstan pa ste, dbu ba rdos pa bstan pa daṅ źes bya ba la sogs pas dpe bstan to; de ci’i phyir źe na? gzugs ni dbu ba rdos pa lta bu ste źes bya ba la sogs pas ni rab tu dbye ba bstan to. de la źes bya ba ni dgar ba’i tshig ste, mkhas pa rnam pa brgyad pos bkar te, phuṅ po la mkhas pa de bstan par ’dod pa’o. de la phuṅ po’i don ni gaṅ cuṅ zad gzugs ’das pa daṅ, ma ’oṅs pa daṅ, da ltar gyi daṅ, naṅ gi daṅ, phyi’i daṅ, rags pa daṅ, phra ba daṅ, ṅan pa daṅ, bzaṅ po daṅ, ñe ba daṅ, riṅ ba de dag thams cad gcig tu bsdus nas bstan pa ni phuṅ po źes bya’o, phuṅ po de la mkhas pa ni phuṅ po la mkhas pa ste, phuṅ po’i mtshan ñid daṅ raṅ bźin gaṅ yin pa rtogs pa’o. ji ltar phuṅ po’i mtshan ñid rtogs par ’gyur źe na? de bstan pa’i phyir gsuṅs pa gaṅ phuṅ po rnams kyi dper bya ba bstan pa ste, dbu ba rdos pa bstan pa daṅ źes bya ba la sogs pa’o. ’di źes bya ni dpe rnams la sñegs so. phuṅ po’i raṅ bźin gaṅ yin pa de daṅ mthun pa’i dper gźag pa ni phuṅ po rnams kyi dper bya ba bstan pa źes bya ste, dpe yaṅ dbu ba rdos pa bstan pa la sogs pa rnam pa bcu’o. dpe rnam pa bcu po de rnams kyaṅ don rnam pa bcu’i dbaṅ du byas nas gsuṅs par rig par bya ste, 1) bdag rtag pa med pa’i don daṅ, 2) bdag med ciṅ gtsaṅ ba’i don spaṅs pa’i don daṅ, 3) bdag med ciṅ mnog chuṅ ba’i don daṅ, 4) sñiṅ po med pa’i don daṅ, 5) mi brtan pa’i don daṅ, 6) don med pa dag kyaṅ spyod yul du gyur źiṅ yid du ’oṅ ba daṅ yid du mi ’oṅ ba’i kun tu loṅs spyod pa med pa’i don daṅ, 7) dṅos po med kyaṅ tha sñad daṅ smra ba sna tshogs byed pa’i don daṅ, 8) don med kyaṅ rnam par śes pa sna tshogs su ’jug pa’i don daṅ, 9) don med par yaṅ dag pa ’dzin pa rnams kyi tiṅ ṅe ’dzin gyi spyod yul du gyur pa’i don daṅ, 10) don med kyaṅ byaṅ chub sems dpa’ rnams bsam pa phyin ci ma log pas sems can thams cad kyi bya ba bsgrub pa’i phyir skye ba len pa’i don to. The ten similes are treated in Mppś pp. 357-87, where also much comparative material is given by Lamotte.


gaṅ ’di phuṅ po rnams kyi dper bya bar bstan pa ste:dbu ba rdos par bstan pa daṅ,chu’i chu bur du bstan pa daṅ,smig rgyur bstan pa daṅ,chu śiṅ gi sdoṅ por bstan pa daṅ,sgyu mar bstan pa daṅ,rmi lam du bstan pa daṅ,brag car bstan pa daṅ,mig yor du bstan pa daṅ,gzugs brñan du bstan pa daṅ,sprul par bstan pa’o.

yad idaṃ skandhānām udāharaṇanidarśanaṃphenapiṇḍanidarśanaṃ;budbudanidarśanaṃ;marīcinidarśanaṃ;kadalīdrumanidarśanaṃ;māyānidarśanaṃ;svapnanidarśanaṃ;pratiśrutkānidarśanaṃ;pratibhāsanidarśanaṃ;pratibimbanidarśanaṃ;nirmitanidarśanaṃ.

Pointing them out with allegories;pointing them out with [the allegory of] lumps of foam;pointing them out with bubbles;pointing them out with a mirage;pointing them out with the trunk of the plantain tree;pointing them out with illusion;pointing them out with a dream;pointing them out with an echo;pointing them out with a shadow figure;pointing them out with a reflected image;pointing them out with a magical creation.




de ci’i phyir źe na?

tat kasya hetoḥ?

Why?

dper gźag pa de dag gi don bstan pa’i phyir de ci’i phyir źe na źes bya ba la sogs pa smos so, de ci’i phyir źe na źes bya ba ni dpe bcu po de dag ji ltar na phuṅ po’i dper ’gyur źe’am, phuṅ po rnams ci’i phyir dpe de daṅ ’dra bar bstan ces bya ba’i don to.


gzugs ni dbu ba rdos pa lta bu ste; dbu ba rdos pa lta bu ni bdag ma yin, sems can ma yin, srog ma yin, gso ba ma yin, skyes bu ma yin, gaṅ zag ma yin no. dbu ba rdos pa’i raṅ bźin gaṅ yin pa, gzugs kyi raṅ bźin yaṅ de yin te; gaṅ ’di la mkhas pa, de ni phuṅ po la mkhas pa źes bya’o.

rūpaṃ phenapiṇḍopamaṃ, phenapiṇḍopamaṃ tu nātmā na sattvo na jīvo na poṣo na puruṣo na pudgalaḥ, yaḥ phenapiṇḍasya svabhāvaḥ so rūpasyāpi svabhāvaḥ, yad atra kauśalyaṃ tat skandhakauśalyam.

Form is like a lump of foam, and what is like a lump of foam cannot be a self, an animated being, a life-principle, a life-sustaining principle, a spirit or personality; the essence of a lump of foam is also the essence of form. Skill in this is skill with the parts of personality.

phuṅ po rnams dpe daṅ mtshan ñid ’dra bar bstan pa’i phyir gzugs ni dbu ba rdos pa lta bu ste źes bya ba la sogs pa smos so. ’dir phuṅ po’i sgra ma smos su zin kyaṅ phuṅ po ñid bśad pa gleṅ ba’i skabs yin pas gzugs kyaṅ phuṅ po źes bya bar draṅs te, gzugs la sogs pa’i yul lṅa daṅ, mig la sogs pa’i dbaṅ po lṅa la sogs pa ni gzugs kyi phuṅ po źes bya’o. gzugs kyi phuṅ po de ni dbu ba rdos pa daṅ ’dra ste, ci’i phyir źe na? bdag rtag pa med pa’i phyir ro, don de ñid bstan pa’i phyir dbu ba rdos pa ni bdag ma yin, sems can ma yin źes bya ba la sogs pa smos te, ’di lta ste, skyes bu la la źig gis chu bo chen po la śel lta bu kha dog daṅ dbyibs su ldan pa’i dbu ba rdos pa maṅ po rgyu ba maṅ po mthoṅ ba daṅ, de dag la sñiṅ po daṅ raṅ bźin yod du re nas lag pa gñis kyis ’dzin ciṅ, blaṅ bar brgal na med par gyur pa daṅ: kye ma ’di go dbu ba rdos pa ste, gsog gsob ṅo bo ñid med do, sñam mo – "... In this way: In the great sea some people see the foam tossed about with form and colour like crystals (yathāsphaṭikavarṇasaṃsthāna). Thinking that it has substance (sāra) and essence (svabhāva) they grasp for it with the hands, but it flies away and comes to nought: ‘Oh, this is only foam, it is worthless (tucchaka), vain (riktaka) without essence (niḥsvabhāva),’ they say."
de bas na dbu ba rdos pa ni bdag gi raṅ bźin ma yin pas na gaṅ zag gi bar gyi raṅ bźin ma yin par śes so, dbu ba rdos pa’i raṅ bźin gaṅ yin pa, gzugs kyi raṅ bźin yaṅ de yin te źes bya ba ni dbu ba rdos pa’i raṅ bźin bdag med ciṅ dṅos po med pa gsog daṅ gsob tu gyur pa gaṅ yin pa gzugs kyi phuṅ po’i raṅ bźin yaṅ de yin te, gzugs kyi phuṅ po la ye śes kyi mig daṅ ldan pas bltas śiṅ brtags te, źib mor gźigs na bdag daṅ raṅ bźin med ciṅ gsog gsob stoṅ pa’i mtshan ñid du gnas pa’i phyir ro.


tshor ba ni chu’i chu bur lta bu’o;’du śes ni smig rgyu lta bu’o;’du byed rnams ni chu śiṅ lta bu’o;rnam par śes pa ni sgyu ma lta bu ste;sgyu ma yaṅ bdag ma yin, sems can ma yin, srog ma yin, gso ba ma yin, skyes bu ma yin, gaṅ zag ma yin no. sgyu ma’i raṅ bźin gaṅ yin pa, rnam par śes pa’i raṅ bźin yaṅ de yin te;gaṅ ’di la mkhas pa, de ni byaṅ chub sems dpa’i phuṅ po la mkhas pa źes bya’o.phuṅ po rnams ni rmi lam lta bu ste; rmi lam yaṅ bdag ma yin, sems can ma yin, srog ma yin, gso ba ma yin, skyes bu ma yin, gaṅ zag ma yin no. rmi lam gyi raṅ bźin gaṅ yin pa, phuṅ po rnams kyi raṅ bźin yaṅ de yin te; gaṅ ’di la mkhas pa, de ni byaṅ chub sems dpa’i phuṅ po la mkhas pa źes bya’o.

vedanā budbudopamā,saṃjñā marīcyupamā,saṃskāraḥ kadalyupamo,vijñānaṃ māyopamaṃ,māyā ca nātmā na sattvo na jīvo na poṣo na puruṣo na pudgalaḥ, yo māyāyāḥ svabhāvaḥ so vijñānasyāpi svabhāvaḥ.yad atra kauśalyaṃ tad bodhisattvasya skandhakauśalyam.skandhāḥ svapnopamāḥ svapnaś ca nātmā na sattvo na jīvo na poṣo na puruṣo na pudgalaḥ, yaḥ svapnasya svabhāvaḥ sa skandhānām api svabhāvaḥ, yad atra kauśalyaṃ tad bodhisattvasya skandhakauśalyam.

Feelings are like bubbles,perception like a mirage,formative factors like the plantain tree,consciousness like an illusion,and an illusion cannot be a self, an animated being, a life-principle, a life-sustaining principle, a spirit or personality; the essence of an illusion is also the essence of consciousness.Skill in this is the bodhisattva’s skill with the parts of personality.The parts of personality are like a dream, and a dream cannot be a self, an animated being, a life-principle, a life-sustaining principle, a spirit or personality; the essence of a dream is also the essence of the parts of personality. Skill in this is the bodhisattva’s skill with the parts of personality.

tshor ba ni chu’i chu bur lta bu źes bya ba la bde ba daṅ, sdug bsṅal daṅ, bde ba yaṅ ma yin sdug bsṅal ba yaṅ ma yin par rnam pa gsum myoṅ ba ni tshor ba ste, ’dir yaṅ phuṅ po źes bya bar sbyar ro; tshor ba’i phuṅ po ni chu’i chu bur daṅ ’dra ste. de ci’i phyir źe na? bdag med ciṅ gtsaṅ ba spaṅs pa’i phyir ro.
’di ltar sems can la la źig gis chu’i naṅ du char bab ste, chu’i chu bur śel gyi nor bu daṅ ’dra bar rnam pa sna tshogs su ’byuṅ ba mthoṅ ba daṅ, de dag rdzas su ruṅ źiṅ rgyan du ruṅ de re nas lag pa gñis kyis ’dzin ciṅ blaṅ bar bśams na med par gyur ciṅ, ma bzuṅ ba’i rnams kyaṅ skyes ma thag tu ’gag ste. rdzas su ruṅ bar ma mthoṅ nas: kye ma ’di go chu’i chu bur te, bdag med pa raṅ bźin med par gsog gsob yin par śes so. de bźin du bde ba daṅ sdug bsṅal la sogs pa’i tshor ba’i phuṅ po la ye śes kyi mig daṅ lag pas bltas śiṅ yod pa daṅ med pa la sogs pa rnam par dpyod na chu’i chu bur daṅ ’dra bar bdag daṅ raṅ bźin med ciṅ gsog daṅ gsob yin pa daṅ, thams cad kyaṅ sdug bsṅal gyi mtshan ñid ’gyur ba daṅ skyes ma thag tu ’jig pa’i raṅ bźin yin par mthoṅ ṅo – "When rain falls into the water, some people see the bubbles as if different kinds of crystal-gems (sphaṭikamaṇi) were originating. Thinking they are substances (dravya) and fit for ornaments they grasp for them with their hands to arrange them, they come to nought, even the ones which are not grasped for burst as soon as they originate. Seeing that they are not substances they learn: ‘Oh, these are bubbles, without self (anātma), without essence (niḥsvabhāva), worthless and vain.’ Thus also the part of personality of feeling, pleasant and unpleasant, etc., is without self and without essence, worthless and vain just like bubbles; grasped with the eyes and hands of wisdom, examined if existent or non-existent, one sees that they are all characterized by suffering (duḥkhalakṣaṇa), having the essence of perishing as soon as they originate."’du śes ni smig rgyu lta bu’o źes bya ba la yul na mtshan mar ’dzin pa ni ’du śes te, yul ni gzugs daṅ sgra la sogs pa’o; mtshan ma ni dkar po daṅ dmar po la sogs pa’o; ’dzin pa ni de ni dkar po ñid yin gyi dmar po ma yin no, źes gcod pa ste. ’du śes kyi phuṅ po ni smig rgyu daṅ ’dra ste, ci’i phyir źe na? bdag med ciṅ mnog chuṅ ba’i phyir ro. ’di lta ste: chu ’dod pa’i skyes bu la la źig dpyid kyi dus na ñi ma’i ’od kyis gduṅs te, smig rgyu ba sna tshogs chu rlabs lta bu mig gis mthoṅ ba daṅ: de dag la chu yin, sñam nas btuṅ bar bya ba’i phyir druṅ du brgyags te btags na chu ma yin par mthoṅ nas: kye ma’o, ’di go smyig rgyu ba ste, bdag med pa gsog gsob ṅo bo ñid med pa źes sems pa, de bźin du log pa sna tshogs kyi rnam par rtog pa maṅ po’i ’du śes kyi phuṅ po la ye śes kyi mig gis bltas te – "... Perception is grasping the distinguishing marks of objects (viṣaye nimittodgrahaṇaṃ saṃjñā), objects are form, sound, etc., distinguishing marks (nimitta) are white and red and so on, grasping is deciding: ‘This is white, not red’. The part of personality perception is like a mirage – why? It is without self and trifling. Thirsty people tormented by the sunlight in summertime see mirages as billows of water with their eyes, and thinking it is water they run to drink. Having discovered it is not, they think: ‘Oh, this is a mirage, without self, worthless and vain, without essence.’ Thus, with the eyes of wisdom (jñānacakṣur) they also see perception, full of thought-constructions (vikalpa) concerned with misunderstandings."
yod pa daṅ med pa la sogs par yaṅ dag par brtags na bdag med pa daṅ dṅos po med par mthoṅ ste, de bas na ’du śes kyaṅ smig rgyu ba bźin du bdag gi raṅ bźin ma yin pas na gaṅ zag gi raṅ bźin ma yin pa’i bar du’o.’du byed rnams ni chu śiṅ lta bu’o źes bya ba la las dge ba daṅ mi dge ba daṅ luṅ du ma bstan pa rnams sna tshogs byed pa ni ’du byed de, de yaṅ ’du byed kyi tshogs rnam pa maṅ po rnams so. ’du byed kyi phuṅ po rnams ni chu śiṅ daṅ ’dra ste, ci’i phyir źe na? sñiṅ po med pa’i phyir ro. ’di lta ste: śiṅ gi sñiṅ po sra ba ’dod pa’i skyes bu la la źig gis chu śiṅ bcad de ’dab ma nas mthar gyis rnam par bśus nas de la mig gis bltas te sñiṅ po yod dam źes brtags na, sñiṅ po yod par ma mthoṅ nas: kye ma’o, ’di go chu śiṅ gi sñiṅ po ste, stoṅ pa dṅos po daṅ raṅ bźin med pa’o, źes sems pa, de bźin du dge ba daṅ mi dge ba daṅ luṅ du mi bstan pa la sogs pa ’du byed kyi phuṅ po rnam pa sna tshogs pa la dam pa daṅ sñiṅ po yod du re ste, śes rab kyi mig gis kun tu bltas nas yod pa daṅ med pa daṅ, gcig daṅ du ma daṅ, bdag daṅ pha rol daṅ gñis ka’i sbyor bas yaṅ dag par brtags na sems tsam daṅ ma skyes pa daṅ yod pa daṅ med pa las ’das pa sñiṅ po med pa chu śiṅ bźin du bdag gi raṅ bźin daṅ bral ba mthoṅ ṅo – "... Formative factors create the different kinds of good, bad and neutral, the multitudes of formative factors are many. The part of personality of formative factors is like the plantain tree. Why? It is without a core (asāra). People who want a hard (dṛḍhasāra) tree and cut down a plantain tree, stripping the bark off it from top to bottom, see that there is no core (sāra) when examining it in this respect: ‘Oh, this has the core of a plantain tree (kadalīsāra), empty, no substance, no essence.’ Thus also the part of personality of different formative factors, concerned with good, bad, neutral, etc.: reflecting on the existence of a principle or a core (sāra), one sees, having viewed it with the eyes of insight (prajñācakṣur), that it is only thought (cittamātra), unborn (anutpanna), beyond being and non-being (bhavābhavasamatikrānta), without a core (asāra) just like the plantain tree, and without the essence of a self (ātmasvabhāvarahita), having thus reflected with effort concerned with the duality of existence and non-existence, one and many, self and others."rnam par śes pa ni sgyu ma lta bu źes bya ba la gzugs la sogs pa’i yul rnams śes pa ni rnam par śes pa ste, de’aṅ mig la sogs pa’i rnam par śes pa brgyad do. rnam par śes pa’i phuṅ po ni sgyu ma daṅ ’dra ste; ci’i phyir źe na? mi brtan pa’i phyir ro. ’di lta ste: skyes bu sgrin po źig gis sgyu ma’i cha lugs kyi bzo bos lha daṅ, mi daṅ gnod sbyin daṅ, dud ’gro’i gzugs sna tshogs kyi sgyu ma rnams sprul pa de dag la mig gis kyaṅ kun du lta źiṅ, raṅ bźin daṅ rgyun du gnas par re nas brtags na, raṅ bźin med ciṅ de ma thag tu ’jig pa yin par mthoṅ nas: kye ma, ’di go sgyu ma ste, stoṅ pa raṅ bźin med pa’o, źes sems pa, de bźin du las kyi bag chags sna tshogs kyis bsgyur ba’i rnam par śes pa’i phuṅ po la śes rab kyi mig gis raṅ bźin daṅ rgyun du gnas par re nas, gcig daṅ du ma’i ṅo bos brtags na, sgyu ma bźin du stoṅ pa ṅo bo ñid med pa skad cig ma re re la ’jig par mthoṅ ṅo – "... Knowing the objects, form, etc., is consciousness (rūpādiviṣaye jñānaṃ vijñānam), it is the eight consciousnesses pertaining to the eye, etc., (cakṣurādivijñānāny aṣṭavijñānāni). The part of personality of consciousness is like a magical creation (vijñānaskandho māyopamaḥ). Why? It is not substantial (adṛḍhatvāt). A cunning man may create various illusory forms of gods, men, demons and animals with the art of magic of illusions. But though they are seen with the eyes, if one examines them hoping they have own being (svabhāva) and continued existence (prabandhasthiti), you see that they have no own being (niḥsvabhāva), they perish at once: ‘Oh, this is only an illusion (māyā), empty (śūnya), without own being (niḥsvabhāva),’ one thinks. In the same way, if one examines with the eye of insight, with a view to the individual and general own-being, the part of personality of consciousness (vijñānaskandha), which is created by the different habits of action (karmavāsanā), hoping it has own being and continued existence, one sees that it perishes each moment (kṣaṇa) like an illusion (māyopama), empty (śūnya) and without own being (niḥsvabhāva)."phuṅ po rnams ni rmi lam lta bu ste źes bya ba la goṅ du bśad pa’i phuṅ po de dag ñid ni yaṅ rmi lam daṅ ’dra ste, ci’i phyir źe na? don med pa dag kyaṅ spyod yul du ’gyur źiṅ yid du ’oṅ ba daṅ yid du mi ’oṅ ba kun du loṅs spyod par byed pa’i phyir ro. ’di ltar rnam par śes pa rnams yul la ’jug par mi nus te, gñid kyis log pas na rtog pa sna tshogs kyi rgyu ba ’byuṅ ba ni rmi lam mo. dper na rmi lam bdag gi raṅ bźin ma yin pa nas gaṅ zag gi bar gyi raṅ bźin ma yin te, dṅos po med kyaṅ dga’ ba daṅ mi dga’ bar ’gyur ba’i yul mthoṅ ba’i tshe dga’ ba daṅ mi dga’ ba’i sems rnam pa sna tshogs skye bar ’gyur ro. de bźin du phuṅ po rnams kyaṅ bdag gi raṅ bźin ma yin pas na gaṅ zag gi bar gyi raṅ bźin ma yin te, dṅos po med mod kyi las dge ba daṅ mi dge ba rnam pa sna tshogs kyi rgyus mtho ris daṅ ṅan soṅ gi bde ba daṅ sdug bsṅal rnams skye bar ’gyur ro – "... The parts of personality mentioned above are like a dream (svapna). Why? Even though it is without real meaning (or objective counterpart, anartha), it becomes a sphere of objects (viṣaya) causing all kinds of pleasant and unpleasant experience. Consciousness (vijñāna) is not able to enter the [outer] sphere of objects (viṣaya), dream is the appearance of activity of different kinds of thought-constructions (vividhakalpanāpracāra) because of sleep (suptatvāt). Dream has no own being as a self (ātmasvabhāva), as it has no own being as a person (pudgalasvabhāva), but even though it is inexistent (abhāva), it creates different kinds of happy and unhappy thoughts (citta) when it sees the happy or unhappy spheres (viṣaya). In the same way the parts of personality (skandha) have no own being as a self (ātmasvabhāva), as they have no own being as a person (pudgalasvabhāva), but even though they are inexistent (abhāva), one is born in the states of happiness and suffering of heaven (svarga) and hell (apāya) by the causes of the different good and bad actions (vividhakuśalākuśalakarmahetubhiḥ)."


phuṅ po rnams ni brag ca lta bu ste; brag ca ni bdag ma yin, sems can ma yin, srog ma yin, gso ba ma yin, skyes bu ma yin, gaṅ zag ma yin no. brag ca’i raṅ bźin gaṅ yin pa, phuṅ po rnams kyi raṅ bźin yaṅ de yin te; gaṅ ’di la mkhas pa, de ni byaṅ chub sems dpa’i phuṅ po la mkhas pa źes bya’o.

skandhāḥ pratiśrutkopamāh pratiśrutkā ca nātmā na sattvo na jīvo na poṣo na puruṣo na pudgalaḥ, yaḥ pratiśrutkāyāḥ svabhāvaḥ sa skandhānām api svabhāvaḥ, yad atra kauśalyaṃ tad bodhisattvasya skandhakauśalyam.

The parts of personality are like an echo, and an echo is not a self, an animated being, a life-principle, a life-sustaining principle, a spirit or personality; the essence of an echo is also the essence of the parts of personality. Skill in this is the bodhisattva’s skill with the parts of personality.

phuṅ po rnams ni brag ca lta bu ste źes bya ba ni phuṅ po rnams ni brag ca daṅ ’dra ste, ci’i phyir źe na? dṅos po med kyaṅ tha sñad daṅ smra ba sna tshogs byed pa’i phyir ro. dper na sgra la brag ca’i sgra brñan bdag gi raṅ bźin ma yin pas na gaṅ zag gi bar gyi raṅ bźin yaṅ ma yin te, dṅos po med ciṅ don med kyaṅ sgra rnam pa sna tshogs ’byuṅ ba. de bźin du chos thams cad bdag med de, raṅ bźin gyis źi ba yin mod kyi, ’on kyaṅ sgra brñan daṅ ’dra ba’i miṅ daṅ tshig daṅ tha sñad du brjod pa maṅ po yaṅ yod do – "... The parts of personality are like an echo (pratiśrutkā). Why? Even though it is immaterial (avastuka) it causes different kinds of expressions (vyavahāra) and speech. The resounding (pratiśabda) in the echo has no own being as a self (ātmasvabhāva), as it has no own being as a person (pudgalasvabhāva), but even though it is immaterial (avastuka) and meaningless (anartha), different kinds of sound (śabda) appear. In the same way, though all moments of existence are without a self (anātma) and essentially peaceful (svabhāvena śāntāḥ), they have all kinds of names, words and expressions in utterances which are like the resounding [echo] (pratiśabda)."


phuṅ po rnams ni mig yor lta bu ste; mig yor kyaṅ bdag ma yin, sems can ma yin, srog ma yin, gso ba ma yin, skyes bu ma yin, gaṅ zag ma yin no. mig yor gyi raṅ bźin gaṅ yin pa, phuṅ po rnams kyi raṅ bźin yaṅ de yin te; gaṅ ’di la mkhas pa, de ni byaṅ chub sems dpa’i phuṅ po la mkhas pa źes bya’o.

skandhāḥ pratibhāsopamāḥ pratibhāsaś ca nātmā na sattvo na jīvo na poṣo na puruṣo na pudgalaḥ, yaḥ pratibhāsasya svabhāvaḥ sa skandhānām api svabhāvaḥ, yad atra kauśalyaṃ tad bodhisattvasya skandhakauśalyam.

The parts of personality are like shadow figures, and a shadow figure is not a self, an animated being, a life-principle, a life-sustaining principle, a spirit or personality; the essence of a shadow figure is also the essence of the parts of personality. Skill in this is the bodhisattva’s skill with the parts of personality.

phuṅ po rnams ni mig yor lta bu ste źes bya ba la śog śog gam dar ram ras la ri mo sna tshogs bris nas brgyaṅs te, phub la de’i naṅ du mtshan mo’i me mar bus na gzugs rnam pa sna tshogs snaṅ ba ni mig yor źes bya’o. yaṅ na snaṅ brñan źes bya ste, khaṅ pa’i naṅ gi ñi zer ’od la brten nas gzugs gcig daṅ gñis la sogs par snaṅ ba’o. yaṅ na gźan gnas pa las gźan du snaṅ ba ni mig yor te, dper na sdoṅ po las mi lta bur ’khrul pa’o. phuṅ po rnams ni mig yor daṅ ’dra ste, ci’i phyir źe na? don med kyaṅ mig yor gyi dus na gzugs rnam pa sna tshogs snaṅ ba, de bźin du don med par yaṅ khams gsum gyi sems daṅ sems las byuṅ ba rnam pa sna tshogs skye źiṅ ’byuṅ ṅo – "... A shadow figure is the following: If one draws some figures on a piece of cotton, silk or paper and stretches it out, and then places a lamp behind it in the night, different kinds of forms (rūpa) appear. Or, as a reflection, dependent on the light in a ray of sun in a house, one, two or many forms (rūpa) appear. Or, it is when something appears as something else in another place, as when one mistakes a post for a man. The parts of personality are like a shadow picture. Why? Though without real meaning (or objective counterpart, anartha), different kinds of forms appear at the time the shadow-picture [is produced], in the same way, though without real meaning (or objective counterpart, anartha), the thoughts and mental events (cittacaitta) of the threefold world (traidhātuka) are born."


phuṅ po rnams ni gzugs brñan lta bu ste; gzugs brñan ni bdag ma yin, sems can ma yin, srog ma yin, gso ba ma yin, skyes bu ma yin, gaṅ zag ma yin no. gzugs brñan gyi raṅ bźin gaṅ yin pa, phuṅ po rnams kyi raṅ bźin yaṅ de yin te; gaṅ ’di la mkhas pa, de ni byaṅ chub sems dpa’i phuṅ po la mkhas pa źes bya’o.

skandhāḥ pratibimbopamāḥ pratibimbaś ca nātmā na sattvo na jīvo na poṣo na puruṣo na pudgalaḥ, yaḥ pratibimbasya svabhāvaḥ sa skandhānām api svabhāvaḥ, yad atra kauśalyaṃ tad bodhisattvasya skandhakauśalyam.

The parts of personality are like a reflected image, and a reflected image is not a self, an animated being, a life-principle, a life-sustaining principle, a spirit or personality; the essence of a reflected image is also the essence of the parts of personality. Skill in this is the bodhisattva’s skill with the parts of personality.

phuṅ po rnams ni gzugs brñan lta bu ste źes bya ba la phuṅ po rnams ni gzugs brñan daṅ ’dra ste, ci’i phyir źe na? don med kyaṅ yaṅ dag par ’dzin pa rnams kyi tiṅ ṅe ’dzin gyi spyod yul du ’gyur ba’i phyir ro. dper na chu’i zla ba daṅ me loṅ dag pa’i naṅ du bźin gyi gzugs brñan du snaṅ ba bdag gi raṅ bźin ma yin pa nas gaṅ zag gi bar gyi raṅ bźin ma yin te, dṅos po med du zin yaṅ bltar snaṅ ba tsam yaṅ yod pa, de bźin du tiṅ ṅe ’dzin la sogs pa’i raṅ bźin daṅ rnal ’byor ba’i phuṅ po rnams kyaṅ bdag gi raṅ bźin ma yin pas na gaṅ zag gi bar gyi raṅ bźin ma yin te, dṅos po med ciṅ raṅ bźin mi dmigs mod kyi, ’on kyaṅ rgya mtsho daṅ ’dra ba’i sems mñam par gnas pa las gzugs brñan snaṅ ba bźin rnam par thar pa daṅ, gzugs daṅ, sprul pa la sogs pa rnam pa sna tshogs ’byuṅ źiṅ snaṅ bar yaṅ byed do – "... The parts of personality are like a reflected image (pratibimba). Why? Even though they are without real meaning [or objective counterpart,] they are a field of concentrations (samādhigocara) for those who practise. As the moon reflected in the water (udakacandra) and the reflected image of the face in a pure mirror have no own being as a self (ātmasvabhāva), they have no own being as a person (pudgalasvbhāva), but even though they are not a real thing (avastuka), they are still reflections to be seen; in the same way with the own being of concentration, etc. (samādhyādisvabhāva), the parts of religious effort (yogaskandha) have no own being as a self (ātmasvabhāva), as they have no own being as a person (pudgalasvbhāva), but even though they are not real things (avastuka) and their own being is not apprehended (nopalabhyate), liberation (vimokṣa), form (rūpa) and magical appearances (nirmita) of different kinds come into being and appear like reflected images (pratibimba) from thought (citta) ever the same (samastha) like the sea (samudra)."


phuṅ po rnams ni sprul pa lta bu ste; sprul pa ni bdag ma yin, sems can ma yin, srog ma yin, gso ba ma yin, skyes bu ma yin, gaṅ zag ma yin no. sprul pa’i raṅ bźin gaṅ yin pa, phuṅ po rnams kyi raṅ bźin yaṅ de yin te; gaṅ ’di la mkhas pa, de ni byaṅ chub sems dpa’i phuṅ po la mkhas pa źes bya’o.

skandhā nirmitopamāḥ nirmitaś ca nātmā na sattvo na jīvo na poṣo na puruṣo na pudgalaḥ, yo nirmitasya svabhāvaḥ sa skandhānām api svabhāvaḥ, yad atra kauśalyaṃ tad bodhisattvasya skandhakauśalyam.

The parts of personality are like a magical creation, and a magical creation is not a self, an animated being, (p. 69) a life-principle, a life-sustaining principle, a spirit or personality; the essence of a magical creation is also the essence of the parts of personality. Skill in this is the bodhisattva’s skill with the parts of personality [understanding the essential characteristics (lakṣaṇa) of the parts of personality according to the mentioned similes].

phuṅ po rnams ni sprul pa lta bu ste źes bya ba la phuṅ po rnams ni sprul pa daṅ ’dra ste, ci’i phyir źe na? don med kyaṅ byaṅ chub sems dpa’ rnams bsam pa phyin ci ma log par sems can thams cad kyi bya ba bsgrub pa’i phyir skye ba len par snaṅ bas so. dper na lha daṅ mi la sogs pa’i sprul pa sna tshogs bdag gi raṅ bźin ma yin pa nas gaṅ zag gi bar gyi raṅ bźin ma yin te, dṅos po med mod kyi, ’on kyaṅ gzugs daṅ dbyibs rnam pa sna tshogs snaṅ ba, de bźin du sems can gyi don du byaṅ chub sems dpa’ ’khor bar ’jug pa yaṅ bdag gi raṅ bźin ma yin pa nas gaṅ zag gi bar gyi raṅ bźin ma yin te, dṅos po med mod kyi, ’on kyaṅ skye ba rnam pa sna tshogs ’byuṅ źiṅ skye bar snaṅ ṅo – "... The parts of personality are like a magical creation (nirmita). Why? Even though [the magical creation] is no objective entity (anartha), the bodhisattvas appear [by means of it] seeking birth with good intentions (aviparītāśaya) to complete what all beings have to do. Although the magical apparitions of gods and men have no own being as selves (ātmasvabhāva), etc., and no own being as persons (pudgalasvabhāva), and accordingly are [really] inexistent (abhāva), they appear with colour and form. In the same way the bodhisattvas enter existence (saṃsāra) for the sake of beings, though they have no own being as selves (ātmasvabhāva), etc., and no own being as persons (pudgalasvabhāva), and accordingly are [really] inexistent (abhāva), but they appear as being born in different states of existence.
gaṅ ’di la mkhas pa, de ni byaṅ chub sems dpa’i phuṅ po la mkhas pa źes bya’o źes bya ba la goṅ du phuṅ po dpe bstan pa’i tshul du phuṅ po’i mtshan ñid la mkhas pa’i byaṅ chub sems dpa’ de ni phuṅ po la mkhas pa yin no źes bya ba’i don to.


phuṅ po źes bya ba, de ni ’jig rten te; ’jig rten kyaṅ ’jig pa’i mtshan ñid do.’jig rten gyi raṅ bźin gaṅ yin pa, de raṅ bźin gyis mi rtag pa’o, raṅ bźin gyis sdug bsṅal ba’o, raṅ bźin gyis stoṅ pa’o, raṅ bźin gyis bdag med pa’o, raṅ bźin gyis źi ba ste; gaṅ ’di la mkhas pa, de ni byaṅ chub sems dpa’i phuṅ po la mkhas pa źes bya’o.

skandha iti sa lokaḥ; loko ’pi luglakṣanaḥ,yo lokasvabhāvaḥ, sa svabhāvenānityaḥ, svabhāvena duḥkhaḥ, svabhāvena śūnyaḥ, svabhāvenānātmā, svabhāvena śāntaḥ; yad atra kauśalyaṃ tad bodhisattvasya skandhakauśalyam.

The parts of personality are the world, and the world has the essential characteristic of destruction [as related to the root luj-, the world is characterized by destruction in each moment (kṣaṇa) ],[and thus] the essence [namely the essential characteristic (lakṣaṇa)] of the world is essentially impermanent, essentially suffering, essentially empty, essentially selfless, essentially in peace. Skill in this is the bodhisattva’s skill with the parts of personality.

phuṅ po źes bya ba, de ni ’jig rten te źes bya ba la phuṅ po źes bya ba ni ’jig rten la bya ste, ’jig rten gyi mtshan ñid gaṅ kyaṅ yin źe na? de’i phyir ’jig rten kyaṅ ’jig pa’i mtshan ñid do źes smras te, ’jig rten gyi mtshan ñid ni skad cig ma re re la ’jig pa’i mtshan ñid do.
Cf. Mvy 3061: lujyata iti lokaḥ; Kośa 518-19: lujyata iti lokaḥ (read lujyata for lakṣyata in the text of Kośa, tib. ’jig); Kośavyākhyā 235-10, and PTSD s. v. lujjati, lujjana. Cf. also Aṣṭa p. 53720-53814; Mppś vol. V, p. IX.don de ñid gsal bar bstan pa’i phyir ’jig rten gyi raṅ bźin gaṅ yin pa, de raṅ bźin gyis mi rtag pa’o źes bya ba smos te, raṅ bźin źes bya ba daṅ mtshan ñid ces bya ba ni don gcig go.
de la med pa’i don ni mi rtag pa’i don te, kun brtags kyi mtshan ñid ri boṅ gi rva bźin dus thams cad du med pas kun brtags raṅ bźin med pa gaṅ yin pa, de ni mi rtag pa’o źes bya’o. raṅ bźin gyis sdug bsṅal ba’o źes bya ba la yaṅ dag pa ma yin par kun rtog pa’i don ni raṅ bźin gyis sdug bsṅal ba’i don to. de’aṅ gźan gyi dbaṅ gi mtshan ñid do. de bas na gźan gyi dbaṅ gis ji ltar ji ltar gzuṅ ba daṅ ’dzin par kun rtog par byed pa, de tsam du sdug bsṅal ba’i raṅ bźin du ’gyur te, sdug bsṅal rnam pa sna tshogs ’byuṅ ba’i rgyur ’gyur ro. raṅ bźin gyis stoṅ pa, raṅ bźin gyis bdag med pa’o źes bya ba la, yoṅs su rtog pa tsam ñid yod pa’i don ni bdag med pa’i don te, des na sems tsam yod kyi dṅos po gźan med par ston to. des bas na yoṅs su rtog gźan gyi dbaṅ tsam ni yod kyaṅ, chos su brtags pa’i dṅos po ni med pas na raṅ bźin gyis stoṅ pa źes bya’o. gaṅ zag tu brtags pa’i dṅos po med pas na raṅ bźin gyis bdag med pa’o źes bya’o. raṅ bźin gyis źi ba ste źes bya ba la gaṅ zag daṅ chos su rnam par rtog pa ñe bar źi ba’i don tam, de dag spaṅs pa’i don ni raṅ bźin gyis źi ba źes bya ste, de yaṅ dṅos su na yoṅs su grub pa’i mtshan ñid don dam pa’i chos kyi dbyiṅs rnam par dag pa’o. de la phyin ci log tu snaṅ ba’i sems ni gñen pos źi bar byas pa med kyi, raṅ bźin gyis skye ba med pa daṅ, ’byuṅ ba med par gnas pa’i phyir ro. de ltar mi rtag pa’i raṅ bźin gaṅ yin pa nas źi ba’i bar gyi raṅ bźin gaṅ yin pa, ’jig rten gyi raṅ bźin yaṅ de yin te, de dag gi raṅ bźin tha dad pa med par śes na byaṅ chub sems dpa’i phuṅ po la mkhas pa źes bya’o – "The meaning of impermanent is the meaning of non-existent (asadartho ’nityārthaḥ): the imagined character (parikalpitalakṣaṇa) is entirely (sarvatra) non-existent (asad) like a hare’s horn (śaśaviṣāṇa) and thus imagined (parikalpita), and without own being (niḥsvabhāva), this is [the meaning of] ‘impermanent’ (tad anityam iti). The sūtra says ’essentially suffering’: the meaning of imagining the inexistent is the meaning of ‘essentially suffering’ (svabhāvena duḥkha ity abhūtaparikalpārthaḥ svabhāvena duḥkhārthaḥ), and that is the dependent character (paratantralakṣaṇam). Thus, to the extent the dependent imagines object and subject, to that extent it appears as having the essence of suffering (tasmāt paratantro yathā yathā grāhyaṃ grāhakaṃ parikalpayati tāvad duḥkhasvabhāvo bhavati), that is, it becomes the cause of various [kinds of] suffering (nānāduḥkhahetur bhavati). The sūtra says ’essentially empty, essentially selfless’: the meaning of ’nothing but imagination’ is the meaning of ’selfless’, thus it teaches ’nothing but thought’, no other being (svabhāvena śūnyaḥ svabhāvenānātmeti parikalpamātrasyaiva bhāvārtho ’nātmārthas, tena cittamātraṃ nānyabhāvaṃ deśayati). Thus, though imagination, as dependent, exists, a thing constructed as a moment of existence do not exist: hence the sūtra says ’essentially empty’; a thing constructed as a person does not exist: hence the sūtra says ’essentially selfless’ (tasmāt parikalpaḥ paratantro ’sti, dharme kalpito bhāvas tu nāsti, svabhāvena śūnya iti, pudgale kalpito bhāvo nāsti, svabhāvenānātmeti). The sūtra says ’essentially in peace’, meaning appeasement of thought-constructions concerning persons and moments of existence, or, ’essentially in peace’ means giving them up (svabhāvena śānta iti pudgaladharmavikalpopaśamārtho vā teṣāṃ prahāṇārtho vā svabhāvena śānta iti); and further, it really means the absolute characteristic, the highest meaning, the pure sphere of all moments of existence (tat punar vastutaḥ pariniṣpannalakṣaṇaṃ paramārtho viśuddhadharmadhātuḥ). There thought appearing as false is not appeased by an antidote, as it is essentially unoriginated, staying unborn (tatra na viparītāvabhāsaṃ cittaṃ pratipakṣeṇa śamitam, svabhāvenānutpādam ajātam avasthitam); and thus the essence of impermanence and so on, up to the essence of peace, is also the essence of the world (evaṃ yo ’nityasvabhāvo yāvac chāntasvabhāvaḥ so ’pi lokasvabhavaḥ).
